Method of Istilam (Touching the Black Stone)
Definition and method of istilam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the correct method of istilam according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the various acceptable positions within the school.

Core Idea
Istilam is sunnah mu'akkadah; the primary method is placing both palms and kissing without sound.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on the method of istilam, the act of touching the Black Stone during tawaf. While it is a confirmed sunnah, there are subtle differences among Hanafi authorities regarding hand placement and whether to wipe the face. Understanding these nuances helps the pilgrim perform the act with confidence and avoid confusion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act being defined
Recognize that istilam is a sunnah act of touching the Black Stone during tawaf. The passage defines it as placing hands and kissing.
2
Extract the primary method
From the text: place both palms on the stone and kiss it without sound. This is the sunnah as per al-Nahr.
Kissing should be without sound.
3
Note the alternative methods
Some sources mention wiping the face after touching (al-Khaniyah), and differences about raising vs. lowering hands (al-Tuhfa).
These are all acceptable within the school.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is to raise hands to shoulder level before touching (al-Bada'i').
This is the preferred method.
5
Understand the hukm level
Istilam is sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting it does not invalidate tawaf.
No compensation required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( والاستلام أن يضع يديه الخ) قال في النهر : وعند الفقهاء هو أن يضع كفيه عليه ويقبله بفيه بلا صوت. وفي الخانية : ذكر مسح الوجه باليد مكان التقبيل لكن بعد أن يرفع يديه كما في الصلاة. كذا في المجتبى ومناسك الكرماني زاد في التحفة ويرسلهما ثم يستلم . وفي البدائع : وغيرها الصحيح أن يرفعهما حذاء منكبيه
His statement: (And istilam is that he places his hands...) He said in al-Nahr: According to the jurists, it is that he places his two palms upon it (the Black Stone) and kisses it with his mouth without sound. And in al-Khaniyah: It mentions wiping the face with the hand instead of kissing, but after raising his hands as in prayer. Likewise in al-Mujtaba and Manasik al-Kirmani, and in al-Tuhfa it adds: he lets them down then does istilam. And in al-Bada'i' and others: the correct view is that he raises them to the level of his shoulders.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage defines the act of istilam (touching the Black Stone) and describes the various methods reported in the Hanafi school. The primary method is for the pilgrim to place both palms on the stone and kiss it without making a sound. This is the sunnah. If one cannot reach the stone, he may touch it and then kiss his hands. Some sources mention wiping the face with the hands after touching the stone, which is similar to the movement in prayer. The passage also notes a difference: some scholars say to raise the hands to the shoulders when touching, while others say to let them down after raising. The relied-upon view is that the hands are raised to the shoulders, which is the method described in al-Bada'i'. The overarching point is that istilam is a confirmed sunnah act, and the methods described are all permissible with the preferred method being the one most closely following the Prophet's example.

Key Terms
الاستلام (al-istilam): Touching the Black Stone as an act of veneration during tawaf
التقبيل (al-taqbil): Kissing the Black Stone (or one's hand after touching it)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary method of istilam in the Hanafi school?
A) Pointing a finger from a distance
B) Placing both palms on the Stone and kissing it without sound
C) Wiping the face with hands after waving
D) Raising hands to the ears and shouting takbir

Key Takeaway
Istilam is a sunnah mu'akkadah performed by placing both palms on the Black Stone and kissing without sound; the mufta bihi method is to raise hands to shoulder level before touching.

Sajdah upon the Black Stone: Inter-Madhhab Dispute and Hanafi Tarjih
Inter-madhhab dispute on ruling of prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on prostration upon the Black Stone, cite the proofs, and evaluate the tarjih within the school.

Core Idea
Prostration upon the Black Stone is recommended in the Hanafi school, based on authentic prophetic action, despite earlier reservations due to lack of transmission in the mashahir.

The question of whether to prostrate upon the Black Stone during Hajj has generated discussion both among Hanafis and across schools. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq, the author first quotes a caution that it is better not to prostrate, then reviews the evidence and corrects that view, ultimately affirming the recommendation based on the action of the Prophet (ﷺ) and Umar (r). We will trace the dispute and the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view in the Hanafi school: prostration upon the Black Stone is recommended (sunnah/mandub).
Earlier Hanafis preferred not to do it due to lack of transmission in the famous works (mashahir).
2
Identify the opponents and their views
List opposing views: Malik considers it an innovation; some Hanafis (e.g., al-Qawwam al-Kaki initially) said it is better not to prostrate.
The Shafi'i position agrees with the Hanafi recommendation.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
The opponents rely on lack of mention in the authoritative Hanafi works and the view that it is an innovation if not proven.
Malik's proof is that it was not a common practice in Medina.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The author cites authentic hadith narrated by Ibn Abbas of the Prophet and Umar prostrating. He argues that authentic hadith overrides silence in the mashahir, and that al-Kaki's own statement is weak after the evidence.
The author uses the principle that a Hanafi scholar (al-Kaki) is more authoritative on Hanafi rulings than a Shafi'i (Ibn Abd al-Salam).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafis and Shafi'is may prostrate; Malikis should not; Hanafis following the earlier caution would also avoid it. The mufta bihi is to prostrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن أمكنه أن يسجد على الحجر الخ) قال في النهر : وهل يندب السجود عليه؟ نقل ابن عبد السلام الشافعي عن أصحابنا ذلك وعن ابن عباس أنه كان يقبله ويسجد عليه وقال : رأيت عمر فعل ذلك، ثم رأيت رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم يفعله ففعلته. رواه ابن المنذر والحاكم وفي المعراج وعن الشافعي أنه يقبله ويسجد عليه وعليه جمهور أهل العلم. وقال مالك : السجود عليه بدعة وعندنا الأولى أن لا يسجد لعدم الرواية في المشاهير. وجزم في البحر بضعف ما في المعراج وفيه نظر إذ صاحب الدار أدرى أي أن الكاكي صاحب المعراج أدرى بالحكم عندنا من ابن عبد السلام الشافعي ولذا نقله في الفتح وأقره . فعل لفعله عليه السلام والفاروق بعده ، وقول القوام الكاكى الأولى أن لا يسجد عندنا ضعيف.
His statement: (And if he can prostrate upon the Stone...) He said in al-Nahr: And is it recommended to prostrate upon it? Ibn Abd al-Salam al-Shafi'i narrated from our companions (Hanafis) that it is, and from Ibn Abbas that he would kiss it and prostrate upon it, and he said: I saw Umar do that, then I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) do it, so I did it. Narrated by Ibn al-Mundhir and al-Hakim. And in al-Mi'raj: and from al-Shafi'i that he kisses it and prostrates upon it, and the majority of scholars are upon this. And Malik said: prostration upon it is an innovation (bid'ah). And with us, the better is not to prostrate due to lack of transmission in the famous (mashahir). And he asserted in al-Bahr that what is in al-Mi'raj is weak, but there is consideration because the owner of the house is more knowledgeable, meaning that al-Kaki, the author of al-Mi'raj, is more knowledgeable of the ruling according to us than Ibn Abd al-Salam al-Shafi'i, and therefore he transmitted it in al-Fath and approved it. He did it (prostration) because of his (the Prophet's) action and that of Umar after him, and the statement of al-Qawwam al-Kaki that 'the better is not to prostrate with us' is weak.
Source pages p. 572

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on prostrating (sajdah) upon the Black Stone during the rituals of Hajj/Umrah. It presents a dispute both within the Hanafi school and with other schools. The majority of scholars (including Imam al-Shafi'i and the Hanafis as reported by Ibn Abd al-Salam) consider it recommended (mandub), citing actions of the Prophet (ﷺ), Umar, and Ibn Abbas. Imam Malik considers it an innovation (bid'ah). The early Hanafi position as stated in the famous works (al-mashahir) is that it is better not to do it because there is no clear transmission. However, the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq first says that the view in al-Mi'raj (by al-Kaki) is weak, but then he retorts that al-Kaki, being a Hanafi scholar, is more knowledgeable about the Hanafi school than Ibn Abd al-Salam al-Shafi'i. He concludes that the action of the Prophet and Umar, as well as al-Kaki's support, indicates that prostration is recommended. Thus the mufta bihi view is that it is sunnah to prostrate, as explicitly stated: the statement that it is better not to prostrate is weak. This shows a refinement within the Hanafi school: the earlier caution is overridden by the authentic hadith.

Key Terms
السجود (al-sujud): Prostration upon the Black Stone as an act of worship
المشاهير (al-mashahir): The famous and widely transmitted works of the Hanafi school (the Zahir al-Riwayah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the final position in this passage, what is the ruling on prostrating upon the Black Stone?
A) It is an innovation (bid'ah)
B) It is better not to do it
C) It is recommended based on the Prophet's action
D) It is prohibited

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately recommends prostration upon the Black Stone due to the authentic Sunnah, overriding earlier caution from lack of transmission in mashahir.

Kissing the Black Stone and Precedence of Tawaf over Salah
Ruling with proof on stone kissing and salah precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi method of kissing the Black Stone and explain when tawaf takes precedence over salah, including the exceptions.

Core Idea
Kiss the Stone without sound; tawaf is the greeting of the House, but prayer comes first if a fard prayer's time is limited.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq clarifies two important rulings for the pilgrim entering the Masjid al-Haram: the sunnah method of kissing the Black Stone and the priority between tawaf and salah. Understanding these ensures one fulfills the sunnah correctly without neglecting obligatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the kissing ruling
Note that the sunnah kissing is done by placing the lips without sound, as mentioned by al-Halabi. This is based on the Prophet's practice.
The act is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Understand the general rule of precedence
The author states that one should not begin with prayer because the greeting of the House is tawaf. This is a general rule: upon entering, tawaf takes priority over tahiyyat al-masjid.
Tawaf is considered a greeting (tahiyyah) for the Kaaba.
3
List the exceptions to the general rule
Identify the cases where salah takes precedence: (a) when people are prevented from tawaf, (b) missed obligatory prayer (fai'ta), (c) fear of time for fard, witr, or sunnah ratibah, (d) fear of missing congregation for fard.
These exceptions protect obligatory acts from being missed.
4
Apply to scenarios
Practice with examples: If one enters and the time for Asr is about to expire, he should pray first. If the time is ample, he should perform tawaf.
The key is whether the fard prayer can be performed in its time after tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا التقبيل المسنون إنما يكون بوضع الشفتين من غير تصويت كما ذكره الحلبي في مناسكه، وقد أشار إلى أنه لا يبدأ بالصلاة لأن تحية البيت الطواف فإن كان حلالاً فيطوف طواف التحية، وإن كان محرماً بالحج فطواف القدوم وهو أيضاً تحية إلا أنه خص بهذه الإضافة . وإن دخل في يوم النحر بعد الوقوف فطواف الفرض يغني كصلاة الفرض تغني عن تحية المسجد أو بالعمرة فطواف العمرة ولا يسن في حقه طواف القدوم واستثنى علماؤنا ما إذا دخل في وقت منع الناس من الطواف أو كان عليه فائتة مكتوبة أو خاف خروج الوقت للمكتوبة أو الوتر أو سنة راتبة أو فوت الجماعة في المكتوبة فإنه يقدم الصلاة على الطواف في هذه المسائل ثم يطوف . وفي قوله الحجر دون أن يصفه بالسواد إشارة إلى أنه حين أخرج من الجنة كان أبيض من اللبن وإنما أسود بمس المشركين والعصاة. كذا في المحيط .

قوله : (وطف مضطبعاً وراء الحطيم آخذاً عن يمينك مما يلي الباب سبعة أشواط) لفعله عليه السلام كذلك لما رواه أبو داود وهو أن يدخل ثوبه تحت يده اليمنى ويلقيه على عاتقه الأيسر. يقال اضطبع بثوبه وتأبط به، وقولهم اضطبع رداءه سهو وإنما الصواب بردائه. كذا في المغرب. وهو سنة مأخوذ من الضبع وهو العضد لأنه يبقى مكشوفاً، وينبغي أن يفعله قبل الشروع في الطواف بقليل. وأما إدخال الحطيم في طوافه فهو واجب لأن الحطيم ثبت أقول : حيث صح الحديث يتبع وإن لم يذكر ذلك في المشاهير لأن ذلك من فضائل الأعمال تثبت بالحديث الضعيف فبالصحيح أولى، وليست المسألة اجتهادية حتى يتوقف فيها على نص من المجتهد ما لم يثتب عنه خلافها فيتبع ما ثبت عنه ولذا - والله أعلم - مشى في اللباب على الاستحباب أن ويستحب يسجد عليه ويكرره مع التقبيل ثلاثاً ا الشيخ رشيد الدين في شرح الكنز ، وكذا نقل السجود عن أصحابنا العز بن جماعة لكن نقل الكاكي الخ قول المصنف : (وطف مضطبعاً) قال العلامة رحمه الله السندي تلميذ ابن الهمام في مناسكه المختصرة والمنلا علي القاري في شرحها ويضطبع أي في جميع الأشواط إن أراد أن يسعى بعده أي يقدم السعي عقبه وإلا لا، أي وإن لم يرد أن يسعى بعد هذا الطواف وأراد أن يؤخر السعي إلى ما بعد الطواف الفرض فلا يرمل ولا يضطبع حينئذ هنا، بل يؤخرهما إلى طواف الزيارة فيرمل فيه، وكذا يضطبع إن لم يكن لابساً ا هـ . وقال المنلا علي في شرح اللباب وهو شرح المنسك المتوسط : من لبس المخيط لعذر هل يسن في حقه التشبه به؟ لم يتعرض له أصحابنا، وذكر بعض الشافعية أن الاضطباع إنما يسن لمن لم يلبس المخيط، وأما من لبسه من الرجال فيتعذر في حقه الإتيان بالسنة أي على وجه الكمال فلا ينافي ما ذكره بعضهم من أنه قد يقال يشرع له جعل وسط ردائه تحت منكبه الأيمن وطرفه الأيسر وإن كان المنكب مستوراً بالمخيط للعذر. قال في عمدة المناسك : وهذا لا يبعد
And this sunnah kissing is only by placing the lips without sound as al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik. And he indicated that one should not begin with prayer because the greeting of the House is tawaf. So if one is non-muhrim, he performs tawaf tahiyyah; if muhrim for Hajj, it is tawaf al-qudum, which is also a greeting but specified by this addition. If he enters on the Day of Nahr after standing, then the obligatory tawaf suffices just as obligatory prayer suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. Or for Umrah, it is tawaf al-umrah, and tawaf al-qudum is not sunnah for him. Our scholars made exceptions: if he enters at a time when people are prevented from tawaf, or he has a missed obligatory prayer, or fears the time for an obligatory prayer, witr, or a regular sunnah, or fears missing the congregation for obligatory prayer, then he gives prayer precedence over tawaf in these cases, then performs tawaf. And in his statement 'the Stone' without describing it as black, there is indication that when it was brought out from Paradise it was whiter than milk, and only became black due to the touch of polytheists and sinners. Thus in al-Muhit. 

His statement: (And perform tawaf with idtiba' behind the Hatim, starting to the right of you towards the door, seven circuits) due to his action (peace be upon him) thus, as narrated by Abu Dawud: he places his garment under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. It is said 'idtiba'a' with his garment and 'ta'abbata' with it. Their saying 'idtiba'a his cloth' is a mistake; rather the correct form is 'with his cloth'. Thus in al-Mughrib. It is a sunnah derived from 'dhab' (the upper arm) because it remains uncovered. He should do it shortly before commencing tawaf. As for including the Hatim in his tawaf, it is obligatory (wajib) because the Hatim is established from the Kaaba. I say: when the hadith is authentic, it is followed even if not mentioned in the famous works because these are acts of virtue established by a weak hadith, so by a sound one it is more appropriate. And the issue is not ijtihadi that requires a text from a mujtahid as long as nothing contrary is established from him, so what is established from him is followed. Therefore - and Allah knows best - the author of al-Lubab followed the recommendation (istihbab) of prostrating upon it and repeating it with kissing three times, as Shaykh Rashid al-Din said in Sharh al-Kanz. Similarly, prostration is narrated from our companions by al-Izz ibn Jama'ah, but al-Kaki narrated something else. The statement of the author: (And perform tawaf with idtiba') said the scholar al-Sindi, the student of Ibn al-Humam in his Mukhtasar Manasik, and Mulla Ali al-Qari in its commentary: he performs idtiba' in all circuits if he intends to do sa'y after it, i.e., he proceeds with sa'y immediately after; otherwise not. That is, if he does not intend to perform sa'y after this tawaf and intends to delay sa'y to after the obligatory tawaf, then he does not do raml or idtiba' here, but rather delays them to tawaf al-ziyarah where he does raml and idtiba' if he is not wearing stitched garments. And Mulla Ali said in Sharh al-Lubab, which is a commentary on al-Munsik al-Mutawassit: For one who wears stitched garments due to an excuse, is it sunnah for him to imitate (idtiba')? Our companions did not address it. Some Shafi'is mentioned that idtiba' is only sunnah for one who is not wearing stitched garments. As for one who wears them among men, it is impossible for him to perform the sunnah perfectly, but it does not contradict what some said that it may be said it is legislated for him to place the middle of his garment under his right shoulder and its left end, even if his shoulder is covered by the stitched garment due to the excuse. He said in Umdat al-Manasik: This is not remote.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion of several important rulings related to tawaf. First, it reiterates that the sunnah kissing of the Black Stone is done by placing the lips without sound. Then it addresses the priority between tawaf and salah: the general rule is that tawaf is the greeting of the Kaaba, so one should begin with tawaf rather than two rak'ahs of prayer, similar to tahiyyat al-masjid. However, the Hanafi scholars make several exceptions: if the time for an obligatory prayer is narrow (e.g., a missed prayer, fear of time running out, fear of missing congregation), then salah takes precedence. The passage also notes that if one enters the Masjid al-Haram on the Day of Nahr, the obligatory tawaf (ifaradah) suffices, just as fard salah suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. 

Next, the passage discusses the ruling on idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) and raml (brisk walking) in tawaf. The sunnah is to perform idtiba' and raml in the first three circuits of tawaf if one intends to proceed directly to sa'y after tawaf. If one does not intend to do sa'y after this tawaf (e.g., he will do sa'y later after tawaf al-ziyarah), then he does not do idtiba' or raml in this tawaf. The idtiba' is performed by placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing the end over the left shoulder. It is a sunnah derived from the Prophet's action. 

Then the passage discusses the obligation of including the Hatim in the tawaf: it is wajib to include the Hatim within the circuit because it is part of the original Kaaba. Even if this is not mentioned in the famous Hanafi works, the authentic hadith is followed. The author also digresses to mention the recommendation of prostrating upon the Black Stone and repeating kissing three times, referencing various authorities. 

Finally, the passage addresses a contemporary issue: if a person wears stitched garments due to a valid excuse (e.g., illness, lack of ihram cloth), is idtiba' still recommended? The Hanafi scholars did not explicitly address this, but some Shafi'is hold that idtiba' is only for those not wearing stitched garments. The author suggests that such a person may still symbolically imitate idtiba' by placing the edge of his garment under his right shoulder even if the shoulder is covered by stitched clothing. This is considered not far-fetched.

Key Terms
التقبيل (al-taqbil): Kissing the Black Stone, a sunnah act.
تحية البيت (tahiyyat al-bayt): Greeting of the House (Kaaba), which is tawaf according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when entering the Masjid al-Haram, which act is given priority unless an exception applies?
A) Two rak'ahs of tahiyyat al-masjid
B) Tawaf (the greeting of the Kaaba)
C) Kissing the Black Stone
D) Sa'y between Safa and Marwah

Key Takeaway
The sunnah is to kiss the Black Stone without sound, and tawaf is the greeting of the Kaaba, but obligatory prayers take precedence when their time is limited.

Idtiba, Raml, Including the Hatim, and Idtiba for Excused Persons
Rulings with proofs on idtiba, raml, Hatim, and concession for excused persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the conditions for performing idtiba and raml, the obligation of including the Hatim in tawaf, and the ruling on idtiba for one wearing stitched garments due to an excuse.

Core Idea
Idtiba and raml are sunnah only when sa'y follows; Hatim must be included in tawaf; idtiba for an excused person may be performed symbolically.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq details several important rulings related to tawaf: the sunnah acts of idtiba (uncovering the right shoulder) and raml (brisk walking), the obligation to include the Hatim within the tawaf circuit, and the situation of one who must wear stitched garments due to an excuse. Understanding these ensures the pilgrim fulfills the sunnah correctly and does not fall into sin by omitting a wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition and sunnah of idtiba
Read the passage to understand how idtiba is performed: placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing it over the left shoulder. It is a sunnah based on the Prophet's action.
The term is derived from 'dhab' (upper arm).
2
Determine the condition for idtiba and raml
The passage states that idtiba and raml are only performed in the first three circuits of tawaf if one intends to do sa'y immediately after. If sa'y is delayed, they are postponed to the tawaf al-ziyarah.
This is a conditional sunnah.
3
Understand the obligation of including the Hatim
The author emphasizes that including the Hatim in the tawaf is wajib (obligatory) because it is part of the original Kaaba. Even if not mentioned in famous works, the authentic hadith is followed.
The hadith is considered strong enough to make it a binding act.
4
Analyze the ruling for idtiba when wearing stitched garments
The passage discusses whether one who wears stitched garments due to an excuse (e.g., illness) should still attempt idtiba. The Hanafi scholars did not address it, but some Shafi'is say idtiba is for those not wearing stitched clothes. The author suggests a symbolic action: placing the edge of the garment under the right shoulder.
This is a case of fiqh taysir (facilitation).

Source Text

وهذا التقبيل المسنون إنما يكون بوضع الشفتين من غير تصويت كما ذكره الحلبي في مناسكه، وقد أشار إلى أنه لا يبدأ بالصلاة لأن تحية البيت الطواف فإن كان حلالاً فيطوف طواف التحية، وإن كان محرماً بالحج فطواف القدوم وهو أيضاً تحية إلا أنه خص بهذه الإضافة . وإن دخل في يوم النحر بعد الوقوف فطواف الفرض يغني كصلاة الفرض تغني عن تحية المسجد أو بالعمرة فطواف العمرة ولا يسن في حقه طواف القدوم واستثنى علماؤنا ما إذا دخل في وقت منع الناس من الطواف أو كان عليه فائتة مكتوبة أو خاف خروج الوقت للمكتوبة أو الوتر أو سنة راتبة أو فوت الجماعة في المكتوبة فإنه يقدم الصلاة على الطواف في هذه المسائل ثم يطوف . وفي قوله الحجر دون أن يصفه بالسواد إشارة إلى أنه حين أخرج من الجنة كان أبيض من اللبن وإنما أسود بمس المشركين والعصاة. كذا في المحيط .

قوله : (وطف مضطبعاً وراء الحطيم آخذاً عن يمينك مما يلي الباب سبعة أشواط) لفعله عليه السلام كذلك لما رواه أبو داود وهو أن يدخل ثوبه تحت يده اليمنى ويلقيه على عاتقه الأيسر. يقال اضطبع بثوبه وتأبط به، وقولهم اضطبع رداءه سهو وإنما الصواب بردائه. كذا في المغرب. وهو سنة مأخوذ من الضبع وهو العضد لأنه يبقى مكشوفاً، وينبغي أن يفعله قبل الشروع في الطواف بقليل. وأما إدخال الحطيم في طوافه فهو واجب لأن الحطيم ثبت أقول : حيث صح الحديث يتبع وإن لم يذكر ذلك في المشاهير لأن ذلك من فضائل الأعمال تثبت بالحديث الضعيف فبالصحيح أولى، وليست المسألة اجتهادية حتى يتوقف فيها على نص من المجتهد ما لم يثتب عنه خلافها فيتبع ما ثبت عنه ولذا - والله أعلم - مشى في اللباب على الاستحباب أن ويستحب يسجد عليه ويكرره مع التقبيل ثلاثاً ا الشيخ رشيد الدين في شرح الكنز ، وكذا نقل السجود عن أصحابنا العز بن جماعة لكن نقل الكاكي الخ قول المصنف : (وطف مضطبعاً) قال العلامة رحمه الله السندي تلميذ ابن الهمام في مناسكه المختصرة والمنلا علي القاري في شرحها ويضطبع أي في جميع الأشواط إن أراد أن يسعى بعده أي يقدم السعي عقبه وإلا لا، أي وإن لم يرد أن يسعى بعد هذا الطواف وأراد أن يؤخر السعي إلى ما بعد الطواف الفرض فلا يرمل ولا يضطبع حينئذ هنا، بل يؤخرهما إلى طواف الزيارة فيرمل فيه، وكذا يضطبع إن لم يكن لابساً ا هـ . وقال المنلا علي في شرح اللباب وهو شرح المنسك المتوسط : من لبس المخيط لعذر هل يسن في حقه التشبه به؟ لم يتعرض له أصحابنا، وذكر بعض الشافعية أن الاضطباع إنما يسن لمن لم يلبس المخيط، وأما من لبسه من الرجال فيتعذر في حقه الإتيان بالسنة أي على وجه الكمال فلا ينافي ما ذكره بعضهم من أنه قد يقال يشرع له جعل وسط ردائه تحت منكبه الأيمن وطرفه الأيسر وإن كان المنكب مستوراً بالمخيط للعذر. قال في عمدة المناسك : وهذا لا يبعد
And this sunnah kissing is only by placing the lips without sound as al-Halabi mentioned in his Manasik. And he indicated that one should not begin with prayer because the greeting of the House is tawaf. So if one is non-muhrim, he performs tawaf tahiyyah; if muhrim for Hajj, it is tawaf al-qudum, which is also a greeting but specified by this addition. If he enters on the Day of Nahr after standing, then the obligatory tawaf suffices just as obligatory prayer suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. Or for Umrah, it is tawaf al-umrah, and tawaf al-qudum is not sunnah for him. Our scholars made exceptions: if he enters at a time when people are prevented from tawaf, or he has a missed obligatory prayer, or fears the time for an obligatory prayer, witr, or a regular sunnah, or fears missing the congregation for obligatory prayer, then he gives prayer precedence over tawaf in these cases, then performs tawaf. And in his statement 'the Stone' without describing it as black, there is indication that when it was brought out from Paradise it was whiter than milk, and only became black due to the touch of polytheists and sinners. Thus in al-Muhit. 

His statement: (And perform tawaf with idtiba' behind the Hatim, starting to the right of you towards the door, seven circuits) due to his action (peace be upon him) thus, as narrated by Abu Dawud: he places his garment under his right armpit and throws it over his left shoulder. It is said 'idtiba'a' with his garment and 'ta'abbata' with it. Their saying 'idtiba'a his cloth' is a mistake; rather the correct form is 'with his cloth'. Thus in al-Mughrib. It is a sunnah derived from 'dhab' (the upper arm) because it remains uncovered. He should do it shortly before commencing tawaf. As for including the Hatim in his tawaf, it is obligatory (wajib) because the Hatim is established from the Kaaba. I say: when the hadith is authentic, it is followed even if not mentioned in the famous works because these are acts of virtue established by a weak hadith, so by a sound one it is more appropriate. And the issue is not ijtihadi that requires a text from a mujtahid as long as nothing contrary is established from him, so what is established from him is followed. Therefore - and Allah knows best - the author of al-Lubab followed the recommendation (istihbab) of prostrating upon it and repeating it with kissing three times, as Shaykh Rashid al-Din said in Sharh al-Kanz. Similarly, prostration is narrated from our companions by al-Izz ibn Jama'ah, but al-Kaki narrated something else. The statement of the author: (And perform tawaf with idtiba') said the scholar al-Sindi, the student of Ibn al-Humam in his Mukhtasar Manasik, and Mulla Ali al-Qari in its commentary: he performs idtiba' in all circuits if he intends to do sa'y after it, i.e., he proceeds with sa'y immediately after; otherwise not. That is, if he does not intend to perform sa'y after this tawaf and intends to delay sa'y to after the obligatory tawaf, then he does not do raml or idtiba' here, but rather delays them to tawaf al-ziyarah where he does raml and idtiba' if he is not wearing stitched garments. And Mulla Ali said in Sharh al-Lubab, which is a commentary on al-Munsik al-Mutawassit: For one who wears stitched garments due to an excuse, is it sunnah for him to imitate (idtiba')? Our companions did not address it. Some Shafi'is mentioned that idtiba' is only sunnah for one who is not wearing stitched garments. As for one who wears them among men, it is impossible for him to perform the sunnah perfectly, but it does not contradict what some said that it may be said it is legislated for him to place the middle of his garment under his right shoulder and its left end, even if his shoulder is covered by the stitched garment due to the excuse. He said in Umdat al-Manasik: This is not remote.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive discussion of several important rulings related to tawaf. First, it reiterates that the sunnah kissing of the Black Stone is done by placing the lips without sound. Then it addresses the priority between tawaf and salah: the general rule is that tawaf is the greeting of the Kaaba, so one should begin with tawaf rather than two rak'ahs of prayer, similar to tahiyyat al-masjid. However, the Hanafi scholars make several exceptions: if the time for an obligatory prayer is narrow (e.g., a missed prayer, fear of time running out, fear of missing congregation), then salah takes precedence. The passage also notes that if one enters the Masjid al-Haram on the Day of Nahr, the obligatory tawaf (ifaradah) suffices, just as fard salah suffices for tahiyyat al-masjid. 

Next, the passage discusses the ruling on idtiba' (uncovering the right shoulder) and raml (brisk walking) in tawaf. The sunnah is to perform idtiba' and raml in the first three circuits of tawaf if one intends to proceed directly to sa'y after tawaf. If one does not intend to do sa'y after this tawaf (e.g., he will do sa'y later after tawaf al-ziyarah), then he does not do idtiba' or raml in this tawaf. The idtiba' is performed by placing the garment under the right armpit and throwing the end over the left shoulder. It is a sunnah derived from the Prophet's action. 

Then the passage discusses the obligation of including the Hatim in the tawaf: it is wajib to include the Hatim within the circuit because it is part of the original Kaaba. Even if this is not mentioned in the famous Hanafi works, the authentic hadith is followed. The author also digresses to mention the recommendation of prostrating upon the Black Stone and repeating kissing three times, referencing various authorities. 

Finally, the passage addresses a contemporary issue: if a person wears stitched garments due to a valid excuse (e.g., illness, lack of ihram cloth), is idtiba' still recommended? The Hanafi scholars did not explicitly address this, but some Shafi'is hold that idtiba' is only for those not wearing stitched garments. The author suggests that such a person may still symbolically imitate idtiba' by placing the edge of his garment under his right shoulder even if the shoulder is covered by stitched clothing. This is considered not far-fetched.

Key Terms
الاضطباع (al-idtiba'): Uncovering the right shoulder by placing the garment under the right armpit and over the left shoulder during tawaf.
الرمل (al-raml): Brisk walking with short steps and shoulder movements in the first three circuits of tawaf.
الحطيم (al-hatim): The semicircular wall (Hijr Isma'il) adjacent to the Kaaba; it must be included within the tawaf circuit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what is the ruling on including the Hatim (Hijr Isma'il) in tawaf?
A) It is sunnah muakkadah
B) It is wajib
C) It is mustahabb
D) It is makruh to include it

Key Takeaway
Idtiba and raml are sunnah only when sa'y follows immediately; the Hatim must be included in tawaf as a wajib; and one with an excuse may perform a symbolic idtiba.

Rulings of Tawaf: Idtiba', Including the Hatim, and Starting Point
Commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq detailing sunan and wajibat of tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between sunnah and wajib actions in tawaf, explain the dalil for including the Hatim, and state the mufta bihi on starting from the Black Stone.

Core Idea
The Hatim is wajib to include as part of the House; starting from the Black Stone is sunnah, not a condition.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq unpacks the concise matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, detailing which actions in tawaf are sunnah (idṭibā‘) and which are wājib (including the Ḥaṭīm). It also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether starting at the Black Stone is wājib or sunnah. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correctly performing tawāf and knowing what requires compensation (dam).

Guided Path
1
Identify each action and its ruling classification
From the matn and commentary, list the actions mentioned: idtiba', including the Hatim, starting from the Black Stone, and circumambulating in reverse. Note whether each is classified as sunnah or wajib by the author.
The ruling for idtiba' is explicitly sunnah; including Hatim is wajib; starting point has ikhtilaf.
2
Locate the dalil for each wajib action
Find the evidence cited for including Hatim (khabar al-wahid confirming it is part of the Ka'bah) and for starting from Black Stone (action of the Prophet, never omitted).
The dalil for Hatim is a single-narrator hadith, giving zanni thubut, hence wajib not fard.
3
Examine the ikhtilaf on starting from the Black Stone
The passage presents two views: Fath al-Qadir says it is wajib; al-Muhit says it is sunnah. Understand the reasoning behind each and note the preferred position.
The tarjih (preferred view) is that it is sunnah based on majority of mashayikh.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If someone starts elsewhere: according to the sunnah view, tawaf is valid but makruh; according to the wajib view, one sins but tawaf is still valid. If one omits the Hatim, a dam becomes due unless repeated.
The ruling on reverse circumambulation is also mentioned: valid but sinful, requiring repeat or dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الحج باب الإحرام
قوله : (وطف مضطبعاً وراء الحطيم آخذاً عن يمينك مما يلي الباب سبعة أشواط) لفعله عليه السلام كذلك لما رواه أبو داود وهو أن يدخل ثوبه تحت يده اليمنى ويلقيه على عاتقه الأيسر. يقال اضطبع بثوبه وتأبط به، وقولهم اضطبع رداءه سهو وإنما الصواب بردائه. كذا في المغرب. وهو سنة مأخوذ من الضبع وهو العضد لأنه يبقى مكشوفاً، وينبغي أن يفعله قبل الشروع في الطواف بقليل. وأما إدخال الحطيم في طوافه فهو واجب لأن الحطيم ثبت كونه من البيت بخير الواحد حتى لو تركه يؤمر بإعادة الطواف من الأصل أو إعادته على الحطيم ما دام بمكة ولو لم يعد لزمه دم ولو استقبل الحطيم وحده لا تجوز صلاته لأن فرضية التوجه ثبتت بنص الكتاب فلا تتأدى بما ثبت بخير الواحد احتياطاً. وله ثلاث أسام: حطيم وحظيرة وحجر. وهو اسم لموضع متصل بالبيت من الجانب الغربي بينه وبين البيت، لأنه حطم من البيت أي كسر فعيل بمعنى مفعول كالقتيل بمعنى المقتول، أو لأن ظلمه فيه حطمه الله كما جاء في الحديث فهو بمعنى فاعل. كذا في كشف الأسرار. وليس كله من البيت بل مقدار ستة أذرع من البيت برواية مسلم عن عائشة. وفي غاية البيان أن فيه قبر هاجر وإسماعيل عليهما السلام وأما أخذه عن يمينه مما يلي الباب فهو واجب أيضاً حتى لو طاف منكوساً صح وأثم لتركه الواجب، ويجب إعادته ما دام بمكة فإن رجع قبل إعادته فعليه دم والحكمة في كونه يجعل البيت عن يساره أن الطائف بالبيت مؤتم به والواحد مع الإمام يكون الإمام على يساره وقيل لأن القلب في الجانب الأيسر، وقيل ليكون الباب في أول طوافه لقوله تعالى واتوا البيوت من أبوابها وأشار يقوله «مما يلي الباب» أن الافتتاح من الحجر الأسود واجب لأنه عليه السلام لم يتركه قط، وقيل شرط حتى لو افتتح من غيره لا يجزئه لأن الأمر بالطواف في الآية مجمل في حق الابتداء فالتحق فعله عليه السلام بياناً له كذا في فتح القدير هنا. وفي باب الجنايات ذكر أن ظاهر الروايات أنه سنة، وذكر في المحيط أنه سنة عند عامة المشايخ لو افتتح من غير الحجر صح مع الكراهة.
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. His statement: (And circumambulate with idtiba', behind the Hatim, taking to your right from the side of the door, seven circuits) due to his ﷺ action thus as narrated by Abu Dawood: that he puts his garment under his right arm and throws it over his left shoulder. It is said iḍṭaba‘a lithawbihi and ta’abbata bihi; their saying iḍṭaba‘a ridā’ahu is a mistake; the correct is biredā’ihi. Thus in al-Mughrib. It is a sunnah derived from al-ḍab‘ which is the upper arm because it remains uncovered. He should do it shortly before starting tawaf. As for including the Hatim in his tawaf, it is obligatory because the Hatim is established as being from the House by khabar al-wāḥid; so much so that if he leaves it, he is ordered to repeat the tawaf from the beginning or repeat it over the Hatim as long as he is in Makkah; and if he does not repeat, a dam becomes incumbent upon him. And if one faces the Hatim alone, his prayer is not valid because the obligation of facing the qibla is established by the text of the Book, so it is not fulfilled by what is established by khabar al-wāḥid as a precaution. It has three names: Hatim, Hazira, and Hijr. It is the name for a place connected to the House on the western side between it and the House, because it was broken from the House, i.e., broken; the pattern fa‘īl in the sense of maf‘ūl like qatīl meaning maqtūl; or because one who oppresses therein, Allah will break him as came in the hadith, so it is in the sense of fā‘il. Thus in Kashf al-Asrār. Not all of it is from the House; rather six cubits from the House according to Muslim’s narration from ‘A’isha. In Ghāyat al-Bayān it contains the grave of Hājar and Ismā‘īl عليهما السلام. As for his taking to his right from the side of the door, it is also obligatory; so much so that if he circumambulates in reverse, it is valid but he sins for leaving the obligatory, and he must repeat it as long as he is in Makkah; if he returns before repeating, a dam is due. The wisdom in placing the House on his left is that the circumambulator follows the House, and the single person with the imam has the imam on his left. It is also said because the heart is on the left side; and it is said so that the door is at the beginning of his tawaf, due to His statement: 'And enter houses from their doors'. And his saying 'from the side of the door' indicates that starting from the Black Stone is obligatory because he ﷺ never abandoned it; and it is said it is a condition, such that if he starts from other than it, it does not suffice, because the command for tawaf in the verse is ambiguous regarding the beginning, so his ﷺ action becomes an explanation. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr here. And in the chapter of offenses it is mentioned that the apparent of the narrations is that it is sunnah, and in al-Muḥīṭ it is mentioned that it is sunnah according to general mashāyikh: if one starts from other than the Black Stone, it is valid with dislike.
Source pages p. 573

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Rā’iq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqā’iq, expanding the ruling on how to perform tawaf. The matn states seven sunan/wajibat: circumambulate with iḍṭibā‘ (uncovering the right shoulder), behind the Ḥaṭīm (the semicircular wall), starting to the right from the side of the door (i.e., from the Black Stone), for seven circuits. The commentator explains each: iḍṭibā‘ is sunnah, derived from the Prophet’s action. Including the Ḥaṭīm within the tawaf is wājib because it is established as part of the Ka‘bah through khabar al-wāḥid (a single-narrator hadith). If omitted, one must repeat the tawaf while in Makkah; if unable, a dam (sacrifice) is due. The Ḥaṭīm is partially from the House (six cubits). The obligation to start from the Black Stone is also wājib; starting from elsewhere is valid but sinful. There is a difference of opinion: some consider it sunnah rather than wājib. The commentator cites different sources: Fath al-Qadīr says wājib; al-Muhīt says sunnah, and the preferred view is that it is sunnah, with dislike if neglected. The passage also notes the wisdom behind each ruling.

Key Terms
اضطباع (iḍṭibā‘): Placing one's garment under the right arm and throwing it over the left shoulder, leaving the right arm exposed.
حطيم (Ḥaṭīm): The semicircular wall adjoining the Ka'bah on the western side, partly from the original House.
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with short steps while moving the shoulders; done in the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on starting tawaf from other than the Black Stone?
A) Tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Tawaf is valid but makruh; it is sunnah to start from the Black Stone.
C) Tawaf is valid and there is no dislike.
D) It is a condition; tawaf is invalid without it.

Key Takeaway
The Hatim must be included in tawaf because it is part of the Ka'bah (wajib), while starting from the Black Stone is sunnah, not a condition, according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Ruling on Tawaf Behind al-Hatim
Ruling on tawaf and definition of al-Hatim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tawaf regarding al-Hatim and explain why it is wajib based on khabar al-wahid.

Core Idea
Al-Hatim is considered part of the Ka'bah by khabar al-wahid; omitting it in tawaf requires repetition or dam.

When performing tawaf around the Ka'bah, you must include the curved area known as al-Hatim (or al-Hijr). This ruling is based on a solitary hadith (khabar al-wahid) that indicates part of al-Hatim is from the original structure. Omitting it does not invalidate tawaf but makes it deficient, requiring either repetition while still in Makkah or a sacrificial animal (dam). This lesson explains the evidence and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tawaf (circumambulation) around the Ka'bah. The specific issue is whether the area of al-Hatim must be included in the circuits. The ruling is that it is wajib to include it; omission is a deficiency.
Wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a khabar al-wahid, specifically the hadith narrated by Muslim from Aisha that six cubits of al-Hatim are from the House.
Hanafis accept khabar al-wahid in furu'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith indicates that part of al-Hatim is part of the Ka'bah. Therefore, tawaf must encompass that area as part of the House. The inference is that the entire al-Hatim area is to be considered part of the circuit.
The hadith specifies 'six cubits'; some scholars infer the whole area.
4
Note the consequence of omission
If one omits al-Hatim, he is ordered to repeat the tawaf from the beginning as long as he is in Makkah. If he leaves without repeating, a dam (sacrificial animal) is obligatory.
The tawaf remains valid (sahih) but incomplete; compensation is required.
5
Distinguish from prayer facing al-Hatim
The text contrasts tawaf with prayer: facing al-Hatim alone in prayer is invalid because the obligation to face the Ka'bah is from the Quran (qat'i), while the inclusion of al-Hatim is from a zanni source. The ruling for prayer is stricter.
This shows hierarchy of evidences: qat'i over zanni.

كونه من البيت بخير الواحد حتى لو تركه يؤمر بإعادة الطواف من الأصل أو إعادته على الحطيم ما دام بمكة ولو لم يعد لزمه دم ولو استقبل الحطيم وحده لا تجوز صلاته لأن فرضية التوجه ثبتت بنص الكتاب فلا تتأدى بما ثبت بخير الواحد احتياطاً. وله ثلاث أسام: حطيم وحظيرة وحجر. وهو اسم لموضع متصل بالبيت من الجانب الغربي بينه وبين البيت ، لأنه حطم من البيت أي كسر فعيل بمعنى مفعول كالقتيل بمعنى المقتول، ظلمه فيه حطمه الله كما جاء في الحديث فهو بمعنى فاعل. كذا في كشف الأسرار . وليس كله من البيت بل مقدار ستة أذرع من البيت برواية مسلم عن عائشة. وفي غاية البيان أن فيه قبر هاجر وإسماعيل عليهما السلام
That (al-Hatim) is part of the House by the evidence of a single narration; so if one abandons it, he is ordered to repeat the tawaf from the beginning or repeat it over al-Hatim as long as he is in Makkah; and if he does not repeat, a dam is incumbent on him. And if one prays facing al-Hatim alone, his prayer is not valid because the obligation of facing the Qibla is established by the text of the Book, so it cannot be fulfilled by what is established by a single narration, as a precaution. And it has three names: Hatim, Hazira, and Hijr. It is a name for a place attached to the House on the western side between it and the House, because it was broken off from the House, i.e., broken, on the pattern of fa'il in the sense of maf'ul, like qatil in the sense of maqtul. (It is also said) 'the oppressor, Allah will break him in it' as came in the hadith, so it is in the sense of fa'il. Thus in Kashf al-Asrar. Not all of it is from the House, but only six cubits from the House according to the narration of Muslim from Aisha. And in Ghayat al-Bayan, it contains the graves of Hajar and Isma'il, peace be upon them.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses two main points: first, the ruling on tawaf (circumambulation) around the Ka'bah with respect to the area known as al-Hatim (also called al-Hijr or al-Hazira). The author states that al-Hatim is considered part of the Ka'bah based on a single narration (khabar al-wahid). Therefore, if a pilgrim omits this area during tawaf, he must repeat the tawaf from the beginning if he is still in Makkah, or else he owes a dam (sacrificial animal). The evidence is that facing the Ka'bah in prayer is a confirmed obligation from the Quran, so it cannot be fulfilled by something established by a single narration. The second point defines al-Hatim: it is the area adjacent to the western side of the Ka'bah, named because it was broken off from the original building. The author mentions three names: Hatim, Hazira, and Hijr. The passage also clarifies that only six cubits of al-Hatim are from the Ka'bah (based on Muslim's narration from Aisha), and according to Ghayat al-Bayan, it contains the graves of Hajar and Isma'il. This passage is typical of the Hanafi method: basing a ruling on a single narration while preserving the primacy of Quranic texts.

Key Terms
حطيم (hatim): The area attached to the Ka'bah on the west, considered part of it for tawaf.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith narrated by one or few narrators, not reaching tawatur.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (e.g., a sheep) required as compensation for omitting a wajib act in Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a pilgrim performs tawaf leaving out the area of al-Hatim?
A) The tawaf is valid with no penalty.
B) He must repeat the tawaf as long as he is in Makkah or pay a dam.
C) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated from the beginning.
D) He only needs to offer a sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
Al-Hatim is considered part of the Ka'bah by khabar al-wahid; omitting it in tawaf requires repetition while in Makkah or a dam otherwise.

Starting Tawaf from the Black Stone: Hanafi Classification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on starting tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on starting tawaf from the Black Stone (fard, wajib, sunnah) and explain why the preferred view is wajib.

Core Idea
Starting from the Black Stone is wajib due to the Prophet's constant practice, but not fard to avoid adding a condition to the Quran.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the legal status of beginning tawaf specifically from the Black Stone? While the Quran commands tawaf generally, the Prophet's practice clarifies the starting point. The author weighs evidence from constant practice (muwazaba) and the verse 'Enter houses from their doors' to determine the correct hukm among fard, wajib, and sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute is about the legal ruling of beginning tawaf from the Black Stone—is it a condition (fard/shart), an obligation (wajib), or a recommended act (sunnah)?
The Quranic command to circumambulate is general; the Prophet's action specifies the starting point.
2
State the three positions
List the views: (1) Muhammad in al-Ruqayat and al-Asl considers it a condition (fard) — tawaf invalid without it. (2) The general body of Hanafi scholars and al-Muhit consider it sunnah. (3) The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers the position of wujub (obligation).
The author's 'al-awjah al-wujub' (the more appropriate view is obligation) is the key refinement.
3
Analyze the evidence
Examine the evidence for each view: For wujub, the Prophet never omitted starting from the Stone (muwazaba) and the verse 'Enter houses from their doors' analogically indicates starting from the door of the Ka'bah. The counterargument that this would be adding to the Quran by a solitary report is rebutted because the Prophet's action is explanatory, not additive.
The author notes that a solitary report (khabar al-wahid) when attached to a general text becomes part of the general text's clarification.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: If one starts elsewhere, according to the fard view, tawaf is invalid and must be repeated. According to the wajib view, tawaf is valid but a dam is due. According to the sunnah view, it is valid but disliked (makruh tanzihi).
The author's preference for wujib balances evidence and avoids the extremes of invalidating or completely excusing.

القدوم سنة وبشروعه فيه يجب إكماله
As for taking it on his right from the direction of the door, that is also obligatory, so that if he performs tawaf in reverse (starting from the left), it is valid but he sins for leaving the wajib. He must repeat it as long as he is in Makkah; if he returns without repeating, a dam is due. The wisdom of making the House on his left is that the circumambulator is following it, and the one following the imam has the imam on his left. It is also said because the heart is on the left side, and it is said so that the door is at the beginning of his tawaf, due to the verse 'Enter houses from their doors' (2:189). He indicated by his saying 'from the direction of the door' that the opening from the Black Stone is obligatory because the Prophet never abandoned it. It is said it is a condition, such that if he opens from elsewhere, it does not suffice, because the command to circumambulate in the verse is general with respect to the beginning, so the Prophet's action (peace be upon him) serves as its clarification, as in Fath al-Qadir here. And in the chapter on injuries, it is mentioned that the apparent of the narrations is that it is sunnah, and it is mentioned in al-Muhit that it is sunnah according to the general body of scholars. If he opens from other than the Black Stone, it is permissible but disliked. Muhammad mentioned in al-Ruqayat that that amount is not permissible and he must repeat, and he (Abu Hanifa?) indicated that in al-Asl, making the beginning from it a fard. End. And the more appropriate view is obligation due to constant practice, and making it fard is far from the principles because it would require adding to the definitive (Quran) by a solitary report. Perhaps the author of al-Muhit meant by 'sunnah' the confirmed sunnah which is in the sense of wajib, and the dislike is tahrimi (prohibitive). And since beginning from the Stone is wajib, beginning the tawaf from the side where the Yemeni corner is close to the Black Stone is determined so that he passes with his entire body over all of the Black Stone. Many common people are seen beginning tawaf while part of the Stone is outside their tawaf — so beware. And his saying 'seven circuits' is a clarification of the obligatory, not the fard, in tawaf, for we have stated that the minimum of seven circuits is wajib, compensated by dam, so the rukn is the majority of the circuits. There is disagreement. And it is contrary to the condition or wajib, so it is not counted. Hence he said: thus he does seven times and fulfills his right in it of ramal etc., i.e., of moving to the right and so on. And if he repeats, the penalty falls. And if he performs tawaf on the wall of the Stone, it is said it is permissible and should be restricted to what is beyond its boundary, which is six or seven cubits. End from al-Lubab and its commentary. He said: 'and the more appropriate view is obligation' and he clarified in al-Minhaj quoting al-Wajiz. The commentator of al-Lubab said regarding 'the necessity of adding to the definitive by a solitary report': I say here that if a solitary report becomes attached as an explanation of a general text, then what is established by it is established by the general text, not by the solitary report, as stated by al-Allama al-Akmal in his commentary on al-Hidaya when discussing the obligatory acts of wudu. So the best answer is to deny the generality (of the command), because the command to circumambulate does not necessitate the obligation of starting from a specific place; rather, it is absolute, indicating sufficiency from any place, and the Prophet's action indicated obligation or sunnah — so understand. This is what appeared to me as an answer. Then I consulted Fath al-Qadir and found it stated: and if it is said it is wajib, it is not far-fetched because constant practice without omission is its evidence, so one sins and it suffices; and if the verse of tawaf contained generality, it would be a condition as Muhammad said, but that is negated with respect to the beginning, so the absolute circumambulation is the fard, and beginning from the Stone is wajib by constant practice. End verbatim. His saying: 'and since beginning from the Stone is wajib' is based on what the author deemed appropriate. This and what is in al-Lubab: 'then he stands' i.e., after wearing the ihram cloth facing the House next to the Black Stone from the direction of the Yemeni corner such that the entire Stone is on his right and his right shoulder is at the edge of the Stone, and he intends tawaf — and this manner is recommended. End. This is based on the view that opening from the Stone is sunnah, which is the statement of the general body of scholars, and the author of al-Lubab relied on it and said it is correct. But what the author claimed of the necessity of passing with his entire body over the Black Stone is not necessary, because if he stands opposite the Stone, the beginning from it is achieved because when one stands with his body opposite the Stone, part of the Yemeni corner enters, as the Stone and its corner do not reach the width of the body of the one opposite it, as in al-Shurnabulaliyyah. What he claimed as necessary is stated in al-Lubab as recommended, and similarly in al-Fath where he said: it is recommended to begin tawaf from the side of the Stone that is on the Yemeni corner, so that he passes with his entire body over all the Stone, and he avoids the disagreement of those who require passage in that manner. End. His saying: 'so the rukn is the majority of the circuits' — apparently this is specific to tawaf al-ziyarah because it is a rukn; as for tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-sadr, they are not, but tawaf al-qudum is sunnah and once started, it must be completed.
Source pages p. 574

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses two major obligations in tawaf: firstly, that the Ka'bah must be on the left side while circumambulating, and that the tawaf must begin from the Black Stone. The primary evidence is the constant practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him), who never omitted starting from the Black Stone, and the verse 'Enter houses from their doors.' The author presents different opinions: some consider it a condition (shart) such that if one starts elsewhere, the tawaf is invalid (Muhammad in al-Ruqayat and al-Asl); others consider it sunnah (the general body of scholars and al-Muhit); the author himself leans toward obligation (wajib) due to evidence of constant practice. He rebuts the argument that making it wajib would be adding to the definitive Quran by a solitary report, by noting that the Prophet's action explains the general command. The second part discusses the number of circuits: the seven circuits are wajib (obligatory) but not fard (integral); the fard is the majority of circuits? Actually, the text says 'الركن أكثر الأشواط' meaning the rukn (pillar) is the majority of the circuits, but then notes that this is specific to tawaf al-ziyarah (the main tawaf of Hajj). For tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf) it is sunnah. The passage also discusses the proper positioning of the body relative to the Black Stone to ensure all of it is encompassed, and concludes that standing opposite the Stone suffices, not necessarily passing with the whole body.

Key Terms
واجب (wajib): An obligation proven by speculative evidence; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
المواظبة (muwazaba): The Prophet's continuous practice without omission, used as evidence for wujub in Hanafi usul.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary hadith; here used as evidence for the practice of starting from the Black Stone.
شرط (shart): Condition; omission renders the act invalid (batil).
ركن (rukn): Pillar; essential part of an act. In tawaf, the majority of circuits is the rukn, not the starting point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred opinion in this passage, what is the ruling if a pilgrim begins tawaf from a point before the Black Stone?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated entirely.
B) The tawaf is valid but the pilgrim must offer a dam (sacrifice) if he does not repeat it while in Makkah.
C) The tawaf is valid and no compensation is needed.
D) The tawaf is valid but the pilgrim is sinful and must repeat all seven circuits.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi position is that starting tawaf from the Black Stone is wajib, not fard or sunnah, based on the Prophet's constant practice (muwazaba) and the explanation of the verse 'Enter houses from their doors'.

Beginning Tawaf from the Black Stone: Wajib, Not Fard nor Sunnah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on beginning tawaf from the Black Stone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on beginning tawaf from the Black Stone, explain why it is wajib rather than fard or sunnah, and apply the thamarah al-khilaf in a practical scenario.

Core Idea
Beginning tawaf from the Black Stone is wajib—obligatory but not fard—due to the Prophet's continuous practice.

This lesson dives into an intra-Hanafi dispute: what is the legal status of starting tawaf precisely from the Black Stone? Some early Hanafi authorities considered it fard, others mere sunnah. The later preferred view, argued by the author of Bahr al-Ra'iq and supported by Fath al-Qadir, is that it is wajib. Understanding this distinction is crucial for practicing Hanafis: omitting a wajib requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate tawaf, whereas a fard omission would require repetition. Let's trace the evidence and reasoning behind the wajib position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Disputed Ruling
The act is beginning the tawaf circuit from the Black Stone. The dispute is whether this is fard (integral), wajib (obligatory but compensable), or sunnah (recommended).
2
Analyze the Evidence for Each View
Imam Muhammad in al-Ruqyat argued it is fard because the Prophet never started elsewhere. The general mashayikh said sunnah because the Quranic command is general. The author argues for wajib based on muwazaba (continuous practice) of the Prophet, which indicates obligation but not the level of fard since adding to a definitive text (Quran) with a solitary report is impermissible.
Focus on the usul principle: a khabar wahid cannot abrogate or add a new fard to the Quran.
3
Understand the Hanafi Distinction: Fard vs Wajib vs Sunnah
In Hanafi fiqh, fard is established by qat'i evidence (Quran/mutawatir) and omission invalidates the act. Wajib is established by zanni evidence (khabar wahid, qiyas) and omission requires compensation (dam) but the act remains valid. Sunnah is recommended without any sin or compensation. The author applies this hierarchy to resolve the dispute.
This is a classic Hanafi usul principle applied to a fiqh ruling.
4
Identify the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
If one begins tawaf before the Black Stone or skips it: under the fard view, the circuit is invalid and must be repeated; under the wajib view, the tawaf is valid but a dam (blood) must be given; under the sunnah view, no penalty. The author's wajib view means the tawaf is valid with dam.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Contemporary Scenario
A person starts tawaf a meter before the Black Stone due to crowd pressure. According to the mufta bihi (wajib view), his tawaf is valid, but he must offer a dam. If he had started after the Stone, he would need to compensate and possibly repeat the circuit if the omission was intentional? Actually, the wajib view says dam suffices; but the author stresses one must ensure the whole body passes over the Stone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجر جاز ويكره. وذكر محمد في الرقيات أنه لم يجز ذلك القدر وعليه الإعادة وإليه أشار في الأصل فقد جعل البداية منه فرضاً ا.هـ. والأوجه الوجوب للمواظبة والافتراض بعيد عن الأصول للزوم الزيادة على القطعي بخبر الواحد، ولعل صاحب المحيط أراد بالسنة السنة المؤكدة التي بمعنى الواجب وتكون الكراهة تحريمية. ولما كان الابتداء من الحجر واجباً كان الابتداء من الطواف من الجهة التي فيها الركن اليماني قريباً من الحجر الأسود متعيناً ليكون ماراً بجميع بدنه على جميع الحجر الأسود وكثير من العوام شاهدناهم يبتدؤون الطواف وبعض الحجر خارج عن طوافهم .فاحذره وقوله سبعة أشواط بيان للواجب لا للفرض في الطواف فإنا قدمنا أن أقل الأشواط السبعة واجبة تجبر بالدم فالركن أكثر الأشواط . واختلف
1
وهو خلاف الشرط أو الواجب فلا يكون محسوباً، ولهذا قال : هكذا يفعل سبع مرات ويقضي حقه فيه من رمل وغيره أي من تيامن ونحوه، وإذا أعاده سقط الجزاء. ولو طاف على جدار الحجر قيل يجوز وينبغي تقييده بما زاد على حده وهو قدر ستة أو سبعة أذرع . ا هـ من اللباب وشرحه قوله : (والأوجه الوجوب) وبه صرح في المنهاج نقلاً عن الوجيز حيث قال في عد الواجبات : والبداءة بالحجر الأسود وهو الأشبه والأعدل فينبغي أن يكون هو المعول (شرح اللباب قوله : (للزوم الزيادة الخ) أقول فيه إن خبر الواحد إذا التحق بياناً للنص المجمل فالثابت به يكون ثابتاً بالنص المجمل لا بخبر الواحد كما صرح به العلامة الأكمل في شرح الهداية عند الكلام على فرائض الوضوء، فالأحسن في الجواب منع الإجمال لأن الأمر بالطواف لا يلزم منه فرضية الابتداء من مكان مخصوص بل هو مطلق يدل على الإجزاء من أي مكان، وفعله عليه السلام أفاد الوجوب أو السنية فافهم. هذا ما ظهر لي في الجواب، ثم راجعت فتح القدير فرأيته قال ما نصه : ولو قيل إنه واجب لا يبعد لأن المواظبة من غير ترك دليله فيأثم به ويجزئ، ولو كان في آية الطواف إجمال لكان شرطاً كما قال محمد ، لكنه منتف في حق الابتداء فيكون مطلق التطوف هو الفرض وافتتاحه من الحجر واجب للمواظبة ا هـ . بحروفه قوله : (ولما كان الابتداء من الحجر واجباً الخ) أي بناء على ما استوجهه المؤلف. هذا وما في اللباب من قوله ثم يقف» أي بعد الاضطباع مستقبل البيت بجانب الحجر الأسود مما يلي الركن اليماني بحيث يصير جميع الحجر عن يمينه ويكون منكبه الأيمن عند طرف الحجر فينوي الطواف وهذه الكيفية مستحبة .اهـ. فهو مبني على أن الافتتاح من الحجر سنة وهو قول عامة المشايخ ومشى عليه صاحب اللباب وقال : إنه الصحيح لكن ما ادعاه المؤلف من لزوم المرور بجميع بدنه على الحجر غير لازم فإنه لو وقف مسامتاً للحجر حصل الابتداء منه لأن من قام مسامتاً بجسده الحجر يدخل فيه شيء من جانب الركن اليماني لأن الحجر وركنه لا يبلغ عرض جسد المسامت له كما في الشرنبلالية، وما ادعى لزومه صرح في اللباب باستحبابه ، وكذا في الفتح حيث قال : وينبغي أن يبدأ بالطواف من جانب الحجر الذي على الركن اليماني ليكون ماراً على جميع الحجر . بجميع بدنه فيحرج من خلاف من يشترط المرور كذلك عليه ا هـ .
The Stone is permissible and disliked. Muhammad mentioned in al-Ruqyat that that amount is not valid and he must repeat, and he pointed to that in al-Asl, so he made the beginning from it fard. End quote. The most apparent is obligation due to continuous practice, and considering it fard is far from the principles because it would necessitate increasing upon the definitive with a solitary report. Perhaps the author of al-Muhit meant by sunnah the confirmed sunnah that is in the sense of wajib, and the dislike would be prohibitively disliked. Since the beginning from the Stone is wajib, the beginning of the tawaf must be from the side that has the Yemeni corner near the Black Stone, determined so that he passes with all his body over all the Black Stone. Many common people, we see them beginning tawaf while part of the Stone is outside their tawaf, so beware. And his saying 'seven circuits' is an explanation of the wajib, not the fard, in tawaf, for we have stated that the minimum of seven circuits is wajib, compensated with blood, so the rukn is more than the circuits. And there is disagreement... 1 ... which is contrary to the condition or the wajib, so it is not counted. For this he said: he does this seven times and fulfills its right in it of raml and other things, i.e., of tayammun and the like, and if he repeats it, the penalty falls. And if he makes tawaf on the wall of the Stone, it is said that it is permissible and should be restricted to what exceeds its limit, which is about six or seven cubits. End quote from al-Lubab and its commentary. His statement: (and the most apparent is obligation) and it is stated in al-Minhaj quoting from al-Wajiz where he said in counting the wajibat: and the beginning with the Black Stone is the most similar and just, so it should be relied upon. (Commentary of al-Lubab: his statement: (due to the necessity of increase etc.) I say in it: if a solitary report becomes a clarification of an ambiguous text, what is established by it is established by the ambiguous text, not by the solitary report, as stated by al-Allama al-Akmal in Sharh al-Hidayah when discussing the faraid of wudu. So the best answer is to deny the ambiguity because the command for tawaf does not necessitate the fardiyya of beginning from a specific place; rather it is absolute, indicating validity from any place, and his action (peace be upon him) indicated obligation or sunna, so understand. This is what appeared to me as an answer, then I consulted Fath al-Qadir and saw that he said verbatim: and if it is said it is wajib, it is not far because continuous practice without abandonment is its evidence, so he sins by it and it suffices, and if there was ambiguity in the verse of tawaf, it would be a condition as Muhammad said, but it is negated with respect to the beginning, so absolute tawaf is fard and its opening from the Stone is wajib due to continuous practice. End quote verbatim. His statement: (and since the beginning from the Stone is wajib etc.) i.e., based on what the author considered apparent. This and what is in al-Lubab from his saying 'then he stands' i.e., after idtiba', facing the House beside the Black Stone from the side of the Yemeni corner, such that all the Stone is to his right and his right shoulder is at the edge of the Stone, then he intends tawaf, and this manner is recommended. End quote. It is based on that the opening from the Stone is sunnah, which is the saying of the general mashayikh, and the author of al-Lubab adopted it and said it is correct. But what the author claimed of the necessity of passing with his entire body over the Stone is not necessary, because if he stands aligned with the Stone, the beginning occurs from it, because one who stands aligned with his body to the Stone, something of the side of the Yemeni corner enters into it because the Stone and its corner do not reach the width of the body aligned with it, as in al-Sharnablaliyya. And what he claimed as necessary is stated in al-Lubab as recommended, and similarly in al-Fath where he said: one should begin tawaf from the side of the Stone that is on the Yemeni corner so that he passes over all the Stone with all his body, thus exiting from the disagreement of those who stipulate passing over it in that manner. End quote.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussion from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses two related issues: the ruling on beginning tawaf from the Black Stone, and the status of the seven circuits. The author first states that if one begins tawaf from elsewhere than the Black Stone, it is permissible but disliked. He then cites Imam Muhammad in al-Ruqyat saying that if one begins at a different point, the circuit does not count and must be repeated—implying the beginning is fard. However, the author deems the most apparent opinion to be that it is wajib (obligatory due to continuous practice, muwazaba) and not fard, because declaring it fard would increase the Quranic command (which is general) with a solitary report (khabar wahid). He suggests that the term 'sunnah' in al-Muhit may mean the confirmed sunnah equivalent to wajib, making the dislike tahrimi. Since the beginning is wajib, one must start tawaf near the Yemeni corner so that the entire body passes over the Black Stone. The author warns against common people beginning tawaf while part of the Stone is left out. Then he turns to 'seven circuits' as an explanation of the wajib, not the fard, in tawaf—the minimum seven circuits are wajib (compensable with blood) while the rukn (integral) is more than seven (i.e., the majority of circuits?). The text includes a footnote marker '1' and a quote from al-Lubab that tawaf on the wall of the Stone is permissible if the wall is over six or seven cubits above the ground. The commentary then refutes the idea of necessity of passing the whole body over the Stone, citing al-Sharnablaliyya that alignment suffices. The discussion ends with a quote from Fath al-Qadir supporting the wajib view. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position that beginning from the Stone is wajib (not fard), and that the minimum seven circuits are also wajib (not fard), with the rukn being more than seven—a subtle but important distinction.

Key Terms
الحجر الأسود (al-hajar al-aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba, from which tawaf begins according to the Sunnah.
المواظبة (al-muwazaba): The continuous practice of the Prophet without interruption; used as evidence for wujub.
الواجب (al-wajib): An act that is obligatory but not at the level of fard; omission requires compensation (dam) but does not invalidate the act.
الكفر (al-khabar al-wahid): A solitary report, i.e., a hadith that does not reach the level of tawatur. In Hanafi usul, it provides zanni evidence and cannot add a new fard to the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Quran explicitly commands it as fard
B) Because the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazaba) indicates obligation, but declaring it fard would add to the Quran with a solitary report
C) Because all scholars agreed it is wajib
D) Because it is a condition of tawaf according to Imam Muhammad

Key Takeaway
Beginning tawaf from the Black Stone is wajib in the Hanafi school—obligatory but not fard—and omission requires a dam (blood sacrifice) while the tawaf remains valid.
