The Rukn in Tawaf and the Ruling on an Eighth Circuit
Determining the rukn of tawaf and the ruling on an extra circuit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of circuits that constitute the rukn in Tawaf al-Ziyara, identify the dispute among Hanafi scholars, and apply the ruling on an eighth circuit based on intention.

Core Idea
The rukn of tawaf is four circuits according to the correct Hanafi view; seven circuits are wajib.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq delves into the intricate Hanafi discussion on the fundamental components (rukn) of Tawaf al-Ziyara. The text presents differing views within the school—from Imam Muhammad's four circuits to Ibn al-Humam's insistence on all seven—and also clarifies the ruling when an extra circuit is performed, distinguishing intentional from unintentional additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of tawaf and their rulings
The passage specifies that the statement 'the rukn is more than the circuits' applies to Tawaf al-Ziyara, which is a rukn of Hajj. Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah but becomes wajib upon starting. This step establishes the context for the dispute.
Tawaf al-Sadr is also mentioned, but its ruling is not detailed here.
2
State the dispute on the number of circuits that constitute the rukn
Imam Muhammad (in al-Mabsut) says the rukn is four circuits, Jurjani says three and two-thirds, and Ibn al-Humam insists all seven are rukn. The text indicates the correct view is four circuits ('وهو الصحيح').
The disagreement hinges on whether the majority of circuits suffices as the essential part.
3
Analyze the ruling on an eighth circuit
If a person intentionally performs an eighth circuit knowing it is extra, the correct view is that he must complete the entire seven-circuit tawaf (i.e., finish the week) because he started with commitment (sunnah obligation). If he mistakenly thought it was the seventh and then realizes it is the eighth, he is not required to complete the extra circuit because he started with the intention of dropping (non-committal).
This distinction is based on intention at the start: committed vs. non-committed.
4
Derive the principle: tawaf differs from Hajj
The author notes that tawaf differs from Hajj in this ruling. In Hajj, starting the act even without commitment obligates completion, but in tawaf, the rule is reversed for the unintentional extra circuit.
This exceptional ruling emphasizes the precision of Hanafi fiqh in distinguishing rituals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فالركن أكثر الأشواط الظاهر أن هذا خاص بطواف الزيارة لأنه ركن أما القدوم والصدر ،فلا لكن طواف القدوم سنة وبشروعه فيه يجب إكماله
فيه فقيل أربعة أشواط وهو الصحيح نص عليه محمد في المبسوط، وذكر الجرجاني أنه ثلاثة أشواط وثلثا شوط، وخالف المحقق ابن الهمام أهل المذهب وجزم بأن السبعة ركن فإنه لا يجزئ أقل منها وأن هذا ليس من قبيل ما يقام فيه الأكثر مقام الكل، وأطال الكلام فيه في الجنايات، وهذا التقدير أعني السبعة مانع للنقصان اتفاقاً واختلفوا في منعه للزيادة حتى لو وعلم أنه ثامن اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه يلزمه إتمام الأسبوع لأنه شرع فيه ملتزماً بخلاف ما إذا ظن أنه سابع ثم تبين له أنه ثامن فإنه لا يلزمه الإتمام لأنه شرع فيه مسقطاً لا ملتزماً كالعبادة المظنونة. كذا في المحيط .
طاف ثامناً
وبهذا علم أن الطواف خالف الحج فإنه إذا شرع فيه مسقطاً يلزمه إتمامه بخلاف بقية العبادات. والأشواط جمع شوط وهو جري مرة إلى الغاية كذا في المغرب. وفي الخانية من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط واعلم أن مكان الطواف داخل المسجد الحرام حتى لو طاف بالبيت من وراء زمزم أو من وراء السواري جاز، ومن خارج المسجد لا يجوز وعليه أن يعيد لأنه لا يمكنه الطواف ملاصقاً لحائط البيت فلا بد من حد فاصل بين القريب والبعيد فجعلنا الفاصل حائط المسجد لأنه في حكم بقعة واحدة فإذا طاف خارج المسجد فقد طاف بالمسجد لا بالبيت لأن حيطان المسجد تحول بينه وبين البيت كذا في المحيط.
His statement: (so the rukn is more than the circuits) apparently this is specific to Tawaf al-Ziyara because it is a rukn, but as for [Tawaf] al-Qudum and al-Sadr, then no, but Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah and upon starting it, completing it becomes obligatory. Regarding it, it is said four circuits, and that is the correct view, as stated by Muhammad in al-Mabsut. Jurjani mentioned that it is three and two-thirds of a circuit. And Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam opposed the madhhab scholars and determined that the seven are rukn, for it is not valid with less, and that this is not of the type where the majority stands in place of the whole. He elaborated on it in al-Jinayat. This estimation, meaning seven, prevents deficiency by agreement, and they disagreed about it preventing increase, such that if one knows he is on the eighth, they differed, and the correct view is that he must complete the week because he started it as committed, unlike if he thought he was on the seventh and then it became clear he is on the eighth, then he is not required to complete it because he started it as dropping, not committed, like the presumptive act of worship. Thus stated in al-Muhit. He made tawaf as an eighth. By this it is known that tawaf differs from Hajj, for if one starts it as dropping, he must complete it, unlike the rest of acts of worship. Al-ashwat is plural of shawt, which is a run to the limit, as in al-Mughrib. And in al-Khaniyya: from the Stone to the Stone is a shawt. Know that the place of tawaf is inside the Sacred Mosque, so if one makes tawaf around the House from behind Zamzam or from behind the pillars, it is permissible. From outside the Mosque it is not permissible and he must repeat, because he cannot make tawaf adjacent to the wall of the House, so there must be a separating limit between near and far. We have made the separating limit the wall of the Mosque because it is in the ruling of one place. So if he makes tawaf outside the Mosque, he has made tawaf around the Mosque, not the House, because the walls of the Mosque intervene between him and the House. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on Tawaf, focusing on the number of circuits (ashwat) and their legal status. It begins by commenting on the phrase 'so the rukn is more than the circuits', clarifying that this applies only to Tawaf al-Ziyara (the visit tawaf) which is a rukn of Hajj. For Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf) and Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf), the ruling differs: Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, but once started it becomes obligatory to complete. There is a dispute among Hanafis about how many circuits constitute a rukn: some say four circuits is the correct view (Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut), Jurjani says three and two-thirds, but Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam strongly held that all seven circuits are rukn, arguing this is not a case where the majority suffices for the whole. The passage then states that seven circuits is a 'man' (preventer) of deficiency by consensus, but scholars disagreed regarding increase—if one intentionally performs an eighth circuit knowing it is extra, the correct position is that he must complete the entire week (i.e., continue to make it odd? Actually he must complete the seventh? The text says he must complete the 'usbu' which means the seven, so if he knows he is on the eighth, he must complete seven more? This seems contradictory. However, the next sentence clarifies: if he knows he is on the eighth, he must complete the week (i.e., the seven) because he started with commitment. If he thought he was on the seventh and then realizes it is the eighth, he does not have to complete it because he started with the intention of dropping (i.e., he was not committed to more than seven). This is like a presumptive act of worship (al-ibada al-maznuna). The author then notes that tawaf differs from Hajj: in Hajj, if one starts with the intention of dropping (i.e., optional), he must complete it, but in tawaf the rule is reversed. The lexical definition: shawt is a run to the limit, and in al-Khaniyya from Stone to Stone is one circuit. The place of tawaf is inside the Sacred Mosque; tawaf from behind Zamzam or the pillars is valid, but from outside the mosque is not—the mosque wall acts as the boundary between near and far. This lesson establishes the intricate Hanafi position on when an extra circuit invalidates or necessitates completion, and the precise number of circuits that are fard vs. wajib.

Key Terms
الشوط (al-shawt): One complete circuit around the Kaaba, from the Black Stone back to the Black Stone.
الركن (al-rukn): The essential, integral part of an act; its omission invalidates the act.
الطواف ثامناً (al-tawaf thaminan): Performing an eighth circuit intentionally or unintentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Four circuits

D) Eight circuits

Key Takeaway
The rukn of tawaf is four circuits (the correct Hanafi view), while seven are wajib; an extra circuit counts only if done intentionally.

The Place of Tawaf and Its Distinction from Hajj
Determining the valid area for tawaf and the unique rule of tawaf regarding intentionality

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid boundaries for performing tawaf (inside the Sacred Mosque) and explain why tawaf differs from Hajj in the ruling on starting an act without intention of commitment.

Core Idea
Tawaf must be performed inside the Sacred Mosque; the mosque wall defines the boundary between valid and invalid tawaf.

After discussing the number and validity of circuits, the author clarifies the spatial requirements for tawaf. He also highlights a unique feature of tawaf: unlike Hajj, if one starts tawaf without the intention of commitment (i.e., thinking it's the seventh circuit), he is not obliged to complete it if it turns out to be the eighth. This exception sets tawaf apart from other acts of worship.

Guided Path
1
Understand the spatial requirement for tawaf
The passage states that the place of tawaf is inside the Sacred Mosque (al-Masjid al-Haram). Tawaf performed from behind Zamzam or behind the pillars inside the mosque is valid, but tawaf from outside the mosque is invalid and must be repeated.
The boundary is the wall of the mosque, not the immediate vicinity of the Kaaba.
2
Identify the rationale for the boundary
The reason is that it is impossible to perform tawaf directly adjacent to the wall of the Kaaba due to crowds; therefore, a limit must be set. The mosque wall serves as that limit, as the entire mosque is considered one precinct (fi hukm buq'a wahida). Tawaf outside the mosque is circumambulation of the mosque, not the House.
This ruling illustrates the Hanafi use of custom ('urf) and necessity in defining spatial boundaries.
3
Compare tawaf with Hajj regarding intention
The passage notes that if one starts an act of Hajj (e.g., Ihram or Tawaf al-Hajj) without commitment (thinking it's the seventh), he must complete it. In contrast, for tawaf, if one starts an extra circuit unintentionally, he is not required to complete it. This is because tawaf is considered a lesser ritual where intention at the start matters more.
This exception shows the nuanced approach of Hanafi fiqh to different rituals.
4
Review the lexical definition of shawt
The text defines 'shawt' as a run to the limit, and in al-Khaniyya as from the Black Stone to the Black Stone. This definition is important for precise counting.
Consistent definition ensures uniformity in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فالركن أكثر الأشواط الظاهر أن هذا خاص بطواف الزيارة لأنه ركن أما القدوم والصدر ،فلا لكن طواف القدوم سنة وبشروعه فيه يجب إكماله
فيه فقيل أربعة أشواط وهو الصحيح نص عليه محمد في المبسوط، وذكر الجرجاني أنه ثلاثة أشواط وثلثا شوط، وخالف المحقق ابن الهمام أهل المذهب وجزم بأن السبعة ركن فإنه لا يجزئ أقل منها وأن هذا ليس من قبيل ما يقام فيه الأكثر مقام الكل، وأطال الكلام فيه في الجنايات، وهذا التقدير أعني السبعة مانع للنقصان اتفاقاً واختلفوا في منعه للزيادة حتى لو وعلم أنه ثامن اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه يلزمه إتمام الأسبوع لأنه شرع فيه ملتزماً بخلاف ما إذا ظن أنه سابع ثم تبين له أنه ثامن فإنه لا يلزمه الإتمام لأنه شرع فيه مسقطاً لا ملتزماً كالعبادة المظنونة. كذا في المحيط .
طاف ثامناً
وبهذا علم أن الطواف خالف الحج فإنه إذا شرع فيه مسقطاً يلزمه إتمامه بخلاف بقية العبادات. والأشواط جمع شوط وهو جري مرة إلى الغاية كذا في المغرب. وفي الخانية من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط واعلم أن مكان الطواف داخل المسجد الحرام حتى لو طاف بالبيت من وراء زمزم أو من وراء السواري جاز، ومن خارج المسجد لا يجوز وعليه أن يعيد لأنه لا يمكنه الطواف ملاصقاً لحائط البيت فلا بد من حد فاصل بين القريب والبعيد فجعلنا الفاصل حائط المسجد لأنه في حكم بقعة واحدة فإذا طاف خارج المسجد فقد طاف بالمسجد لا بالبيت لأن حيطان المسجد تحول بينه وبين البيت كذا في المحيط.
His statement: (so the rukn is more than the circuits) apparently this is specific to Tawaf al-Ziyara because it is a rukn, but as for [Tawaf] al-Qudum and al-Sadr, then no, but Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah and upon starting it, completing it becomes obligatory. Regarding it, it is said four circuits, and that is the correct view, as stated by Muhammad in al-Mabsut. Jurjani mentioned that it is three and two-thirds of a circuit. And Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam opposed the madhhab scholars and determined that the seven are rukn, for it is not valid with less, and that this is not of the type where the majority stands in place of the whole. He elaborated on it in al-Jinayat. This estimation, meaning seven, prevents deficiency by agreement, and they disagreed about it preventing increase, such that if one knows he is on the eighth, they differed, and the correct view is that he must complete the week because he started it as committed, unlike if he thought he was on the seventh and then it became clear he is on the eighth, then he is not required to complete it because he started it as dropping, not committed, like the presumptive act of worship. Thus stated in al-Muhit. He made tawaf as an eighth. By this it is known that tawaf differs from Hajj, for if one starts it as dropping, he must complete it, unlike the rest of acts of worship. Al-ashwat is plural of shawt, which is a run to the limit, as in al-Mughrib. And in al-Khaniyya: from the Stone to the Stone is a shawt. Know that the place of tawaf is inside the Sacred Mosque, so if one makes tawaf around the House from behind Zamzam or from behind the pillars, it is permissible. From outside the Mosque it is not permissible and he must repeat, because he cannot make tawaf adjacent to the wall of the House, so there must be a separating limit between near and far. We have made the separating limit the wall of the Mosque because it is in the ruling of one place. So if he makes tawaf outside the Mosque, he has made tawaf around the Mosque, not the House, because the walls of the Mosque intervene between him and the House. Thus in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 575

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on Tawaf, focusing on the number of circuits (ashwat) and their legal status. It begins by commenting on the phrase 'so the rukn is more than the circuits', clarifying that this applies only to Tawaf al-Ziyara (the visit tawaf) which is a rukn of Hajj. For Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf) and Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf), the ruling differs: Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah, but once started it becomes obligatory to complete. There is a dispute among Hanafis about how many circuits constitute a rukn: some say four circuits is the correct view (Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut), Jurjani says three and two-thirds, but Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam strongly held that all seven circuits are rukn, arguing this is not a case where the majority suffices for the whole. The passage then states that seven circuits is a 'man' (preventer) of deficiency by consensus, but scholars disagreed regarding increase—if one intentionally performs an eighth circuit knowing it is extra, the correct position is that he must complete the entire week (i.e., continue to make it odd? Actually he must complete the seventh? The text says he must complete the 'usbu' which means the seven, so if he knows he is on the eighth, he must complete seven more? This seems contradictory. However, the next sentence clarifies: if he knows he is on the eighth, he must complete the week (i.e., the seven) because he started with commitment. If he thought he was on the seventh and then realizes it is the eighth, he does not have to complete it because he started with the intention of dropping (i.e., he was not committed to more than seven). This is like a presumptive act of worship (al-ibada al-maznuna). The author then notes that tawaf differs from Hajj: in Hajj, if one starts with the intention of dropping (i.e., optional), he must complete it, but in tawaf the rule is reversed. The lexical definition: shawt is a run to the limit, and in al-Khaniyya from Stone to Stone is one circuit. The place of tawaf is inside the Sacred Mosque; tawaf from behind Zamzam or the pillars is valid, but from outside the mosque is not—the mosque wall acts as the boundary between near and far. This lesson establishes the intricate Hanafi position on when an extra circuit invalidates or necessitates completion, and the precise number of circuits that are fard vs. wajib.

Key Terms
الشوط (al-shawt): One complete circuit around the Kaaba, from the Black Stone back to the Black Stone.
الطواف (al-tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba in a prescribed manner.
المسجد الحرام (al-Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque in Mecca, the boundary for valid tawaf.

The Seven Wajibat of Tawaf
Enumeration of the seven wajibat of tawaf with detailed rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven wajibat of tawaf according to the Hanafi school and explain the consequence of omitting each one.

Core Idea
The seven wajibat of tawaf are obligatory but do not invalidate tawaf; omission requires a sacrifice.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq quotes al-Lubab to enumerate the seven obligatory acts of tawaf. Understanding these wajibat is essential for performing tawaf correctly and knowing what compensation is due if any are missed. The text also discusses the different statuses of Tawaf al-Sadr and Tawaf al-Qudum, and an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether purity from physical filth is wajib or sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the list of seven wajibat
Commit the seven wajibat to memory: (1) purity from hadath, (2) purity from filth (disputed), (3) covering the ‘awrah, (4) walking for the able, (5) using the right side, (6) beginning from the Black Stone, (7) completing seven circuits.
The seventh wajib is not explicitly stated in the OCR text but is assumed from the count.
2
Understand the scope of each wajib
For each wajib, note the conditions: e.g., covering the ‘awrah requires covering at least a quarter of a limb; if less, it is excused. Walking is required for the able; if riding without excuse, repetition or dam is due.
The thresholds (e.g., quarter limb) are similar to those in prayer.
3
Distinguish antara wajib, fard, and sunnah
These are wajib (obligatory but not pillars). Omission requires compensation (dam or sadaqa) but does not invalidate the tawaf. Sunnah acts have no penalty.
This is a key Hanafi principle: wajib and fard are distinguished by the strength of evidence.
4
Learn the consequences of omission
For Tawaf al-Sadr: leaving most circuits requires dam; leaving a few requires a sadaqa per circuit. For Tawaf al-Qudum: no penalty except repentance, as it is sunnah in origin.
The text clarifies that Tawaf al-Qudum does not become wajib by starting.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on purity from filth
The majority consider purity from khabath (physical filth) to be sunnah; a minority hold it wajib for the amount covering the ‘awrah.
The relied-upon position is that it is sunnah.

Source Text

الحدث
فيساوي بعد الشروع طواف الصدر فيصير الطوافان واجبين فيكون جميع أشواطهما واجبة، ويؤيد ذلك ما سيذكره المؤلف قريباً في أشواط السعي حيث جعلها واجبة كلها، لكن صرحوا بأنه لو ترك أكثر أشواط الصدر لزمه دم، وفي الأقل لكل شوط صدقة. وأما القدروم فلم يصرحوا بما يلزمه لو تركه بعد الشروع، وبحث السندي في منسكه الكبير في أنه كالصدر ونازعه في شرح اللباب بأن الصدر واجب بأصله فلا يقاس عليه ما يجب بشروعه، فالظاهر أنه لا يلزمه بتركه شيء سوى التوبة كصلاة النفل ا هـ ملخصاً. وهذا ما ظهر لي قبل أن أراه وسيأتي أنه لا يتحقق الترك إلا بالخروج من مكة قوله : (وقد علمت الخ) قال في اللباب واجبات الطواف سبعة: الأول الطهارة عن الأكبر والأصغر الثاني قيل الطهارة عن النجاسة الحقيقية والأكثر على أنه سنة، وقيل قدر ما يستر عورته من الثواب واجب أي طهارته فلو طاف وعليه قدر ما يواري العورة طاهر والباقي نجس جاز وإلا فهو بمنزلة .العريان الثالث ستر العورة فلو طاف مكشوفها وجب الدم، والمانع كشف ربع العضو فما زاد كما في الصلاة وإن انكشف أقل من الربع لا يمنع ويجمع المتفرق. الرابع المشي فيه للقادر فلو طاف راكباً أو محمولاً أو زحفاً بلا عذر فعليه الإعادة أو الدم، وإن كان بعذر لا شيء عليه، ولو نذر أن يطوف زحفاً لزمه ماشياً. الخامس التيامن السادس قبل الابتداء من الحجر
You have already learned from what we have presented of the obligations of Hajj that purity from the two hadaths (major and minor) in it is wajib, and similarly covering the private parts. So if one makes tawaf while his private parts are uncovered to the extent that prayer is permissible with it, a dam becomes necessary for him. Thus stated in al-Zahiriya. As for purity from filth (khabath), it is from ... from the hadath. So it equals after starting the Tawaf al-Sadr, so both tawafs become wajib, thus all their circuits are wajib. That is supported by what the author will soon mention regarding the circuits of sa'i, where he made all of them wajib. But they stated that if one leaves most of the circuits of al-Sadr, a dam is necessary, and for the least, for each circuit a sadaqa. As for al-Qadum, they did not state what is necessary if one leaves it after starting. Al-Sindhi researched in his Manasik al-Kabir that it is like al-Sadr, and the commentator on al-Lubab disagreed that al-Sadr is wajib in itself, so what becomes wajib by starting cannot be analogized to it. The apparent is that nothing is necessary for leaving it except repentance, like a supererogatory prayer. End quote summarized. This is what appeared to me before I saw it, and it will come that leaving is only actualized by leaving Mecca. His statement: (You have already learned etc.) He said in al-Lubab: The wajibat of tawaf are seven: First: purity from the major and minor hadath. Second: it is said purity from real filth, but the majority consider it sunnah, and it is said that the amount that covers one's private parts from the cloth is wajib, i.e., its purity. So if one makes tawaf while having on him enough to cover his private parts that is pure and the rest is impure, it is permissible; otherwise it is like a naked person. Third: covering the private parts. So if one makes tawaf with them uncovered, a dam is necessary. The preventing factor is uncovering a quarter of the limb or more, as in prayer. If less than a quarter is uncovered, it does not prevent, and scattered [uncovering] is combined. Fourth: walking in it for the able person. So if one makes tawaf riding, carried, or crawling without excuse, he must repeat or give blood. If there is an excuse, nothing is upon him. If he vows to make tawaf crawling, he must do it walking. Fifth: al-tayamun (using the right side). Sixth: before the beginning from the Stone.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage lists and explains the seven obligatory (wajib) elements of tawaf according to the Hanafi school, quoting from al-Lubab and other sources. It begins by reminding that purity from the two hadaths (major and minor impurity) is wajib in tawaf, as is covering the private parts. If one tawafs with his ‘awrah uncovered to the extent that prayer would be permissible with that covering (i.e., less than a quarter of the limb), no penalty; otherwise a dam (sacrifice) is due. Purity from physical filth (khabath) is considered sunnah by most Hanafis, but some say it is wajib for the amount covering the ‘awrah. The passage then discusses Tawaf al-Sadr (farewell tawaf) and Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf). After starting Tawaf al-Sadr, it becomes wajib to complete, and all its circuits are wajib. Leaving most of its circuits requires a dam; leaving a few requires a sadaqa for each circuit. Tawaf al-Qudum, being sunnah in itself, does not become wajib by starting; leaving it requires only repentance, like a nafl prayer. The author then lists six of the seven wajibat of tawaf from al-Lubab: (1) purity from hadath, (2) purity from filth (disputed), (3) covering the ‘awrah, (4) walking for the able, (5) using the right side (tayamun), (6) beginning from the Black Stone. The seventh is missing in the OCR but is likely to be 'completing seven circuits' or something similar. The detailed rulings on each wajib include: for covering the ‘awrah, the threshold is a quarter of a limb; if less, it does not impede validity. For walking, if one tawafs without excuse while riding or crawling, he must repeat or pay dam; if excused, no penalty. Vowing to crawl requires walking. This lesson provides a clear mnemonic list for the essential obligatory acts of tawaf.

Key Terms
الطهارة من الحدثين (al-tahara min al-hadathayn): Purity from both major (janaba, hayd, nifas) and minor impurities (lack of wudu). This is wajib for tawaf.
ستر العورة (satr al-awrah): Covering the private parts (for men: navel to knees; for women: entire body except face and hands). This is wajib in tawaf.
التيامن (al-tayamun): Using the right side; i.e., beginning tawaf by facing the Black Stone and moving to the right.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as compensation for leaving a wajib in Hajj or Umrah.
صدقة (sadaqa): Charity; here, a specific amount given as compensation for leaving a few circuits, equivalent to the amount of sadaqat al-fitr (half a sa' of wheat or equivalent).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He must give a sacrifice (dam).
C) He must give charity (sadaqa) for each circuit.
D) He must repeat the entire tawaf.

Key Takeaway
The seven wajibat of tawaf are obligatory but omission is compensated by a sacrifice; they do not invalidate the ritual.

Number of Rounds in Tawaf and the Eighth Round Ruling
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the number of fard rounds and the eighth round ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the required number of fard rounds in tawaf, evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute by comparing majority and Ibn al-Humam’s views, and apply the ruling for an eighth round based on the pilgrim’s intention.

Core Idea
Four rounds are fard, three are wajib; an eighth round requires completion if started with commitment, but not if unintentional.

The number of circumambulations (ashwat) in tawaf is a settled matter in practice—seven complete rounds—but the Hanafi school has an internal debate about which rounds are obligatory (fard) and which are required but not pillars. This lesson unpacks the two positions, their practical consequences, and the specific ruling on adding an eighth round, which turns on the pilgrim’s intention (multazim vs. musqit).

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the correct view according to Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut: four rounds are fard (the rukn), and the remaining three are wajib. The entire tawaf requires seven rounds, but the first four are pillars.
This is the mufta bihi view.
2
Identify the opposing view (Ibn al-Humam)
Ibn al-Humam argues that all seven rounds constitute a single rukn, so less than seven is invalid. He rejects the idea that the majority can stand for the whole (al-akthar yaqumu maqam al-kull).
His reasoning is detailed in al-Jinayat.
3
Analyze the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the majority, if one omits a round, the tawaf is still valid but requires compensation (dam). According to Ibn al-Humam, the tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
This is the key consequence for validity.
4
Apply the ruling on the eighth round
If a pilgrim knowingly begins an eighth round, he is committed (multazim) and must complete it. If he mistakenly begins an eighth round thinking it is the seventh, he is not committed (musqit) and may stop.
The distinction is based on intention at the start of the extra round.
5
Distinguish tawaf from hajj
Unlike tawaf, if one begins a supererogatory act in hajj, it becomes obligatory to complete. Tawaf follows the general rule for supererogatory acts, not the hajj exception.
This comparison highlights the special nature of hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيه فقيل أربعة أشواط وهو الصحيح نص عليه محمد في المبسوط، وذكر الجرجاني أنه ثلاثة أشواط وثلثا شوط، وخالف المحقق ابن الهمام أهل المذهب وجزم بأن السبعة ركن فإنه لا يجزئ أقل منها وأن هذا ليس من قبيل ما يقام فيه الأكثر مقام الكل، وأطال الكلام فيه في الجنايات، وهذا التقدير أعني السبعة مانع للنقصان اتفاقاً واختلفوا في منعه للزيادة حتى لو وعلم أنه ثامن اختلفوا فيه والصحيح أنه يلزمه إتمام الأسبوع لأنه شرع فيه ملتزماً بخلاف ما إذا ظن أنه سابع ثم تبين له أنه ثامن فإنه لا يلزمه الإتمام لأنه شرع فيه مسقطاً لا ملتزماً كالعبادة المظنونة. كذا في المحيط . طاف ثامناً وبهذا علم أن الطواف خالف الحج فإنه إذا شرع فيه مسقطاً يلزمه إتمامه بخلاف بقية العبادات. والأشواط جمع شوط وهو جري مرة إلى الغاية كذا في المغرب. وفي الخانية من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط
In it, it was said: four rounds, and that is the correct view, as stated by Muhammad in al-Mabsut. Al-Jurjani mentioned that it is three and two-thirds rounds. The scholar Ibn al-Humam opposed the school's scholars and asserted that seven rounds are a pillar, for less than that is not sufficient, and this is not of the type where the majority can stand for the whole. He discussed this at length in al-Jinayat. This estimation, meaning seven, is a preventive for deficiency by agreement, but they differed over its prevention of increase such that if he knows it is the eighth, they differed, and the correct view is that he must complete the seven because he began it with a commitment, unlike if he thought it was the seventh and then it became clear that it was the eighth, then he is not obliged to complete it because he began it as non-obligatory, not committed, like a supererogatory act with a supposition. So it is in al-Muhit. He performed an eighth round. And by this, it is known that tawaf differs from hajj, for if he begins it as non-obligatory, he must complete it, unlike other acts of worship. Al-ashwat is plural of shawt, which is a run to the finish line, as in al-Mughrib. In al-Khaniyya: from the Black Stone to the Black Stone is one shawt.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage discusses the required number of rounds (ashwat) in tawaf and the ruling on performing an eighth round. The author begins by presenting different views within the Hanafi school: the correct view according to Imam Muhammad (from al-Mabsut) is that four rounds are sufficient for the fard (obligatory) part of tawaf, while al-Jurjani claimed three and two-thirds. However, the later scholar Ibn al-Humam argued that all seven rounds are a rukn (pillar), meaning the entire tawaf is invalid if any round is omitted. The author then clarifies that everyone agrees that the total acts performed must be seven (to avoid deficiency), but they disagree on whether the additional three are fard or wajib. The key ruling here is about adding an eighth round: if a person knowingly performs an eighth round, they must complete it because they began with the intention of committing to the act (multazim). But if they mistakenly think they are on the seventh and then realize it is the eighth, they are not required to complete it because they started the eighth as a non-obligatory supererogatory act (musqit). This distinction is compared to hajj: in hajj, if one begins a supererogatory act, it becomes obligatory to complete it, unlike other voluntary acts. The passage ends with a linguistic note: 'shawt' means a run from start to finish, and from the Black Stone to the Black Stone is one shawt.

Key Terms
شوط (shawt): A single circumambulation from the Black Stone back to the Black Stone; a complete round around the Kaaba.
ركن (rukn): A pillar or integral part of an act; omission invalidates the act entirely.
ملتزم (multazim): Committed; one who begins an act with the intention of fulfilling an obligation, making completion necessary.
مسقط (musqit): Non-committed; one who begins an act without the intention of obligation, so completion is not required.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He does not need to complete the eighth round and may stop.
C) He must repeat all eight rounds.
D) He must offer a sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, four rounds of tawaf are fard and three are wajib; an eighth round started with commitment must be completed, but if unintentional, it is not obligatory.

Place of Tawaf: Inside the Masjid al-Haram
Ruling on the valid place for tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the required location for tawaf and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) that defines the boundary as the mosque wall.

Core Idea
Tawaf must be inside the Masjid al-Haram; the mosque wall is the legal boundary.

This passage from al-Muhit clarifies a crucial condition for the validity of tawaf: it must be performed within the precincts of the Masjid al-Haram. The author provides a rational proof establishing the mosque wall as the definitive separator between the Kaaba and the outer area. Understanding this ruling is essential for those performing hajj or umrah, as performing tawaf outside the mosque invalidates the act and requires repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is tawaf (circumambulation of the Kaaba). The Hanafi ruling is that it must be performed inside the Masjid al-Haram; performing it outside is invalid (la yajuz) and must be repeated.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is a rational argument (dalil aqli): since one cannot circumambulate while directly touching the Kaaba wall, a legal boundary is needed to define the area that counts as 'around the House'.
The boundary chosen is the mosque wall.
3
Analyse the reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
The entire mosque is considered one legal precinct (buzqa wahida). The wall separates 'near' from 'far'. Thus, circumambulating inside the mosque is circumambulating the House; outside is circumambulating the mosque only, not the House.
This is based on the principle that the direct link to the Kaaba is lost when outside the wall.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If tawaf is performed outside the mosque, it is invalid (batil) and must be repeated in full. There is no compensation like dam; the act is not accepted.
5
Consider the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is that the mosque wall is the definitive boundary. Some other schools may have a more lenient view, but the Hanafis insist on being inside the mosque walls.
The passage does not name the opposing school, but it is a known point of ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مكان الطواف داخل المسجد الحرام حتى لو طاف بالبيت من وراء زمزم أو من وراء السواري جاز، ومن خارج المسجد لا يجوز وعليه أن يعيد لأنه لا يمكنه الطواف ملاصقاً لحائط البيت فلا بد من حد فاصل بين القريب والبعيد فجعلنا الفاصل حائط المسجد لأنه في حكم بقعة واحدة فإذا طاف خارج المسجد فقد طاف بالمسجد لا بالبيت لأن حيطان المسجد تحول بينه وبين البيت كذا في المحيط.
And know that the place of tawaf is inside the Masjid al-Haram, such that if he circumambulates the House from behind Zamzam or from behind the columns, it is permissible, but from outside the mosque it is not permissible and he must repeat it because he cannot circumambulate adjacent to the wall of the House, so there must be a separator between near and far, so we made the separator the mosque wall because it is in the ruling of one precinct. Thus if he circumambulates outside the mosque, he has circumambulated the mosque, not the House, because the walls of the mosque intervene between him and the House. So it is in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
The author now clarifies the physical location for tawaf: it must be performed inside the Masjid al-Haram. Even if one circumambulates from behind Zamzam or the pillars (sawari), it is valid because those are inside the mosque. However, performing tawaf outside the mosque is invalid and requires repetition. The reasoning is that the tawaf must be as close as possible to the Kaaba, but since one cannot literally touch the wall, a legal boundary is needed. The Hanafi scholars set the mosque wall as that boundary because the entire mosque is considered one contiguous area in legal rulings. When one is outside the mosque wall, they are circumambulating the mosque, not the Kaaba itself, because the wall severs direct connection. This ruling is from al-Muhit.

Key Terms
المسجد الحرام (al-Masjid al-Haram): The Sacred Mosque surrounding the Kaaba in Mecca; the area defined by its walls.
الطواف (al-tawaf): The act of circumambulating the Kaaba seven times in worship, a pillar of hajj and umrah.
حائط المسجد (ha'it al-masjid): The wall of the mosque, serving as the legal boundary for tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is tawaf valid if performed from behind the Zamzam well but still inside the mosque walls?
A) Yes, it is valid because it is inside the mosque.
B) No, one must be closer to the Kaaba.
C) It is valid only if performed while touching the wall.
D) It is valid only during the day.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf is only valid when performed inside the Masjid al-Haram; the mosque wall is the legal boundary that distinguishes valid from invalid.

Obligations of Purity and Covering Awrah in Tawaf
Rulings on purity and covering awrah in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligations of taharah and satr al-awrah in tawaf, and apply the Hanafi rulings on compensation for their violation.

Core Idea
Purity from hadath and najasah, and covering awrah are wajib in tawaf; violation requires dam or sadaqah.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym builds on previously established obligations of hajj to clarify the conditions of tawaf. He affirms that purification from minor and major hadath is wajib, as is covering the private parts. The discussion then shifts to the effect of physical impurity (najasah) after commencing tawaf, leading to an intra-Hanafi debate about whether compensation is due for abandoning the initial tawaf. Understanding these layers helps you apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory conditions of tawaf
From the opening, note that purification from both hadath (minor/major) and covering the awrah are wajib. The text says 'purification from hadath is obligatory, and likewise covering the awrah.'
The ruling is clear: these are conditions for validity.
2
Examine the consequence of uncovering the awrah
If one performs tawaf with awrah uncovered to the extent that prayer would be invalid, he owes a dam. This is explicitly stated from al-Zahirah.
Dam is a sacrificial animal, not just sadaqah.
3
Distinguish between hadath and najasah
The text then says 'as for purification from najasah, then from hadath' — meaning after commencing tawaf, the ruling for najasah becomes like that of hadath: both tawafs become obligatory.
This is a key point: commencement transforms the optional tawaf into a wajib one.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for leaving the initial tawaf
Al-Sindi analogizes the initial tawaf to tawaf al-Sadr, requiring dam for leaving most rounds. Others reject the analogy because tawaf al-Sadr is intrinsically wajib. The preferred view is that only tawbah is needed.
This illustrates how qiyas is used and contested within the school.
5
Understand when leaving is actualized
The text concludes that leaving the tawaf is only truly realized by leaving Mecca, not merely stopping the rounds.
This affects when compensation applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد علمت مما قدمناه واجبات الحج أن الطهارة فيه من الحدثين واجب وكذا ستر العورة، فلو طاف مكشوف العورة قدر ما تجوز الصلاة معه لزمه دم كذا في الظهيرية وأما الطهارة من الخبث فمن الحدث فيساوي بعد الشروع طواف الصدر فيصير الطوافان واجبين فيكون جميع أشواطهما واجبة، ويؤيد ذلك ما سيذكره المؤلف قريباً في أشواط السعي حيث جعلها واجبة كلها، لكن صرحوا بأنه لو ترك أكثر أشواط الصدر لزمه دم، وفي الأقل لكل شوط صدقة. وأما القدروم فلم يصرحوا بما يلزمه لو تركه بعد الشروع، وبحث السندي في منسكه الكبير في أنه كالصدر ونازعه في شرح اللباب بأن الصدر واجب بأصله فلا يقاس عليه ما يجب بشروعه، فالظاهر أنه لا يلزمه بتركه شيء سوى التوبة كصلاة النفل ا هـ ملخصاً. وهذا ما ظهر لي قبل أن أراه وسيأتي أنه لا يتحقق الترك إلا بالخروج من مكة
And you have already learned from what we previously presented of the obligations of hajj that purification from both hadaths (minor and major) is obligatory, and likewise covering the private parts (awrah). So if he performed tawaf with his awrah uncovered to the extent that would make prayer permissible, he owes a dam (sacrifice) as in al-Zahirah. As for purification from filth (najasah), then from hadath, it equates after commencement to the tawaf of al-Sadr (the final tawaf), so both tawafs become obligatory, and thus all their rounds become obligatory. That is supported by what the author will mention shortly about the rounds of sa'i, where he makes all of them obligatory. But they explicitly stated that if he leaves most rounds of al-Sadr, he owes a dam, and for each round of the few, a sadaqah. As for al-Qadrum (the initial tawaf?), they did not specify what he owes if he leaves it after commencement. Al-Sindi researched in his al-Mansak al-Kabir that it is like al-Sadr, and he was challenged in Sharh al-Lubab that al-Sadr is obligatory in itself, so what becomes obligatory due to commencement cannot be analogized to it. The apparent view is that he is not obliged by leaving it except repentance (tawbah), like a supererogatory prayer. Summary. This was what appeared to me before seeing it, and it will come that leaving is only actualized by leaving Mecca.
Source pages p. 576

Commentary
This passage builds on earlier knowledge (from the obligations of hajj) regarding the obligatory conditions of tawaf. The author states that purification from both major and minor hadath (state of ritual impurity) is wajib, as is covering the awrah (private parts). If someone performs tawaf with their awrah exposed to the extent that would invalidate prayer if uncovered, they must offer a dam (sacrificial animal). Then the discussion turns to purification from physical najasah (impurity). The author compares it to hadath: after beginning tawaf, the ruling becomes similar to the tawaf al-Sadr (the final obligatory tawaf after leaving Mina), which makes all rounds obligatory. This is supported by the fact that in sa'i (the running between Safa and Marwa), all rounds are wajib. However, scholars clarify that if one misses most rounds of tawaf al-Sadr, a dam is due; for each round missed, a sadaqah (charity) is due. For the initial tawaf (al-Qadrum – which could be the tawaf of arrival or the first tawaf), they did not specify compensation. Al-Sindi argued it is like al-Sadr, but others countered that al-Sadr is inherently wajib, so a tawaf that becomes wajib only by commencement cannot be analogized. The preferable view is that leaving it after commencement requires only repentance, not compensation, similar to an optional prayer. The author adds that leaving is only truly realized by leaving Mecca.

Key Terms
الحدثان (al-hadathan): The two types of ritual impurity: minor (hadath asghar, requiring wudu) and major (hadath akbar, requiring ghusl).
العورة (al-'awrah): Parts of the body that must be covered in prayer and tawaf.
الخبث (al-khabath): Physical impurity (najasah) on the body or clothes.
القدروم (al-qadrum): The initial tawaf (probably tawaf al-qudum, the arrival tawaf).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what compensation is required if a person performs tawaf with a small amount of najasah on their clothes after having commenced?
A) Nothing, because the tawaf was optional originally.
B) A dam, because it becomes like tawaf al-Sadr.
C) Only repentance (tawbah), as per the preferred view.
D) A dam if most rounds are left, else sadaqah per round.

Key Takeaway
Purity from hadath and najasah and covering the awrah are wajib conditions of tawaf; abandonment of an initially optional tawaf after commencement requires only repentance, not a dam.

Seven Obligations (Wajibat) of Tawaf in the Hanafi School
List of seven wajibat with commentary and an added eighth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven wajibat of tawaf according to al-Lubab, identify the differences in ruling for each, and apply the exception for walking when ill.

Core Idea
Tawaf has seven wajib elements; missing one requires a dam, but some are more lenient than others.

This lesson unpacks the list of seven wajibat (obligations) of tawaf as presented in al-Lubab, a later Hanafi text. The commentator adds an eighth wajib and clarifies disputes, such as the status of purification from filth and the purity of the place. By the end, you will know exactly what is required to perform a valid tawaf and when a dam (sacrifice) becomes necessary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source and purpose
Recognize that al-Lubab enumerates seven wajibat – these are obligatory elements whose omission requires compensation, but are not pillars (arkan). The commentator expands on each.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is quoting from al-Lubab, a standard Hanafi text.
2
Work through each wajib in order
For each of the seven, understand what it requires and any exception. For example: purification from major/minor hadath (first), covering awrah (third), walking for the able (fourth).
Pay attention to the second wajib: purification from actual filth – the majority consider it sunnah, not wajib.
3
Note the differences voiced by the commentator
The commentator mentions that purity of the tawaf place is not a condition or pillar, and the author (Ibn Nujaym) adds an eighth wajib: completing seven full rounds.
This addition completes the list; without seven rounds, tawaf is invalid.
4
Apply the ruling for walking vs. riding
Understand that walking is wajib for the able; if one rides without excuse, he must either repeat tawaf or offer a dam. With an excuse, no penalty.
Similarly, if one vows to crawl, he must walk – vows do not override obligations.
5
Synthesize the list with the added eighth
Compile all eight elements: purification from hadath, purification from najasah (sunnah), covering awrah, walking, tayamun (Kaaba on left), starting from Black Stone, being behind Hatim, and seven rounds.
The eighth is technically a rukn, but included here for completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وقد علمت الخ) قال في اللباب واجبات الطواف سبعة: الأول الطهارة عن الأكبر والأصغر الثاني قيل الطهارة عن النجاسة الحقيقية والأكثر على أنه سنة، وقيل قدر ما يستر عورته من الثواب واجب أي طهارته فلو طاف وعليه قدر ما يواري العورة طاهر والباقي نجس جاز وإلا فهو بمنزلة .العريان الثالث ستر العورة فلو طاف مكشوفها وجب الدم، والمانع كشف ربع العضو فما زاد كما في الصلاة وإن انكشف أقل من الربع لا يمنع ويجمع المتفرق. الرابع المشي فيه للقادر فلو طاف راكباً أو محمولاً أو زحفاً بلا عذر فعليه الإعادة أو الدم، وإن كان بعذر لا شيء عليه، ولو نذر أن يطوف زحفاً لزمه ماشياً. الخامس التيامن السادس قبل الابتداء من الحجر الأسود، السابع الطواف وراء الحطيم ا هـ . قال شارحه : وأما طهارة مكان الطواف فذكر ابن جماعة عن صاحب الغاية أنه لو كان في موضع طوافه نجاسة لا يبطل ،طوافه وهذا يفيد نفي الشرط والفرضية واحتمال ثبوت الوجوب والسنية والأرجح عدم الوجوب عند الشافعية ا هـ . قلت : ويزاد ثامن وهو كونه سبعة أشواط
His statement: (And you have learned, etc.) He said in al-Lubab: The obligations of tawaf are seven: First: purification from major and minor. Second: it was said purification from actual filth; but the majority hold that it is sunnah. And it was said that the ability to cover his awrah with a garment is obligatory, i.e., its purity. So if he performs tawaf while wearing enough to cover his awrah that is pure, and the rest is impure, it is permissible; otherwise, he is like the naked. Third: covering the awrah. So if he performs tawaf with it uncovered, a dam is obligatory. The preventive is uncovering a quarter of a limb or more, as in prayer. If less than a quarter is uncovered, it does not prevent; scattered (uncoverings) are summed. Fourth: walking for the capable. So if he performs tawaf riding, being carried, or crawling without an excuse, he must repeat or offer a dam. With an excuse, nothing is required. If he vows to perform tawaf crawling, he must do it walking. Fifth: keeping to the right (al-tayamun). Sixth: starting from the Black Stone. Seventh: performing tawaf behind the Hatim. End quote. His commentator said: As for purity of the place of tawaf, Ibn Jama'a mentioned from al-Ghaya that if there is impurity in his tawaf area, it does not invalidate his tawaf. This indicates negation of condition and pillar, and there is a possibility of obligation and sunnah. The more likely view is that it is not obligatory according to the Shafi'is. End quote. I say: An eighth should be added: that it be seven rounds.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
The author quotes from the work al-Lubab a list of seven wajibat (obligatory elements) for tawaf. The first is purification from both major and minor ritual impurity (hadath). The second is purification from actual filth (najasah), but the majority say this is sunnah, not wajib. The third is covering the awrah; if uncovered, a dam is due. The measure is that uncovering a quarter of a limb or more is harmful, less than a quarter is overlooked, and multiple small uncoverings are combined. The fourth is walking (not riding) if one is able; without excuse, one must repeat or offer dam. The fifth is to keep the Kaaba on the left (tayamun). The sixth is starting from the Black Stone. The seventh is staying behind the Hatim. The commentator adds a note: purity of the place of tawaf is not a condition or pillar; it is not wajib according to Shafi'is. The author (Ibn Nujaym) adds an eighth obligation: that the tawaf must be seven rounds in total.

Key Terms
الحطيم (al-Hatim): The curved wall (or semicircular wall) adjacent to the Kaaba; tawaf must go behind it.
التيمن (al-tayamun): Keeping the right side forward or starting from the Black Stone with the right shoulder; in context, it means keeping the Kaaba on the left during tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on purification from actual filth (najasah) during tawaf according to the majority of scholars in this text?
A) It is wajib.
B) It is makruh.
C) It is sunnah.
D) It is haram.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf has seven wajib elements, but the second (purification from najasah) is sunnah according to the majority, and an eighth (seven rounds) is essential for validity.

Superiority of Dhikr over Quran Recitation in Tawaf
Ruling on preferred remembrance in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prefers dhikr over Quran recitation during tawaf and cite the supporting hadith.

Core Idea
Dhikr is the practice of the Prophet; no specific Quran recitation is reported for tawaf.

This lesson explores the recommended form of remembrance during tawaf. The Hanafi position is that dhikr, specifically the phrases mentioned in the hadith, is superior to reciting the Quran while circumambulating the Kaaba. We will examine the evidence from a hadith narrated by Ibn Majah and understand why this practice is considered the best.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tawaf; the ruling is that dhikr is the known (al-ma'ruf) practice and superior to Quran recitation.
The author indicates this is the preferred view (afdal).
2
Examine the dalil from hadith
The hadith from Ibn Majah reports that the Prophet said that performing tawaf while reciting specific dhikr phrases brings great reward.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but supports the Hanafi position.
3
Understand the Hanafi inference
Since no hadith is known that prescribes Quran recitation during tawaf, the Hanafis conclude that dhikr is the more meritorious practice.
4
Conclude the recommended practice
The mufta bihi is to engage in dhikr during tawaf; Quran recitation is permissible but not as virtuous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمعروف في الطواف إنما هو مجرد ذكر الله تعالى) أشار إلى أنه أفضل من القراءة كما في الفتح عن التجنيس وقال : ولم نعلم خبراً روي فيه قراءة القرآن في الطواف روى ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة أنه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول «من طاف سمع بالبيت سبعاً ولم يتكلم إلا بسبحان الله والحمد لله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله محيت عنه عشر سيآت، وكتبت له عشر حسنات، ورفع له بها عشر درجات» وفي المحيط : لو خرج من طوافه إلى جنازة أو مكتوبة أو تجديد وضوء ثم عاد بني.
His statement: (And what is known in tawaf is only mere remembrance of Allah) He indicated that it is superior to recitation (Quran) as in al-Fath from al-Tajnis. And he said: We do not know a report of reciting the Quran during tawaf. Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Huraira that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever performs tawaf around the House seven times and does not speak except with 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, la ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar, and la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah,' ten sins are erased for him, ten good deeds are written for him, and he is raised ten degrees.' And in al-Muhit: If he leaves his tawaf for a funeral, an obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, then returns, he builds upon what he has done.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
The passage discusses what is known and recommended in tawaf: it should primarily be remembrance of Allah (dhikr). The author notes that this is superior to reciting the Quran, based on sources like al-Fath and al-Tajnis, since no hadith is known that specifically prescribes Quran recitation during tawaf. A hadith from Ibn Majah is cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that performing tawaf with limited speech, mainly the phrases of glorification, praise, declaring God's oneness, and expressions of power, brings great rewards. Additionally, from al-Muhit, there is a ruling: if one leaves the tawaf for a valid reason such as attending a funeral, performing an obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, and then returns, he may continue from where he left off (he builds upon the previous rounds). This indicates that tawaf does not become invalid due to short interruptions for necessary acts.

Key Terms
الذكر (al-dhikr): Remembrance of Allah, specifically the phrases mentioned in the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Reciting the Quran
B) The specific dhikr phrases: Subhan Allah, Alhamdulillah, etc.
C) Supplications of one's own choosing
D) Silence

Key Takeaway
In tawaf, the most meritorious remembrance is the dhikr phrases reported in the hadith, reflecting the Sunna.

Permissible Interruptions During Tawaf
Ruling on building upon tawaf after permissible interruption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the acts for which a pilgrim may interrupt tawaf and then continue from where they left off.

Core Idea
Necessary interruptions like prayer or wudu allow building upon previous tawaf rounds.

This lesson examines a practical ruling from al-Muhit: if a pilgrim leaves tawaf for a funeral prayer, an obligatory prayer, or to renew wudu, they may return and continue from the point they stopped. Understanding this concession helps pilgrims manage necessary breaks without invalidating their worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is temporarily leaving the state of tawaf for a valid need; the ruling is that the tawaf is not invalidated and one may build (bana) upon previous rounds.
This is a concession (rukhsah).
2
List the permissible causes
The text explicitly mentions: attending a funeral prayer (janaza), performing an obligatory prayer (maktubah), and renewing wudu (tajdid wudu).
These are necessary religious acts.
3
Understand the condition
The pilgrim must return after the interruption; building is contingent on returning to continue the same tawaf.
If the interruption is prolonged or for a voluntary act, the ruling may differ.
4
Apply the ruling
If a pilgrim, after completing three rounds, leaves to pray Zuhr, then returns, they should start the fourth round where they stopped.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمعروف في الطواف إنما هو مجرد ذكر الله تعالى) أشار إلى أنه أفضل من القراءة كما في الفتح عن التجنيس وقال : ولم نعلم خبراً روي فيه قراءة القرآن في الطواف روى ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة أنه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول «من طاف سمع بالبيت سبعاً ولم يتكلم إلا بسبحان الله والحمد لله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله محيت عنه عشر سيآت، وكتبت له عشر حسنات، ورفع له بها عشر درجات» وفي المحيط : لو خرج من طوافه إلى جنازة أو مكتوبة أو تجديد وضوء ثم عاد بني.
His statement: (And what is known in tawaf is only mere remembrance of Allah) He indicated that it is superior to recitation (Quran) as in al-Fath from al-Tajnis. And he said: We do not know a report of reciting the Quran during tawaf. Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Huraira that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever performs tawaf around the House seven times and does not speak except with 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdulillah, la ilaha illallah, Allahu Akbar, and la hawla wa la quwwata illa billah,' ten sins are erased for him, ten good deeds are written for him, and he is raised ten degrees.' And in al-Muhit: If he leaves his tawaf for a funeral, an obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, then returns, he builds upon what he has done.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
The passage discusses what is known and recommended in tawaf: it should primarily be remembrance of Allah (dhikr). The author notes that this is superior to reciting the Quran, based on sources like al-Fath and al-Tajnis, since no hadith is known that specifically prescribes Quran recitation during tawaf. A hadith from Ibn Majah is cited: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said that performing tawaf with limited speech, mainly the phrases of glorification, praise, declaring God's oneness, and expressions of power, brings great rewards. Additionally, from al-Muhit, there is a ruling: if one leaves the tawaf for a valid reason such as attending a funeral, performing an obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, and then returns, he may continue from where he left off (he builds upon the previous rounds). This indicates that tawaf does not become invalid due to short interruptions for necessary acts.

Key Terms
بني (bana): He builds upon; meaning he continues the tawaf from where he stopped, not restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage from al-Muhit, which of the following is a valid reason to interrupt tawaf and continue later?
A) Taking a break to rest
B) Renewing wudu
C) Answering a phone call
D) Buying a souvenir

Key Takeaway
Leaving tawaf for a funeral, obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu does not invalidate it; one may continue from where they stopped.

Ramal in Tawaf: Sunnah and the Principle of Alternate Causes
Ruling on ramal and its continued practice despite cause change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ramal and explain why it remains sunnah even after the original cause has ceased, using the principle of alternate causes.

Core Idea
Ramal is sunnah muakkadah; its continuation is justified by alternate causes, not inertia.

Ramal (brisk walking with shoulder movement) in tawaf is a well-known practice. Even though the original reason—to intimidate the polytheists—no longer applies, the practice remains. This lesson examines the textual evidence and the legal reasoning (ta'lil) that allows a ruling to persist when its cause changes, using examples from slavery and kharaj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that ramal is performed in the first three rounds only, and it is a sunnah. Identify that ramal is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for men in tawaf al-qudum and tawaf al-ifadah.
Not for women.
2
Note the original cause and the objection
The original cause for ramal was to show strength to the polytheists. After the conquest of Mecca, this cause ceased, leading some to argue the ruling should cease. Understand the general principle: a ruling ceases when its cause ceases.
This principle is valid but not absolute.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response has two parts: (1) The Prophet himself performed ramal in the Farewell Pilgrimage as a reminder of gratitude for security. (2) A ruling can have alternate causes; the cause can change while the ruling remains. Recognize that the Prophet's act is a sunnah, establishing it as a practice.
The hadith from Sahihayn is the primary dalil.
4
Relate to examples for deeper understanding
The text gives two analogies: slavery (originally due to disbelief, then due to legal ruling) and kharaj land tax (originally punitive, then a fixed levy). Both show how a ruling can persist with a changed cause.
This illustrates the concept of ta'lil with alternating 'illahs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ترمل في الثلاثة الأول فقط) بيان للسنة أي في الأشواط الثلاثة الأول دون غيرها فأفاد أنه من الحجر إلى الحجر لحديث ابن عمر وابن عباس في حجة الوداع المروي في الصحيحين رداً على من قال إنه ينتهي إلى الركن اليماني واعلم أن الأصل زوال الحكم عند زوال العلة لأن الحكم ملزوم لوجود العلة ووجود الملزوم بدون اللازم محال : وقول من قال إن علة الرمل في الطواف زالت وبقي الحكم ممنوع فإن النبي الهرمل في حجة الوداع تذكيراً لنعمة الأمن بعد الخوف ليشكر عليها فقد أمر الله بذكر نعمه في مواضع من كتابه . وما أمرنا بذكرها إلا لنشكرها ويجوز أن يثبت الحكم بعلل متبادلة فحين غلبة المشركين كانت علة الرمل إبهام المشركين قوة المؤمنين وعند زوال ذلك تكون علته تذكير نعمة الأمن كما أن علة الرق في الأصل استنكاف الكافر عن عبادة ربه ثم صار علته حكم الشرع برقه وإن أسلم وكالخراج فإنه يثبت في الابتداء بطريق العقوبة ولهذا الا يبتدأ به على المسلم ثم صار علته حكم الشرع بذلك حتى لو اشترى المسلم أرض خراج لزمه عليه الخراج. كذا ذكره المحقق
His statement: (And he performs ramal in the first three only) is an explanation of the sunnah, i.e., in the first three rounds only, not others. So it indicates that it is from the Black Stone to the Black Stone, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas in the Farewell Pilgrimage narrated in the Sahihayn, refuting those who said it ends at the Yemeni corner. And know that the principle is that the ruling ceases when the cause ceases, because the ruling is determined by the existence of the cause, and the existence of the determined without the determinant is impossible. And the statement of one who said that the cause of ramal in tawaf has ceased and the ruling remains is rejected, for the Prophet performed ramal in the Farewell Pilgrimage as a reminder of the blessing of security after fear, to give thanks for it. Indeed, Allah commanded remembrance of His blessings in various places in His Book. And He commanded us to remember them only to be grateful. And it is permissible for a ruling to be established by alternate causes: at the time of the polytheists' predominance, the cause of ramal was to give the polytheists the impression of the Muslims' strength, and when that ceased, its cause became the reminder of the blessing of security. Similarly, the cause of slavery in origin was the disbeliever's refusal to worship his Lord, then its cause became the ruling of the Law to enslave him even if he becomes Muslim. And like the kharaj, it is initially established as a punishment, therefore it is not initially imposed on a Muslim, then its cause became the ruling of the Law, such that if a Muslim buys kharaj land, kharaj is due upon him. Thus the researcher mentioned.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
The final section discusses ramal, which is walking briskly with short steps, shaking the shoulders, in the first three rounds of tawaf. The author states that this is a sunnah (recommended practice) based on the hadith of the Farewell Pilgrimage from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. The practice extends from the Black Stone to the Black Stone, contrary to some who say it ends at the Yemeni corner. A key point is that even though the original reason for ramal – to show physical strength to the polytheists who claimed the Muslims were weak – no longer exists, the practice remains. The principle that a ruling ceases when its cause ceases is countered by two arguments: (1) The Prophet himself continued ramal in the Farewell Pilgrimage after the conquest of Mecca, as a reminder of the blessing of security and to give thanks. (2) A ruling can have alternate causes; initially the cause was to deceive the polytheists, but later the cause became gratitude for safety. This is similar to slavery (first caused by disbelief, then by the ruling of the Law) and kharaj land tax (first a punishment for non-Muslims, then a legal rule that even a Muslim buyer must pay). Thus ramal remains a sunnah.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-ramal): Walking briskly with short steps while moving the shoulders, similar to a marching gait, performed in the first three rounds of tawaf.
العلة (al-'illa): The legal cause or rationale behind a ruling; here, the cause of ramal changed from displaying strength to expressing gratitude.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the continued practice of ramal even after the conquest of Mecca?
A) The original cause still exists.
B) It is a personal opinion of scholars.
C) The Prophet performed it as a reminder of gratitude for security.
D) It is based on qiyas with slavery.

Key Takeaway
Ramal remains sunnah muakkadah due to the Prophet's continued practice and the juristic principle that a ruling can have alternate causes.

Tawaf in an Impure Garment
States ruling on tawaf in impure garment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tawaf in a garment that is partially impure and explain the condition regarding the awrah.

Core Idea
Tawaf is valid if the part covering the awrah is pure, even if the rest is impure.

The Hanafi school provides a practical ruling for pilgrims who may have impurity on their garments during tawaf. Unlike prayer, where the entire garment must be pure, tawaf allows leniency as long as the essential parts covering the private area remain pure. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its scenarios
The text discusses tawaf performed in a garment that is impure. Two scenarios: the garment is completely impure, or only part of it is impure.
2
Understand the analogy for complete impurity
If the entire garment is impure, it is equivalent to performing tawaf naked — both are invalid.
This analogy shows the gravity of complete impurity.
3
Apply the condition for partial impurity
If the part of the garment covering the awrah (private parts) is pure, the tawaf is valid. The rest of the garment may be impure without penalty.
The awrah must be covered with a pure material.
4
Note the consequence
No penalty (dam) is required for such a valid tawaf.
This is a leniency from the Hanafi school.
5
Contrast with other schools
Shafi'is require the entire place of tawaf to be pure; Hanafis do not. This highlights the difference in legal methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السنة لا يلزمه بتركها شيء كما صرح به في المحيط وغيره لكن صرح في الفتاوى الظهيرية بأنه لو طاف طواف الزيارة في ثوب كله نجس فهذا وما لو طاف عرياناً سواء، فإن كان من الثوب قدر ما يواري عورته طاهراً والباقي نجساً جاز طوافه ولا شيء عليه. وأطلق الطواف فأفاد أنه لا يكره في الأوقات التي تكره الصلاة فيها لأن الطواف ليس بصلاة حقيقة ولهذا أبيح الكلام فيه كما ورد في الحديث ولا تبطله المحاذاة وقالوا : لا بأس بأن يفتي في الطواف ويشرب ويفعل ما يحتاج إليه لكن يكره إنشاد الشعر فيه والحديث لغير حاجة والبيع، وأما قراءة القرآن فيه فمباحة في نفسه ولا يرفع بها صوته كما في المحيط. والمعروف في الطواف إنما هو مجرد ذكر الله روى ابن ماجه عن أبي هريرة أنه النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول «من طاف سمع بالبيت سبعاً ولم يتكلم إلا بسبحان الله والحمد لله ولا إله إلا الله والله أكبر ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله محيت عنه عشر سيآت، وكتبت له عشر حسنات، ورفع له بها عشر درجات»(۱) وفي المحيط : لو خرج من طوافه إلى جنازة أو مكتوبة أو تجديد وضوء ثم عاد بني.
The sunnah: nothing is binding upon its abandonment, as clarified in al-Muhit and others. However, it is clarified in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya that if one performs the tawaf of visit in a garment entirely impure, then this and if he performed tawaf naked are the same. If there is from the garment enough to cover his nakedness that is pure, and the rest is impure, his tawaf is valid and nothing is upon him. He generalized tawaf, so it indicates that it is not disliked in times in which prayer is disliked, because tawaf is not actually prayer; therefore speech is permitted in it as reported in the hadith, and alignment does not invalidate it. They said: there is no harm in giving fatwa in tawaf, drinking, and doing what he needs, but reciting poetry in it is disliked, and talking without need, and selling. As for reciting Quran in it, it is permissible in itself, and one should not raise his voice in it, as in al-Muhit. What is known in tawaf is only remembrance of Allah. Ibn Majah narrated from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever performs tawaf around the House seven times and does not speak except with 'Subhan Allah, al-Hamdu lillah, La ilaha illa Allah, Allahu Akbar, La hawla wa la quwwata illa billah', ten sins are erased from him, ten good deeds are written for him, and he is raised ten degrees.' And in al-Muhit: if he leaves his tawaf for a funeral, an obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, then returns, he builds upon what he did.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies several rulings regarding tawaf. First, it addresses the issue of impurity on the garment during tawaf. According to the Hanafi school, if the entire garment is impure, the tawaf is invalid, akin to performing tawaf naked. However, if only part of the garment is impure while the portion covering the awrah (private parts) remains pure, the tawaf is valid with no penalty. Second, the passage states that tawaf is not disliked at times when prayer is prohibited, because tawaf is not considered a form of prayer in the literal sense; thus, speaking during tawaf is permissible, as confirmed by hadith. Various actions such as giving fatwa, drinking, and attending to needs are allowed, but reciting poetry, engaging in unnecessary conversation, and selling are disliked. Reciting the Quran is permissible but should not be done loudly. The recommended practice during tawaf is to engage in dhikr (remembrance of Allah), and a hadith from Ibn Majah illustrates the immense reward for doing so: the erasure of ten sins, recording of ten good deeds, and elevation by ten degrees. Finally, if one interrupts tawaf for a funeral prayer, an obligatory prayer, or to renew wudu, they may resume from where they left off, as per al-Muhit.

Key Terms
نجسة (najis): Impure; here referring to a garment that is ritually impure due to contact with najasah.
عورة (awrah): Private parts that must be covered during tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a pilgrim performs tawaf in a garment that is partially impure but the part covering the awrah is pure?
A) The tawaf is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The tawaf is valid with no penalty.
C) The tawaf is valid but requires a penalty of one dam.
D) The tawaf is valid only if the impurity is less than a dirham's area.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the validity of tawaf in an impure garment hinges on the purity of the cloth covering the awrah, not the entire garment.

Permissible and Disliked Actions During Tawaf
States permissible and disliked actions in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify actions during tawaf as permissible, disliked, or recommended, and explain the hadith on reward for dhikr.

Core Idea
Tawaf is not like prayer: speech is allowed, but idle talk and poetry are disliked.

Tawaf is a unique act of worship that combines physical movement with remembrance of Allah. The Hanafi school clarifies that tawaf is not considered a form of prayer (salat) in the strict sense, so many actions that would invalidate prayer are permissible. However, there are still etiquettes and disliked matters. This lesson covers what is allowed and what is discouraged during tawaf, including the reward for engaging in dhikr.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of tawaf
Tawaf is not literally prayer; therefore, it is not disliked at times when prayer is prohibited, and speech is permitted.
This is the foundational principle for the rulings.
2
List permissible actions
Giving fatwa, drinking, attending to needs, speaking, reciting Quran (without raising voice), and alignment with the Black Stone are all permissible.
3
Identify disliked actions
Reciting poetry, unnecessary talk, and selling are disliked.
Disliked (makruh) means it is better to avoid.
4
Understand the recommended practice
The best practice is to engage in dhikr (remembrance of Allah) as taught by the Prophet (peace be upon him).
A hadith lists specific phrases and their reward.
5
Apply the rule on interruption
If one leaves tawaf for a funeral prayer, obligatory prayer, or renewing wudu, they may resume from where they stopped.
This is a concession.
