Raml in Tawaf: Legal Cause and the Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Explains raml, its legal cause, and compares Hanafi-Shafi'i views on purity of place.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raml and explain why its continuation is justified despite the change in its original cause.

Core Idea
Raml remains sunnah even after its original cause ceases because legal causes are indicators, not effectors.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a key fiqh question: why does raml (brisk walking) continue as a sunnah in tawaf after its original cause—showing strength to the polytheists—has disappeared? The text explains that the cause shifted to gratitude, supported by an important usul principle that legal causes are merely indicators. It also compares the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on purity of place in tawaf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on raml
Identify the ruling: raml is sunnah muakkadah in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum, from the Black Stone to the Black Stone.
Based on hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas.
2
Identify the objection to the continuation of raml
Some argue that since the original cause (showing strength) is gone, the ruling should cease. This is based on the principle that a ruling is concomitant with its cause.
The objection is mentioned and refuted.
3
Trace the Hanafi response using the shift in cause
The Hanafi response: the cause shifted from demonstrating strength to gratitude. Legal causes are indicators (amarat), not effectors (mu'thirat), so the ruling can persist. This is supported by analogies with slavery and kharaj.
Refer to Ibn al-Humam's discussion.
4
Note the dispute with the Shafi'is on purity of place
Hanafis say purity of place is not a condition; tawaf is valid even if the ground is impure. The Shafi'i view is that it is not wajib (most likely view).
Text cites Ibn Jama'ah from al-Ghayat.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If there is impurity on the mataf, Hanafis consider tawaf valid; Shafi'is consider it invalid unless the impurity is small.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ترمل في الثلاثة الأول فقط) بيان للسنة أي في الأشواط الثلاثة الأول دون غيرها فأفاد أنه من الحجر إلى الحجر لحديث ابن عمر وابن عباس في حجة الوداع المروي في الصحيحين رداً على من قال إنه ينتهي إلى الركن اليماني واعلم أن الأصل زوال الحكم عند زوال العلة لأن الحكم ملزوم لوجود العلة ووجود الملزوم بدون اللازم محال : وقول من قال إن علة الرمل في الطواف زالت وبقي الحكم ممنوع فإن النبي الهرمل في حجة الوداع تذكيراً لنعمة الأمن بعد الخوف ليشكر عليها فقد أمر الله بذكر نعمه في مواضع من كتابه . وما أمرنا بذكرها إلا لنشكرها ويجوز أن يثبت الحكم بعلل متبادلة فحين غلبة المشركين كانت علة الرمل إبهام المشركين قوة المؤمنين وعند زوال ذلك تكون علته تذكير نعمة الأمن كما أن علة الرق في الأصل استنكاف الكافر عن عبادة ربه ثم صار علته حكم الشرع برقه وإن أسلم وكالخراج فإنه يثبت في الابتداء بطريق العقوبة ولهذا الا يبتدأ به على المسلم ثم صار علته حكم الشرع بذلك حتى لو اشترى المسلم أرض خراج لزمه عليه الخراج. كذا ذكره المحقق الأسود، السابع الطواف وراء الحطيم ا هـ . قال شارحه : وأما طهارة مكان الطواف فذكر ابن جماعة عن صاحب الغاية أنه لو كان في موضع طوافه نجاسة لا يبطل طوافه وهذا يفيد نفي الشرط والفرضية واحتمال ثبوت الوجوب والسنية والأرجح عدم الوجوب عند الشافعية ا هـ . قلت : ويزاد ثامن وهو كونه سبعة أشواط قوله : والمعروف في الطواف إنما هو مجرد ذكر الله تعالى) أشار إلى أنه أفضل من القراءة كما في الفتح عن التجنيس وقال : ولم نعلم خبراً روي فيه قراءة القرآن في أكمل الدين في شرح البزدوي من بحث القدرة الميسرة. وقد رد المحقق ابن الهمام في باب العشر والخراج كون الحكم ملزوماً لوجود العلة في العلل الشرعية لأن العلل الشرعية أمارات على الحكم لا مؤثرات فيجوز بقاء الحكم بعد زوال علته وإنما ذلك في العلل العقلية. وأشار بقوله بعد ذلك ثم أخرج إلى الصفا» إلى أنه لا يرمل إلا في طواف بعده سعي، فلو أراد تأخير السعي إلى طواف الزيارة لا يرمل في طواف القدوم، وذكر الشارح معزياً إلى الغاية إذا كان قارناً لم يرمل في طواف القدوم إن كان رمل في طواف العمرة. وأشار بقوله «فقط» إلى أنه لو ترك الرمل في الشوط الأول لا يرمل إلا في الشوطين بعده وبنسيانه في الثلاثة الأول لا يرمل في الباقي لأن ترك الرمل في الأربعة سنة ، فلو رمل فيها لكان تاركاً للسنتين وكان ترك أحدهما أسهل، فإن زاحمه الناس في الرمل وقف، فإذا وجد مسلكاً رمل لأنه لا بدل له فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون بخلاف استلام الحجر لأن الاستقبال بدل له. وفي الولوالجية : ولو رمل في الكل لم يلزمه شيء ا.هـ. وينبغي أن يكره تنزيهاً لمخالفة السنة. والرمل كما في الهداية أن يهز في مشيته الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، وقيل هو إسراع مع تقارب الخطا دون الوثوب والعدو وهو في اللغة كما في ضياء الحلوم بفتح الفاء والعين الهرولة. وفي فتح القدير : وهو بقرب البيت أفضل فإن لم يقدر فهو في البعد من البيت أفضل من الطواف بلا رمل مع القرب منه .
His statement: 'Perform raml in the first three only.' Explanation of the sunnah, i.e. in the first three circuits and not others. So it indicates that it is from the Black Stone to the Black Stone, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas during the Farewell Pilgrimage narrated in the two Sahihs, in response to those who said it ends at the Yemeni corner. Know that the principle is that the ruling ceases when the cause ceases, because the ruling is concomitant with the existence of the cause, and the existence of the concomitant without the necessary is impossible. The statement of those who said that the cause of raml in tawaf has ceased and the ruling remains is rejected, for the Prophet performed raml during the Farewell Pilgrimage as a reminder of the blessing of security after fear, to be grateful, for Allah commanded remembrance of His blessings in places of His Book. He only commanded us to remember them so that we may be grateful. It is permissible that the ruling is established by alternating causes: when the polytheists were dominant, the cause of raml was to make the polytheists perceive the Muslims as strong; when that ceases, its cause becomes the reminder of the blessing of security. Similarly, the cause of slavery originally was the disbeliever's disdain for worshipping his Lord, then its cause became the legal ruling of enslaving him even if he becomes Muslim. And like kharaj, which is initially established as a penalty, therefore it is not initially imposed on a Muslim, then its cause becomes the legal ruling, so that if a Muslim buys kharaj land, kharaj is incumbent upon him. Thus mentioned by al-Muhaqqiq al-Aswad, the seventh: tawaf behind al-Hatim. End. His commentator said: As for the purity of the place of tawaf, Ibn Jama'ah mentioned from the author of al-Ghayat that if there is impurity in the place of his tawaf, it does not invalidate his tawaf. This indicates negation of condition and obligation, and possibility of confirming obligation and sunnah, but the most likely (according to the Shafi'is) is that it is not obligatory. End. I say: an eighth is added, which is that it is seven circuits. His statement: 'What is known in tawaf is only the remembrance of Allah' indicates that it is better than recitation, as in al-Fath from al-Tajnis. He said: We do not know any report that recitation of Quran in tawaf is transmitted from Akmal al-Din in his commentary on al-Bazdawi from the discussion of capacity. Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam rejected in the chapter of 'ushr and kharaj the notion that the ruling is necessarily tied to the existence of the cause in legal causes, because legal causes are indicators of the ruling, not effectors; so it is permissible for the ruling to remain after the cause ceases. That is only in rational causes. His statement: 'there is no raml except in tawaf followed by sa'y' indicates that if one intends to delay sa'y to the tawaf of visitation, he does not perform raml in the tawaf of arrival. The commentator mentioned, attributing to al-Ghayat, that if one is a qarin (performing Hajj and Umrah together) and he should not perform raml in the tawaf of arrival if he performed raml in the tawaf of Umrah. His statement 'only' indicates that if one misses raml in the first circuit, he only performs raml in the two circuits after, and if he forgets the first three, he does not perform raml in the remaining, because refraining from raml in the four is sunnah. If he were to perform raml in them, he would be abandoning two sunnats, and abandoning one of them is easier. If people crowd him during raml, he stops, and when he finds a path, he performs raml because it has no substitute; so he stops until he performs it in the prescribed manner, unlike touching the Black Stone because facing it is a substitute. In al-Walwalijiyya: if one performs raml in all circuits, nothing is incumbent upon him. It should be considered slightly disliked (makruh tanzihan) due to contravening the sunnah. Raml, as in al-Hidayah, is to shake the shoulders in one's walk like a dueler strutting between two rows. It is also said it is speeding with short steps without hopping or running. In Arabic, as in Diya' al-Hulum, with fat-ha on the fa' and 'ayn, it means harwalah (brisk walking). In Fath al-Qadir: performing raml near the House is better; if unable, then performing tawaf with raml from a distance is better than tawaf without raml near the House.
Source pages p. 577

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq provides an extensive discussion of raml (brisk walking) in tawaf. The author explains that raml is a sunnah in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), from the Black Stone to the Black Stone, based on the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. There is a principle in usul al-fiqh that a ruling should cease when its cause ceases, but the commentator defends the continuation of raml by pointing out that the cause may shift: originally raml was to demonstrate strength to the polytheists, but after Mecca's conquest, the cause became gratitude for security. This is supported by analogies with slavery and kharaj. The passage then shifts to a discussion of purity of place in tawaf, contrasting the Hanafi position (not a condition) with the Shafi'i view (most likely not obligatory). The author also clarifies that raml is only performed in tawaf followed by sa'y, and if missed early, it is not made up later. Practical details include: if crowded, one stops and resumes when possible; raml is defined as shaking the shoulders or brisk short steps; and performing raml nearer the House is better, but if crowded, performing it from a distance is better than omitting it entirely. The discussion concludes with a reminder that raml is sunnah mu'akkada, and doing it in all circuits is makruh tanzihan.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-raml): Brisk walking with short steps, shaking the shoulders, performed in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum. Synonym: harwalah.
العلة (al-illah): The legal cause that provides the rationale for a ruling; here the cause of raml shifted from demonstrating strength to gratitude.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what should a pilgrim do if he accidentally performed raml in all seven circuits of tawaf al-qudum?
A) He must repeat the tawaf.
B) Nothing is incumbent upon him, but it is slightly disliked.
C) He must perform sajda al-sahw.
D) He should repeat the first three circuits with raml.

Key Takeaway
Raml in tawaf remains a confirmed sunnah even after its original cause changes, because Hanafi usul treats legal causes as indicators, and the ruling can persist through a new cause.

Ruling on Istilam (Touching the Black Stone) During Tawaf
Provides ruling and proof for istilam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istilam and identify its proof from the Hadith of Bukhari.

Core Idea
Istilam is a sunnah act of wiping or pointing; its method is derived from the Prophet's tawaf on a camel.

When performing tawaf, every pilgrim passes by the Black Stone. What should one do? The text provides a clear ruling based on the Prophet's action, balancing ease and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that 'istilam' refers to touching the Black Stone. The ruling is that it is sunnah, not wajib.
The text says 'istalama' as an instruction, but it is not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Bukhari where the Prophet performed tawaf on a camel and pointed to the Stone with something in his hand, saying Allahu Akbar.
This indicates that pointing suffices when one cannot reach.
3
Understand the method
Istilam can be done by hand, by kissing, or by pointing (with hand or a stick) if unable to reach.
The linguistic root 'salama' means to wipe.
4
Note the condition
The phrase 'in istata'ta' (if you are able) implies that one should not cause harm to others. That is, avoid pushing or harming other pilgrims.
Harm (idha') is prohibited even while performing a sunnah.
5
Apply when unable
If it is too crowded, simply pointing with the hand or a stick while saying takbir is sufficient to fulfill the sunnah.
This follows the Prophet's example on the camel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واستلم الحجر كما مررت به إن استطعت أي من غير إيذاء لحديث البخاري أنه عليه السلام طاف على بعير كما أتى إلى الركن أشار بشيء في يده وكبر . وفي المغرب : استلم الحجر تناوله بيده أو بالقبلة أو بالكف من السلمة بفتح السين وكسر اللام وهي مسحه الطواف. أقول: ورأيت في السراج الوهاج أنه يستحب أن يقرأ في أيام الموسم ختمة في الطواف . وفي شرح اللباب : قد يقال إنه قرأ آية ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٠١] الآية. بين الركنين مشيراً إلى جوازه ومشعراً بأنه عدل عن القراءة دفعاً للحرج عن الأمة لئلا يتوهموا أن القراءة في الطواف شرط أو واجب كما في الصلاة، وأما ما قيل من أن قراءة آية «ربنا» إنما كانت على قصد الدعاء دون القراءة فهو مع عدم الاطلاع على الإرادة بعيد بحسب العادة
His statement: 'And touch the Black Stone as you pass by if you are able' i.e., without causing harm, based on the hadith of Bukhari that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tawaf on a camel, when he approached the corner he pointed with something in his hand and said 'Allahu Akbar.' In al-Mughrib: 'Istilam of the Stone' means taking it with the hand or by kissing or with the palm. From salama (with fatha on seen and kasra on lam) meaning wiping it. 'Tawaf'. I say: I saw in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that it is recommended to read a complete recitation of the Quran during the days of the season. And in Sharh al-Lubab: It may be said that he recited the verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah' [2:201] between the two corners, indicating its permissibility and suggesting that he turned away from recitation to avoid hardship for the ummah, lest they think that recitation in tawaf is a condition or obligation as in prayer. As for what is said that the recitation of the verse 'Rabbana' was intended as supplication rather than recitation, it is, without knowledge of the intention, far-fetched according to custom.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage covers two separate but related topics: istilam (touching the Black Stone) and recitation during tawaf. For istilam, the author explains that it is performed with the hand, by kissing, or with the palm, and if one is unable, he may use a stick or simply point, as the Prophet did from his camel. The evidence is a hadith from Bukhari. The second part discusses recitation of Quran during tawaf. While the author in a previous lesson stated that 'what is known in tawaf is only remembrance of Allah', here he notes that it is recommended to recite a complete Quran recitation during the days of the Hajj season. He also references Sharh al-Lubab, which mentions that the Prophet recited the verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah' (Our Lord, give us good in this world) between the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone. This was done to avoid causing hardship for the ummah, who might mistakenly believe that reciting Quran during tawaf is obligatory like in prayer. Some claimed the Prophet's recitation was actually supplication, but the author considers this far-fetched without proof. Thus, reciting Quran during tawaf is permissible and recommended, but one should not neglect dhikr, which is considered better.

Key Terms
استلم (istalama): To touch the Black Stone with the hand or by kissing, or to point to it if unable.
السلمة (al-salamah): The act of wiping; here used in the linguistic definition of istilam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the evidence for the method of istilam (touching the Black Stone) described?
A) A hadith from Ibn Majah
B) A hadith from Bukhari showing the Prophet pointed with something in his hand
C) A hadith from Muslim about kissing the stone
D) Consensus of the Companions

Key Takeaway
Istilam is a sunnah act that can be performed by pointing when unable, following the Prophet's example in Bukhari.

Ruling on Reciting the Quran During Tawaf
Provides ruling and proof for recitation during tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on reciting Quran during tawaf and distinguish it from obligatory recitation in prayer.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran during tawaf is permissible and recommended, but dhikr is better; it is not obligatory like in prayer.

Pilgrims often wonder if they can recite Quran while performing tawaf. The text clarifies that it is allowed, even recommended, but one should not neglect the established dhikr. The Prophet's own practice provides evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting Quran during tawaf. The ruling from the text is that it is recommended (mustahabb) but not obligatory; dhikr is actually better.
The author cites a source recommending a complete recitation during the season.
2
Examine the proof
Sharh al-Lubab mentions that the Prophet recited the verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah' (2:201) between the two corners of the Kaaba during tawaf.
This indicates the permissibility of recitation.
3
Understand the reason
The Prophet turned away from recitation (i.e., he did not make it continuous) to avoid causing hardship for the ummah, lest they think recitation is a condition or obligation like in prayer.
The aim is to prevent misunderstanding about the nature of tawaf.
4
Refute the alternative claim
Some claimed that the Prophet's recitation was actually supplication (dua), not Quran recitation. The author considers this far-fetched (ba'id) according to custom, lacking evidence.
Thus, the stronger view is that it was Quran recitation, supporting permissibility.
5
Derive the final ruling
Reciting Quran during tawaf is permissible and recommended (mustahabb), but one should prioritise dhikr and dua, which are the established acts of worship in tawaf.
The mufta bihi is that recitation is allowed, but dhikr is superior.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (واستلم الحجر كما مررت به إن استطعت أي من غير إيذاء لحديث البخاري أنه عليه السلام طاف على بعير كما أتى إلى الركن أشار بشيء في يده وكبر . وفي المغرب : استلم الحجر تناوله بيده أو بالقبلة أو بالكف من السلمة بفتح السين وكسر اللام وهي مسحه الطواف. أقول: ورأيت في السراج الوهاج أنه يستحب أن يقرأ في أيام الموسم ختمة في الطواف . وفي شرح اللباب : قد يقال إنه قرأ آية ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة ﴾ [البقرة: ٢٠١] الآية. بين الركنين مشيراً إلى جوازه ومشعراً بأنه عدل عن القراءة دفعاً للحرج عن الأمة لئلا يتوهموا أن القراءة في الطواف شرط أو واجب كما في الصلاة، وأما ما قيل من أن قراءة آية «ربنا» إنما كانت على قصد الدعاء دون القراءة فهو مع عدم الاطلاع على الإرادة بعيد بحسب العادة
His statement: 'And touch the Black Stone as you pass by if you are able' i.e., without causing harm, based on the hadith of Bukhari that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed tawaf on a camel, when he approached the corner he pointed with something in his hand and said 'Allahu Akbar.' In al-Mughrib: 'Istilam of the Stone' means taking it with the hand or by kissing or with the palm. From salama (with fatha on seen and kasra on lam) meaning wiping it. 'Tawaf'. I say: I saw in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that it is recommended to read a complete recitation of the Quran during the days of the season. And in Sharh al-Lubab: It may be said that he recited the verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah' [2:201] between the two corners, indicating its permissibility and suggesting that he turned away from recitation to avoid hardship for the ummah, lest they think that recitation in tawaf is a condition or obligation as in prayer. As for what is said that the recitation of the verse 'Rabbana' was intended as supplication rather than recitation, it is, without knowledge of the intention, far-fetched according to custom.

Commentary
This passage covers two separate but related topics: istilam (touching the Black Stone) and recitation during tawaf. For istilam, the author explains that it is performed with the hand, by kissing, or with the palm, and if one is unable, he may use a stick or simply point, as the Prophet did from his camel. The evidence is a hadith from Bukhari. The second part discusses recitation of Quran during tawaf. Raml During Tawaf: Continuity vs. Crowding
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether to stop for raml mid-tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on whether to stop for raml during tawaf when crowded, prioritizing muwalat over raml.

Core Idea
If crowded mid-tawaf, do what raml you can; do not break continuity for a disputed sunnah.

The pilgrim performing tawaf with raml may face heavy crowds. Should he stop and wait to perform raml properly, or continue and do as much as possible? This lesson examines the Hanafi position, which prioritizes the established sunnah of continuity (muwalat) over the debated sunnah of raml when they conflict.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing raml during tawaf. The ruling concerns whether to stop in the middle if unable to perform raml due to crowding.
Raml is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for men.
2
Locate the dalil and basis
The primary basis is the sunnah of muwalat (continuity) between circuits and parts of tawaf, which is agreed upon among scholars, with some even deeming it wajib.
The text cites no explicit hadith but relies on ijma' and the principle of avoiding hardship.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The proof is that muwalat is a stronger sunnah (or wajib) compared to raml, which is a sunnah disputed by some. When two sunnahs conflict, the stronger takes precedence.
The 'wajh' is the argument from priority and avoidance of hardship (haraj).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Mansak al-Kabir allowed stopping in the middle to perform raml properly. Mulla Ali opposed this, arguing it breaks muwalat and causes hardship.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference; both views are from later scholars.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Mulla Ali's view is preferred because it avoids hardship and upholds the stronger sunnah. The text states: 'do what you can and leave what you cannot.'
The mufta bihi position: do not stop in the middle; perform raml to the extent possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن زاحمه الناس في الرمل وقف الخ) كذا عبر في المنسك الكبير للسندي : قال منلا علي في شرح اللباب : أنه يقف في الأثناء وهو مستبعد جداً عرفاً وعادة لما فيه من الحرج والمشقة، ولكون الموالاة بين الأشواط وأجزاء الطواف سنة متفق عليها بل قال بعض العلماء: إنها واجبة فلا تترك لحصول سنة مختلف فيها، فلو حصل التزاحم في الأثناء يفعل ما يقدر عليه من الرمل ويترك ما لا يقدر عليه ا هـ . وحاصله أنه إنما يقف للرمل إذا حصلت الزحمة قبل الشروع في الطواف لأن المبادرة إليه مستحبة وهي لا تدافع الرمل الذي هو سنة مؤكدة، أما إذا حصلت في الأثناء فلا يقف لئلا تفوت الموالاة قوله : (فإن لم يقدر الخ) أي لو كان في القرب من البيت زحمة تمنعه من الرمل فالطواف وهو يوهم
His statement: 'If people crowd him in raml, he stops, etc.' Thus expressed in al-Mansak al-Kabir of al-Sindi: Mulla Ali said in Sharh al-Lubab: he stops in the middle, but this is far-fetched customarily and habitually because of the hardship and difficulty, and because continuity (muwalat) between circuits and parts of tawaf is an agreed-upon sunnah; rather, some scholars say it is wajib, so it is not abandoned for the sake of a sunnah that is disputed. So if crowding occurs in the middle, he does what he can of raml and leaves what he cannot. End. The summary: he only stops for raml if crowding occurs before starting tawaf, because rushing to it is recommended and does not contradict raml which is a confirmed sunnah. But if it occurs during, he does not stop, so as not to lose continuity. His statement: 'if he is unable, etc.' i.e., if there is a crowd near the House preventing him from raml, then tawaf... and it gives the impression.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage addresses a practical issue: if a pilgrim is performing raml (brisk walking) during tawaf and encounters crowding, should he stop and wait to perform raml properly? The text presents two views. According to al-Mansak al-Kabir, one should stop if possible, but Mulla Ali in Sharh al-Lubab finds this impractical because of hardship and because continuity (muwalat) between circuits is an established sunnah, and some scholars even consider it wajib. Therefore, the preferred view is that if crowding occurs before starting tawaf, one may delay until there is space to perform raml properly. However, if one is already in the middle of tawaf, he should not stop, but rather do as much raml as possible and continue, because breaking the continuity would be worse than missing the raml in that circuit. This reflects the Hanafi principle that when two sunnahs conflict, the one with stronger basis (muwalat) takes precedence, especially when the other (raml) is disputed by some scholars. The passage ends with a note that if one is unable to perform raml due to crowding, the tawaf is still valid, though the exact implication is not fully stated.

Key Terms
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Continuity between the circuits of tawaf and between its parts, considered a sunnah or even wajib by some Hanafi scholars.
الزحام (al-ziham): Crowding of people during tawaf, which may prevent proper performance of raml.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in this passage, what should a pilgrim do if he encounters crowding while performing raml in the middle of tawaf?
A) Stop and wait until there is space to perform raml properly.
B) Continue the tawaf without raml, then repeat the circuit later.
C) Perform as much raml as possible and continue, without stopping.
D) Abandon the tawaf and restart later.

Key Takeaway
When raml is impossible mid-tawaf due to crowding, perform what you can and continue; do not break muwalat.

Raml in Tawaf: Definition, Ruling, and Practical Issues
Explains the sunnah of raml, its definition, when performed, and how to handle crowding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of raml, identify when it is required, and explain how to perform it under crowded conditions.

Core Idea
Raml is a sunnah in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum; if missed, it has no substitute.

In this lesson, we examine the sunnah of raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) during tawaf. The Hanafi school specifies that raml is only performed in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when sa'y follows immediately. We will also discuss what to do if crowded and the ruling if one forgets or does raml in all circuits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when followed by sa'y.
2
Determine the conditions for raml
It is only in tawaf al-qudum followed by sa'y; for a qarin, it is not repeated if already done in Umrah.
3
Handle missing or forgetting raml
If the first circuit is missed, raml in the next two; if all first three are missed, no makeup in the remaining four.
Because not ramling in the last four is a separate sunnah.
4
Apply the ruling when crowded
Stop and resume when possible; raml has no substitute unlike istilam of the Black Stone.
5
Define raml
From al-Hidayah: quick walking with shoulder movement, like a warrior, without jumping.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بقوله بعد ذلك ثم أخرج إلى الصفا» إلى أنه لا يرمل إلا في طواف بعده سعي، فلو أراد تأخير السعي إلى طواف الزيارة لا يرمل في طواف القدوم، وذكر الشارح معزياً إلى الغاية إذا كان قارناً لم يرمل في طواف القدوم إن كان رمل في طواف العمرة. وأشار بقوله «فقط» إلى أنه لو ترك الرمل في الشوط الأول لا يرمل إلا في الشوطين بعده وبنسيانه في الثلاثة الأول لا يرمل في الباقي لأن ترك الرمل في الأربعة سنة ، فلو رمل فيها لكان تاركاً للسنتين وكان ترك أحدهما أسهل، فإن زاحمه الناس في الرمل وقف، فإذا وجد مسلكاً رمل لأنه لا بدل له فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون بخلاف استلام الحجر لأن الاستقبال بدل له. وفي الولوالجية : ولو رمل في الكل لم يلزمه شيء ا.هـ. وينبغي أن يكره تنزيهاً لمخالفة السنة. والرمل كما في الهداية أن يهز في مشيته الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفين، وقيل هو إسراع مع تقارب الخطا دون الوثوب والعدو وهو في اللغة كما في ضياء الحلوم بفتح الفاء والعين الهرولة. وفي فتح القدير : وهو بقرب البيت أفضل فإن لم يقدر فهو في البعد من البيت أفضل من الطواف بلا رمل مع القرب منه.
And he indicated by his statement 'then he exits to al-Safa' that one only raml in a tawaf followed by sa'y. If he intends to delay the sa'y to the tawaf of ziyarah, he does not raml in the tawaf of qudum. The commentator mentioned, attributing to al-Ghayah, that if one is a qarin, he does not raml in tawaf al-qudum if he had already ramled in the tawaf of umrah. And he indicated by his statement 'only' that if he leaves the raml in the first circuit, he only ramls in the two following circuits; and if he forgets it in the first three, he does not raml in the rest because leaving raml in the four is sunnah. If he ramled in them, he would be leaving two sunnahs, and leaving one of them is easier. If the crowd presses him during raml, he stops; when he finds a path, he ramls because it has no substitute, so he stops until he completes it in the prescribed manner, unlike istilam of the Black Stone because facing it is a substitute for it. In al-Walwaljiyyah: if he ramled in all circuits, nothing is required of him. End. And it should be considered makruh tanzihan for opposing the sunnah. Raml, as in al-Hidayah, is that one moves his shoulders in his walking like a warrior striding between two rows. It is also said that it is speed with short steps without jumping or running. In language, as in Diya' al-Hulum, it is hurried walking. In Fath al-Qadir: it is better near the House; if unable, then raml at a distance from the House is better than tawaf without raml when close to it.
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the rulings of raml (quick walking with shoulder movement) in tawaf. The author clarifies that raml is performed only in a tawaf that is immediately followed by sa'y, specifically tawaf al-qudum. If one postpones sa'y until after tawaf al-ziyarah, then raml is not performed in tawaf al-qudum. For a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together), if he already did raml in the tawaf of Umrah, he does not repeat it in tawaf al-qudum. The ruling 'only' indicates that if the first circuit is missed, raml is only done in the subsequent two (i.e., the remaining circuits of the first three). Forgetting raml in the first three circuits means it is not made up in the last four, because not ramling in the last four is a sunnah in itself. Raml in all circuits would mean leaving two sunnahs (raml in the first three and not ramling in the last four), so it is better to leave one. If one is unable to raml due to crowding, he stops until there is space; unlike istilam, where one can gesture from a distance, raml has no substitute. According to al-Walwaljiyyah, if one does raml in all circuits, there is no sin but it is makruh tanzihan. The definition of raml is given from al-Hidayah: moving shoulders like a warrior, quick steps without leaping. Proximity to the Kaaba makes raml better, but if unable, ramling at a distance is superior to doing tawaf without raml near the Kaaba.

Key Terms
الرمل (al-raml): Quick walking with shoulder movement and short steps, like a warrior striding, without jumping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which circuits of tawaf is raml prescribed according to the Hanafi school?
A) All seven circuits
B) The first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when followed by sa'y
C) Only the first circuit
D) The last four circuits

Key Takeaway
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when followed by sa'y; if crowding prevents it, one stops and resumes when able.

Kissing the Yemeni Corner: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Relied-Upon Position
Intra-Hanafi dispute on kissing the Yemeni corner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi relied-upon position on touching vs kissing the Yemeni corner, identify the proofs for each side, and apply the tarjih mechanism.

Core Idea
Kissing the Yemeni corner is not sunnah in the Hanafi school; touching suffices, and the relied-upon position rejects gesturing.

The Black Stone is kissed, but the Yemeni corner? This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether kissing the Yemeni corner is sunnah. We'll examine the textual proofs and see how later Hanafi authorities settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The core question: when touching the Yemeni corner during tawaf, is it sunnah to also kiss it, or is merely touching sufficient?
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (zahir al-riwaya) hold that kissing the Yemeni corner is not sunnah; touching is enough. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that kissing is sunnah and if unable, one should gesture.
3
Examine the textual proofs
The majority relies on the authentic hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari, Muslim): 'I did not see the Prophet touch any corner except the two Yemeni ones' – indicating only touching. Muhammad relies on the less authentic hadith of Ibn Abbas (al-Daraqutni) that the Prophet kissed the Yemeni corner.
The hadith of Ibn Umar is considered stronger in transmission (ahad but sahih).
4
Apply the tarjih mechanism
Later Hanafi authorities (al-Kirmani, al-Nukhbah, al-Bada'i') declared Muhammad's narration weak. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is to touch the Yemeni corner without kissing, and if unable, one does not gesture.
The ruling is based on the preponderance of evidence (tarjih bi al-dalil).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واستلم الحجر كما مررت به إن استطعت أي من غير إيذاء لحديث البخاري أنه عليه السلام طاف على بعير كما أتى إلى الركن أشار بشيء في يده وكبر . وفي المغرب : استلم الحجر تناوله بيده أو بالقبلة أو بالكف من السلمة بفتح السين وكسر اللام وهي مسحه. قوله : (فإن زاحمه الناس في الرمل وقف الخ) كذا عبر في المنسك الكبير للسندي : قال منلا علي في شرح اللباب : أنه يقف في الأثناء وهو مستبعد جداً عرفاً وعادة لما فيه من الحرج والمشقة، ولكون الموالاة بين الأشواط وأجزاء الطواف سنة متفق عليها بل قال بعض العلماء: إنها واجبة فلا تترك لحصول سنة مختلف فيها، فلو حصل التزاحم في الأثناء يفعل ما يقدر عليه من الرمل ويترك ما لا يقدر عليه ا هـ. وحاصله أنه إنما يقف للرمل إذا حصلت الزحمة قبل الشروع في الطواف لأن المبادرة إليه مستحبة وهي لا تدافع الرمل الذي هو سنة مؤكدة، أما إذا حصلت في الأثناء فلا يقف لئلا تفوت الموالاة . قوله : (فإن لم يقدر الخ) أي لو كان في القرب من البيت زحمة تمنعه من الرمل فالطواف في البعد من البيت مع الرمل أفضل. قوله : (إن الاستلام في الابتداء والانتهاء سنة) سقط لفظ والانتهاء من بعض النسخ والصواب إثباته لأنه موجود في الولوالجية وليلائم قوله «وفيما بين ذلك». هذا وفي شرح اللباب : ولا تنافي بين الأقوال فإن استلام طرفيه أكد مما بينهما ولعل السبب أنه يتفرع على الاستلام فيما بينهما نوع من ترك الموالاة بخلاف طرفيها. ثم هل يرفع اليدين في كل تكبير يستقبل به في مبدأ كل شوط أو يختص بالأول، فمال ابن الهمام إلى أن الثاني هو المعول، وظاهر كلام الكرماني والطحاوي وبعض الأحاديث يؤيد الثاني فينبغي أن يرفعهما مرة ويتركهما أخرى فإن الجمع في موضع الخلاف مهما أمكن أحرى . قوله : ( والدلائل تشهد له) قيد بالدلائل لأنه من حيث المذهب ظاهر الرواية هو الأول كما في الهداية والكافي وغيرهما. قال الكرماني: وهو الصحيح. وقال في النخبة : ما عن محمد ضعيف جداً. وفي البدائع لا خلاف في أن تقبيله ليس بسنة. وفي السراجية ولا يقبله في أصح الأقاويل والحاصل أن الأصح هو الاكتفاء بالاستلام، والجمهور على عدم التقبيل والإتفاق على ترك السجود فإذا عجز عن استلامه فلا يشير إليه إلا رواية عن محمد. كذا في شرح اللباب . قوله (وإن الأصل في النسبة إلى اليمن والشام الخ الأصوب الاقتصار على اليمن لإيهامه أن
And touch the Black Stone as you pass by it if you are able, i.e., without causing harm, based on the hadith of Bukhari that he (peace be upon him) performed tawaf on a camel; when he came to the corner, he gestured with something in his hand and said 'Allahu Akbar'. In al-Mughrib: istilam of the Black Stone is to take it with the hand or with a kiss or with the palm, from 'silmah' with fat-h on the sin and kasr on the lam, meaning wiping. His statement: (If the crowd presses him in raml, he stops, etc.) This is how it is expressed in al-Mansak al-Kabir of al-Sindi: Mulla Ali in Sharh al-Lubab said that he stops in the middle, but this is very far from common practice due to hardship and difficulty, and because continuity (muwalat) between circuits and parts of tawaf is agreed upon as sunnah; indeed some scholars said it is obligatory, so it should not be left for the sake of a sunnah that is disputed. If crowding occurs in the middle, he does what he can of raml and leaves what he cannot. End. The summary: he only stops for raml if the crowding occurs before starting tawaf, because starting tawaf is recommended and does not conflict with raml which is a confirmed sunnah. But if it occurs during, he does not stop lest continuity be lost. His statement: (If he is unable, etc.) meaning if there is crowding near the House preventing raml, then tawaf at a distance with raml is better. His statement: (Istilam at the beginning and end is sunnah) - the word 'and the end' is missing from some copies, but the correct version includes it because it is in al-Walwaljiyyah and to be consistent with his statement 'and between that'. This, and in Sharh al-Lubab: there is no contradiction between the statements; indeed istilam at the two ends is more emphasized than between them, perhaps because istilam between them leads to a kind of break in continuity unlike the ends. Then, does one raise the hands in every takbir at the start of each circuit or specifically the first? Ibn al-Humam inclined to the second being the relied-upon view. The apparent meaning of al-Kirmani, al-Tahawi, and some hadith supports the second. So one should raise them once and leave them another time, because combining in a point of disagreement whenever possible is more appropriate. His statement: (And the proofs witness for him) - he qualified with 'proofs' because from the perspective of the madhhab, the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) is the first, as in al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, and others. Al-Kirmani said it is correct. In al-Nukhbah: what is from Muhammad is very weak. In al-Bada'i': there is no dispute that kissing it is not sunnah. In al-Sirajiyyah: he does not kiss it in the most correct views. The conclusion: the most correct is to suffice with istilam, and the majority are against kissing, and there is agreement on leaving prostration. So if one is unable to do istilam, he does not gesture towards it except in a narration from Muhammad. This is in Sharh al-Lubab. His statement: (And the original in attribution to Yemen and Syria, etc.) The more correct is to confine to Yemen because of the implication that...
Source pages p. 578

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings in tawaf. First, istilam (touching) of the Black Stone is a confirmed sunnah; if unable, pointing with the hand suffices. The commentary then returns to the issue of stopping for raml when crowded: the relied-upon view is that one should not stop in the middle of tawaf but should do as much as possible, because maintaining continuity (muwalat) is more important. Next, istilam at the beginning and end of tawaf is more emphasized than between circuits. A subsidiary issue is raising the hands in takbir at the start of each circuit: the most reliable position is to raise them only at the first circuit, but to combine occasionally is better. The main dispute concerns kissing the Yemeni corner: according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the zahir al-riwaya), it is not sunnah to kiss it; Muhammad al-Shaybani considered it sunnah and even gestured when unable. The relied-upon position is the former, based on strong hadith from Ibn Umar. Thus, the Hanafi practice is to touch the Yemeni corner without kissing, and if unable, one does not gesture.

Key Terms
الاستلام (al-istilam): Touching the Black Stone or the Yemeni corner with the hand or palm, sometimes with a kiss, as a sunnah during tawaf.
الركن اليماني (al-rukn al-yamani): The corner of the Kaaba facing Yemen, located before the Black Stone. It is touched but not kissed according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is haram to touch it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi relied-upon position distinguishes between the Black Stone (kissed) and the Yemeni corner (touched only), with the majority rejecting kissing and gesturing.

Kissing the Yemeni Corner During Tawaf: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on istilam with intra-Hanafi dispute on kissing the Yemeni Corner

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on kissing the Yemeni Corner, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Kissing the Yemeni Corner is not sunnah in the Hanafi school despite evidence for it.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced internal disagreement within the Hanafi school regarding the Yemeni Corner of the Kaaba. While the Black Stone is clearly kissed during tawaf, the status of the Yemeni Corner is disputed between Imam Abu Hanifa and his student Imam Muhammad. We will explore the proofs each side relies on and understand why the school ultimately follows Abu Hanifa's view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on touching the Yemeni Corner
According to Abu Hanifa, touching the Yemeni Corner is mustahabb but kissing it is not sunnah. This is the relied-upon position.
Touching includes istilam with the hand.
2
Identify Imam Muhammad's alternative view
Imam Muhammad considered touching and kissing the Yemeni Corner to be sunnah, analogous to the Black Stone.
This creates an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the proofs from both sides
Muhammad cites hadiths showing the Prophet kissing the Yemeni Corner and his constant practice. Abu Hanifa relies on the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet only touched the two Yemeni corners without specifying kissing, and the fact that the Yemeni Corner is not a foundational corner.
The hadiths are all ahad; the Hanafi method weighs constant practice (muwazabah) and the strength of transmission.
4
Apply Hanafi usul principles for tarjih
The school prefers Abu Hanifa's view because the evidence for kissing is not as strong, and the Yemeni Corner is not a rukn of the Kaaba like the Black Stone (part of the Hatim is from the original building, making the Yemeni Corner a middle point).
Analogy (qiyas) to the Black Stone is rejected due to a difference in illah.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that kissing the Yemeni Corner is not sunnah. A Hanafi pilgrim should touch it without kissing.
This ruling is found in al-Hidayah and other major works.

Source Text

كلما مررت به إن استطعت واختم الطواف به وبركعتين في المقام أو حيث تيسر من الحجر، أفاد أن استلام الحجر بين كل شوطين سنة كما صرح به في غاية البيان. وذكر في المحيط والولوالجي في فتاواه أن الاستلام في الابتداء والانتهاء سنة وفيما بين ذلك أدب. ولم يذكر المصنف استلام غير الحجر لأنه لا يستلم الركن العراقي والشامي، وأما اليماني فيستحب أن يستلمه ولا يقبله وعند محمد هو سنة وتقبيله مثل الحجر الأسود والدلائل تشهد له فإن ابن عمر قال : لم أر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يمس من الأركان إلا اليمانيين كما في الصحيحين. وعن ابن عباس أنه عليه السلام كان يقبل الركن اليماني ويضع يده عليه. روان الدارقطني. وعنه عليه السلام إذا استلم الركن اليماني قبله رواه البخاري في تاريخه. وعن أنه قال : ما تركت استلام هذين الركنين الركن اليماني والحجر الأسود منذ رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يستلمهما . رواه مسلم وأبو داود. وقد علمت أن استلام الحجر والركن اليماني يعم التقبيل فقد دل على سنية استلامه وأظهر منه ما رواه أحمد وأبو داود عن ابن أنه عليه السلام لا يدع أن يستلم الحجر والركن اليماني في كل طوافه، فإنه صريح في المواظبة الدالة على السنية. واعلم أنه قد صرح في غاية البيان أنه لا يجوز استلام غير الركنين وهو تساهل فإنه ليس فيه ما يدل على التحريم وإنما هو مكروه كراهة التنزيه. والحكمة في عدم استلامهما أنهما ليسا من أركان البيت حقيقة لأن بعض الحطيم من البيت فيكون الركنان إذن وسط البيت وأن الأصل في النسبة إلى اليمن والشام يمني وشامي ثم حذفوا إحدى يائي النسبة وعوضوا منها ألفاً فقالوا اليماني والشامي بالتخفيف وبعضهم يشدده كما في الصحاح. قوله: (وإن الأصل في النسبة إلى اليمن والشام الخ الأصوب الاقتصار على اليمن لإيهامه أن يائي النسبة وعوضوا منها ألفاً فقالوا اليماني والشامي بالتخفيف وبعضهم يشدده كما في الصحاح). قال في الصحاح : الشأم بلاد تذكر وتؤنث ورجل شأمي وشآمي على فعال، وشأمي أيضاً حكاه سيبويه ولا تقل شأم. وقال أيضاً: اليمن بلاد للعرب والنسبة إليهم يمني ويمان مخففة والألف عوض من ياء النسب فلا يجتمعان قال سيبويه : وبعضهم يقول يماني بالتشديد ا هـ . فقول المؤلف ثم حذفوا إحدى يائي النسبة يعني من يمني فقط وكذا قوله «بالتخفيف» راجع إلى اليماني.
Whenever you pass by it, if you can, and end the tawaf with it and two rak'ahs at the Maqam or wherever is easy from the mosque, it indicates that touching the stone between every two circuits is sunnah, as stated in Ghayat al-Bayan. In al-Muhit and al-Walwalji's Fatawa, it is mentioned that touching at the beginning and end is sunnah, and what is in between is adab. The author did not mention touching other than the stone because the Iraqi and Syrian corners are not touched. As for the Yemeni corner, it is recommended to touch it but not kiss it, while according to Muhammad it is sunnah and its kissing is like the Black Stone, and proofs support him. Ibn Umar said: I did not see the Prophet touch any of the corners except the two Yemeni ones, as in the Sahihs. From Ibn Abbas: He used to kiss the Yemeni corner and place his hand on it, related by al-Daraqutni. And from him: If he touched the Yemeni corner, he kissed it, narrated by al-Bukhari in his Tarikh. And from him: I have never left touching these two corners, the Yemeni and the Black Stone, since I saw the Messenger of Allah touching them, narrated by Muslim and Abu Dawud. You have learned that touching the stone and the Yemeni corner includes kissing, so it indicates the sunnah nature of touching, and more evident is what Ahmad and Abu Dawud narrated from Ibn that he would not stop touching the stone and the Yemeni corner in every tawaf of his, which is explicit in constant practice indicating sunnah. Know that it has been stated in Ghayat al-Bayan that it is not permissible to touch other than the two corners, but this is lenient; there is nothing indicating prohibition, rather it is makruh tanzihan. The wisdom in not touching them is that they are not actually part of the house's corners because part of the Hatim is from the house, so the two corners become in the middle of the house, and that the original in attribution to Yemen and Syria is Yamani and Shami, then they omitted one of the two ya's of attribution and substituted an alif, saying al-Yamani and al-Shami with lightening, and some emphasize it as in al-Sihah. He said: (And the original in attribution to Yemen and Syria... the proper is to restrict to Yemen because it implies that... ya's of attribution and substituted an alif, saying al-Yamani and al-Shami with lightening, and some emphasize it as in al-Sihah). Al-Sihah said: al-Sham is a land, masculine and feminine, and a man is Shami and Sha'ami on fa'al, and also Shami narrated by Sibawayh, and do not say Sham. It also said: Yemen is a land of Arabs, and attribution to them is Yamani and Yaman, lightened, and the alif is a substitute for the ya of the relative, so they do not combine. Sibawayh said: Some say Yamani with emphasis, end. So the author's 'then they omitted one of the two ya's of attribution' means from Yamani only, and likewise his saying 'with lightening' refers to al-Yamani.
Source pages p. 579

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding tawaf. It deals with the rulings of istilam (touching) the Black Stone and the Yemeni Corner. The author first establishes that istilam of the Black Stone between each two circuits is sunnah, citing Ghayat al-Bayan. He then notes that according to al-Muhit and al-Walwalji, istilam at the beginning and end is sunnah, but in between it is adab (proper conduct). The matn did not mention touching other corners because the Iraqi and Syrian corners are not touched. Regarding the Yemeni Corner, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the preferred view (Abu Hanifa) is that it is recommended (mustahabb) to touch it without kissing, while Imam Muhammad holds that touching and kissing it is sunnah, like the Black Stone. The author provides several hadith proofs supporting Muhammad's view, including actions of the Prophet reported by Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas. However, he notes that according to Ghayat al-Bayan, touching only the two corners is permissible, and touching others is makruh tanzihi, not haram. The wisdom is that the other corners are not true corners of the Kaaba due to the Hatim. The passage also includes a linguistic discussion about the relative adjectives 'Yamani' and 'Shami', explaining the elision of the ya of attribution. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the school is still the view of Abu Hanifa, as stated in al-Hidayah and other works, that kissing the Yemeni Corner is not sunnah.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): Touching the Black Stone or Yemeni Corner with the hand or body as an act of veneration during tawaf.
الركن اليماني (al-rukn al-yamani): The corner of the Kaaba facing Yemen, between the Black Stone and the Syrian corner.
تقبيل (taqbil): Kissing the Black Stone or Yemeni Corner during tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is sunnah, like the Black Stone.
B) It is mustahabb to touch but not sunnah to kiss.
C) It is makruh tanzihi to touch it.
D) It is haram to kiss it.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's relied-upon position is that the Yemeni Corner is touched but not kissed, based on Abu Hanifa's view, despite evidence for kissing.

The Two Rak'ahs After Tawaf: Wajib with Conditions
Ruling with proof on the two rak'ahs after tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the two rak'ahs after tawaf as wajib, explain the proof, and apply the conditions for place, time, and performance.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after every tawaf are wajib, not fard, and are not compensated by a blood offering.

After completing tawaf, what is the ruling on the two rak'ahs? Is it obligatory or just recommended? In this passage from the Radd al-Muhtar, the author clarifies the Hanafi position: it is wajib on the correct view. This lesson unpacks the proof, the flexibility of time and place, and the recommended etiquette.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The passage states that the two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib according to the correct view. Recognize that 'wajib' in Hanafi fiqh is a level above sunnah but below fard, requiring the act but not making the tawaf invalid if omitted.
The ruling applies after any tawaf, whether fard, wajib, sunnah, or nafl.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author alludes to the Quranic verse 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (2:125) and the Prophet's action of reciting it before praying two rak'ahs after tawaf. This is the primary evidence.
The hadith is from Jabir (Muslim), which is ahad, so the dalil is zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) indicates obligation unless there is a contrary indicator. The Prophet recited the verse and then prayed, showing he understood it as a command. Thus, the wajh is that the command is for obligation.
Other schools interpret the command as recommendation due to other contexts.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
The passage says 'on the correct view', implying there is a difference. Shafi'is consider them sunnah mu'akkadah. The practical difference: for Hanafis, omitting them is a sin but no dam; for Shafi'is, omitting them is not sinful but it's a lost reward.
Hanbalis also consider them wajib but compensated by dam, unlike Hanafis.
5
Apply the Conditions and Preferences
The passage details that there is no restriction on time or place—they can be prayed even after returning home. However, it is sunnah to pray immediately after tawaf, and the best place is behind Maqam Ibrahim. Delay is makruh unless in a disliked time.
If performed in a makruh time (e.g., after Asr before Maghrib), it is valid but with karahah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: ( فواجبة على الصحيح) أي بعد كل طواف فرضاً كان أو واجباً أو سنة أو نفلاً، ولا يختص جوازها بزمان ولا بمكان ولا تفوت ولو تركها لم تجبر بدم ولو صلاها خارج الحرم ولو بعد الرجوع إلى وطنه جاز، ويكره والسنة الموالاة بينهما وبين الطواف ويستحب مؤكداً أداؤها خلف المقام ثم في الكعبة ثم في الحجر تحت الميزاب ثم كل ما قرب من الحجر إلى البيت ثم باقي الحجر ثم ما قرب إلى البيت ثم المسجد ثم الحرم ثم لأفضلية بعد الحرم بل الإساءة، والمراد بما خلف المقام قيل ما يصدق عليه ذلك عادة وعرفاً مع القرب، وعن ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه إذا أراد أن يركع خلف المقام جعل بينه وبين المقام صفاً أو صفين أو رجلاً أو رجلين. رواه عبد الرزاق. ولو صلى أكثر من ركعتين جاز، ولا تجزئ المنذورة والمكتوبة عنها، ولا يجوز اقتداء مصلي ركعتي الطواف بمثله لأن طواف هذا غير طواف الآخر، ويكره تأخيرها عن الطواف إلا في وقت مكروه أي لأن الموالاة سنة . ولو طاف بعد العصر يصلي المغرب ثم ركعتي الطواف ثم سنة المغرب ولا تصلي إلا في وقت مباح فإن صلاها في وقت مكروه قيل صحت مع الكراهة .
His saying: (It is wajib according to the correct view) i.e., after every tawaf, whether it is fard, wajib, sunnah, or nafl. Its permissibility is not restricted to any time or place, nor is it lost; if one leaves it, it is not compensated by a dam. If one prays it outside the Sanctuary or even after returning to his homeland, it is permissible. It is makruh, and the sunnah is to perform it in immediate succession to the tawaf. It is strongly recommended to perform it behind the Maqam, then in the Ka'bah, then in the Hatim under the spout, then as close as possible to the House, then the rest of the Hatim, then what is close to the House, then the mosque, then the Haram, then outside the Haram, which is an offense. What is meant by 'behind the Maqam' is, it is said, whatever is customarily considered behind it with proximity. From Ibn Umar: when he wanted to prostrate behind the Maqam, he would place between himself and the Maqam a row or two rows, or a man or two men, related by Abd al-Razzaq. If one prays more than two rak'ahs, it is permissible. A vowed or obligatory prayer does not suffice for it. It is not permissible for one praying the two rak'ahs of tawaf to follow another person praying the same, because this person's tawaf is different from that person's. It is makruh to delay them from the tawaf except in a makruh time, because immediate succession is sunnah. If one performs tawaf after Asr, he prays Maghrib first, then the two rak'ahs of tawaf, then the sunnah of Maghrib, and does not pray them except in a permissible time; if he prays them in a makruh time, it is said it is valid with karahah.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage addresses the two rak'ahs performed after every tawaf. The author clarifies the matn's statement that they are 'wajib according to the correct view'. This means that after any tawaf—whether it is fard (obligatory, like Hajj/Umrah), wajib (necessary), sunnah (voluntary), or nafl (supererogatory)—one must pray two rak'ahs. The ruling is derived from the Quranic verse 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (2:125), which the Prophet complied with after his tawaf. Importantly, these two rak'ahs are not compensated by a dam (animal sacrifice) if omitted; they remain obligatory in the sense that they are a required component of the tawaf, but they are not fard. There is flexibility in time and place: they can be performed at any time of day or night (except at makruh times), and anywhere within the Haram or even outside Makkah, though the reward varies. The best place is behind the Maqam of Ibrahim, then inside the Ka'bah, then in the Hatim, then close to the House, etc. It is makruh to delay them without necessity, as immediate succession (muwalat) is sunnah. If one prays more than two rak'ahs, it is permissible, but the two rak'ahs are the minimum. Neither a vowed (nadhr) prayer nor an obligatory prayer (like fard) can substitute for them. Imitating the prayer by following another person performing the same two rak'ahs is not allowed because each person's tawaf is separate. If tawaf is performed after Asr, one should wait for Maghrib time to pray the two rak'ahs, but if prayed in a disliked time, it is valid with karahah.

Key Terms
ركعتا الطواف (rak'ata al-tawaf): Two units of prayer performed after completing a tawaf, wajib according to the correct Hanafi view.
المقام (al-maqam): The Station of Ibrahim, a stone near the Ka'bah where Ibrahim stood; preferred place to pray the two rak'ahs.
الموالاة (muwalat): Immediate succession or continuity; here, performing the two rak'ahs directly after tawaf without undue delay.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the two rak'ahs after tawaf?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mandub

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib, best performed behind Maqam Ibrahim immediately after tawaf, and if omitted, no dam is required but one is sinful and must pray later.

Forgetting Tawaf Prayer and Starting Another Tawaf
Ruling on forgetting tawaf prayer and starting another tawaf, and obligation of separate prayer for each tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who forgets the two rak'ahs of tawaf and remembers after starting another tawaf, and apply the distinction based on circuit completion.

Core Idea
If you start a new tawaf before praying the previous tawaf's two rak'ahs, cancel if less than one circuit; otherwise complete both.

During Hajj or Umrah, it is common to perform multiple tawafs. What happens if you forget to pray the two rak'ahs after a tawaf and only remember after starting another tawaf? The Hanafi school provides a clear distinction based on whether you have completed one circuit of the second tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person has performed a tawaf, forgotten its two-rak'ah prayer, and then started a second tawaf without praying the first one.
2
Check the stage of the second tawaf
Determine if the person has completed one full circuit of the second tawaf or not.
Less than one circuit means the second tawaf has not yet properly begun; one or more circuits means it is underway.
3
Apply the ruling
If less than one circuit: cancel the second tawaf, go back and pray the first tawaf's prayer, then restart the second tawaf later. If one or more circuits: complete the second tawaf, then pray the prayer for the first tawaf, and later pray the prayer for the second tawaf after finishing it.
Each tawaf requires its own two rak'ahs.
4
Note the principle for multiple tawafs
If one performs multiple tawafs, each requires its own two rak'ahs prayed separately after that tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع : طاف ونسي ركعتي الطواف فلم يتذكر إلا بعد شروعه في طواف آخر، فإن كان قبل تمام شوط رفضه وبعد إتمامه لا بل يتم طوافه الذي شرع فيه وعليه لكل أسبوع ركعتان، ولو طاف فرضاً أو غيره ثمانية أشواط إن كان على ظن أن الثامن سابع فلا شيء عليه كالمظنون ابتداء، وإن علم أنه الثامن اختلف فيه والصحيح أنه يلزمه سبعة أشواط للشروع. ولو طاف أسابيع فعليه لكل أسبوع ركعتان على حدة، ولو شك في عدد الأشواط في طواف الركن أو العمرة أعاده ولا يبنى على غالب ظنه بخلاف السلاة . وقيل : إذا كان يكثر ذلك يتحرى، ولو أخبره عدل بعدد يستحب يأخذ بقوله، ولو أخبره عدلان وجب الأخذ بقولهما. وصاحب العذر الدائم إذا طاف أربعة أشواط ثم خرج الوقت توضأ وبنى ولا شيء عليه، ولو حاذته امرأة في الطواف لا يفسد وتمامه في اللباب
Branches: One performed tawaf and forgot the two rak'ahs of tawaf and did not remember until after starting another tawaf. If it was before completing a circuit, he cancels that tawaf; if after completing a circuit, no, rather he completes the tawaf he started, and he owes two rak'ahs for each circuit. If he performs tawaf, fard or otherwise, eight circuits, and he thought the eighth was the seventh, there is nothing on him, like the one who is mistaken from the beginning. If he knows it is the eighth, there is a difference of opinion; the correct view is that it is obliged to perform seven circuits for the initiation. If he performs multiple tawafs, for each tawaf he owes two rak'ahs separately. If he has doubt about the number of circuits in a tawaf of rukn or Umrah, he repeats it and does not rely on his predominant opinion, unlike in prayer. It is said: if this happens frequently, he may estimate. If a just person informs him of a number, it is recommended to take his word; if two just persons inform him, it is obligatory to take their word. The person with a continuous excuse who performs four circuits and then the time goes out, he performs wudu and builds (upon what he has done) and there is nothing on him. If a woman passes by him in tawaf, it does not invalidate tawaf. The rest is in al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This section presents several subsidiary rulings (furu') related to tawaf and its prayer. First, if someone forgets to pray the two rak'ahs after tawaf and only remembers after starting another tawaf: if the second tawaf is less than one complete circuit, he abandons it and prays the first tawaf's two rak'ahs; if he has completed one or more circuits of the second tawaf, he should complete that tawaf and then pray two rak'ahs for the first tawaf and two for the second later. Second, if one performs eight circuits unintentionally, thinking the eighth was the seventh, his tawaf is valid with seven circuits and the extra is disregarded; but if he knows it is the eighth, the correct view is that only seven circuits are counted for the tawaf and the extra is invalid. Third, if one performs multiple tawafs, he must pray two rak'ahs after each one separately. Fourth, doubt in the number of circuits during a required tawaf (like for Hajj or Umrah) requires repeating the entire tawaf; one cannot depend on conjecture, as can be done in prayer. However, if doubt occurs frequently, one may estimate. Fifth, if a reliable person reports the number of circuits, it is recommended to accept a single report and obligatory to accept two reports. Sixth, a person with a continuous excuse (e.g., chronic bleeding) who completes four circuits and then the valid prayer time expires may perform wudu and continue from where he left off, with no penalty. Seventh, if a woman passes directly in front of a person during tawaf, it does not invalidate the tawaf (unlike prayer). The author refers to al-Lubab for further details.

Key Terms
رفضه (rafadahu): To cancel the ongoing tawaf because it was started in error (remembering missed prayer earlier).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if a person forgets the two rak'ahs of tawaf and remembers after starting another tawaf and completing two circuits, what should he do?
A) Cancel the second tawaf and pray the missed prayer.
B) Complete the second tawaf, then pray the missed prayer and later the second tawaf's prayer.
C) Continue the second tawaf and pray only the missed prayer after.
D) Make prostration of forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
If you forget tawaf prayer and start another tawaf, the ruling depends on whether you have completed one circuit: cancel if less, complete if more.

Eight Circuits, Doubt, and Testimony in Tawaf
Rulings on performing eight circuits, doubt in circuit count, and acceptance of witness testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on extra circuits, doubt in circuit count, and acceptance of witness testimony in tawaf.

Core Idea
In tawaf, doubt requires full repetition; dominant opinion does not apply, unlike prayer. Two just witnesses must be accepted.

Tawaf is a precise act of worship. What happens if you perform eight circuits by mistake or doubt the number completed? The Hanafi school has specific rules distinguishing between known error and doubt, and also regarding testimony of reliable informants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario of eight circuits
Distinguish between performing eight circuits mistakenly thinking the eighth was the seventh, and knowingly performing eight.
2
Apply the ruling for eight circuits
If mistaken (thought eighth was seventh): valid, only seven counted, no penalty. If knowingly eight: the correct view is that only seven are valid for the tawaf; the extra is void.
The text says 'the correct view' (al-sahih) is that seven are required for the initiation.
3
Handle doubt in circuits
If doubtful about the number of circuits in an obligatory tawaf (rukun or Umrah), one must repeat the entire tawaf, unlike in prayer where predominant opinion suffices.
Exception: if doubt occurs frequently, one may estimate (taharrī).
4
Apply the rule of testimony
If one just person reports the number, it is recommended to accept; if two just persons report, it is obligatory to accept their word.
Just (adl) means reliable and upright.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فروع : طاف ونسي ركعتي الطواف فلم يتذكر إلا بعد شروعه في طواف آخر، فإن كان قبل تمام شوط رفضه وبعد إتمامه لا بل يتم طوافه الذي شرع فيه وعليه لكل أسبوع ركعتان، ولو طاف فرضاً أو غيره ثمانية أشواط إن كان على ظن أن الثامن سابع فلا شيء عليه كالمظنون ابتداء، وإن علم أنه الثامن اختلف فيه والصحيح أنه يلزمه سبعة أشواط للشروع. ولو طاف أسابيع فعليه لكل أسبوع ركعتان على حدة، ولو شك في عدد الأشواط في طواف الركن أو العمرة أعاده ولا يبنى على غالب ظنه بخلاف السلاة . وقيل : إذا كان يكثر ذلك يتحرى، ولو أخبره عدل بعدد يستحب يأخذ بقوله، ولو أخبره عدلان وجب الأخذ بقولهما. وصاحب العذر الدائم إذا طاف أربعة أشواط ثم خرج الوقت توضأ وبنى ولا شيء عليه، ولو حاذته امرأة في الطواف لا يفسد وتمامه في اللباب
Branches: One performed tawaf and forgot the two rak'ahs of tawaf and did not remember until after starting another tawaf. If it was before completing a circuit, he cancels that tawaf; if after completing a circuit, no, rather he completes the tawaf he started, and he owes two rak'ahs for each circuit. If he performs tawaf, fard or otherwise, eight circuits, and he thought the eighth was the seventh, there is nothing on him, like the one who is mistaken from the beginning. If he knows it is the eighth, there is a difference of opinion; the correct view is that it is obliged to perform seven circuits for the initiation. If he performs multiple tawafs, for each tawaf he owes two rak'ahs separately. If he has doubt about the number of circuits in a tawaf of rukn or Umrah, he repeats it and does not rely on his predominant opinion, unlike in prayer. It is said: if this happens frequently, he may estimate. If a just person informs him of a number, it is recommended to take his word; if two just persons inform him, it is obligatory to take their word. The person with a continuous excuse who performs four circuits and then the time goes out, he performs wudu and builds (upon what he has done) and there is nothing on him. If a woman passes by him in tawaf, it does not invalidate tawaf. The rest is in al-Lubab.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This section presents several subsidiary rulings (furu') related to tawaf and its prayer. First, if someone forgets to pray the two rak'ahs after tawaf and only remembers after starting another tawaf: if the second tawaf is less than one complete circuit, he abandons it and prays the first tawaf's two rak'ahs; if he has completed one or more circuits of the second tawaf, he should complete that tawaf and then pray two rak'ahs for the first tawaf and two for the second later. Second, if one performs eight circuits unintentionally, thinking the eighth was the seventh, his tawaf is valid with seven circuits and the extra is disregarded; but if he knows it is the eighth, the correct view is that only seven circuits are counted for the tawaf and the extra is invalid. Third, if one performs multiple tawafs, he must pray two rak'ahs after each one separately. Fourth, doubt in the number of circuits during a required tawaf (like for Hajj or Umrah) requires repeating the entire tawaf; one cannot depend on conjecture, as can be done in prayer. However, if doubt occurs frequently, one may estimate. Fifth, if a reliable person reports the number of circuits, it is recommended to accept a single report and obligatory to accept two reports. Sixth, a person with a continuous excuse (e.g., chronic bleeding) who completes four circuits and then the valid prayer time expires may perform wudu and continue from where he left off, with no penalty. Seventh, if a woman passes directly in front of a person during tawaf, it does not invalidate the tawaf (unlike prayer). The author refers to al-Lubab for further details.

Key Terms
الظن الغالب (al-zann al-ghalib): Predominant opinion or conjecture used in prayer for doubt, but not allowed for tawaf in the standard Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a person is doubtful about the number of circuits during Tawaf al-Ifadah (obligatory), what must he do?
A) Rely on his predominant opinion and continue.
B) Repeat the entire tawaf.
C) Continue with the lower number.
D) Make prostration of forgetfulness.

Key Takeaway
In tawaf, certainty is required; doubt necessitates full repetition, and two just witnesses must be accepted.

Continuous Excuse and Passing Woman in Tawaf
Rulings on continuous excuse (sahib al-'udhr al-da'im) in tawaf and woman passing by.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a person with a continuous excuse (sahib al-'udhr al-da'im) in tawaf and the effect of a woman passing by during tawaf.

Core Idea
A person with a continuous excuse may build on incomplete tawaf after renewing wudu; a woman's passage does not invalidate tawaf.

Some individuals suffer from chronic conditions like continuous nosebleed or urinary incontinence. How does this affect tawaf? Also, does a woman passing in front of the person during tawaf break the tawaf, as it would in prayer? The Hanafi school provides clear answers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person with continuous excuse
This is someone whose wudu is perpetually invalid due to a continuous condition (e.g., chronic bleeding, incontinence).
2
State the ruling for tawaf with continuous excuse
If such a person performs four circuits of tawaf and then the valid prayer time (for wudu) expires, he may perform wudu and continue from where he left off (build upon the circuits). He does not need to restart the tawaf.
The ruling applies to any time expiry; he can resume after wudu.
3
Apply the ruling on woman passing by
If a woman passes directly in front of a person during tawaf, it does not invalidate the tawaf, unlike in prayer where it would break the prayer.
4
Understand the distinction from prayer
In prayer, a woman passing within close proximity invalidates the prayer, but in tawaf, there is no such rule because tawaf does not have the same restrictions on passing in front.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Two Rak'ahs After Tawaf: Obligation and Subsidiary Rulings
Ruling on the obligation of the two rak'ahs after tawaf with evidence and detailed furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the two rak'ahs after tawaf (wajib) and apply the subsidiary rulings on place, time, forgetting, and multiple tawafs.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after each tawaf are wajib – a distinct obligation established by the Prophet's practice and the Qur'anic command.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling on the two rak'ahs performed after every circumambulation (tawaf). While many Muslims know it is recommended, the Hanafi school holds it is wajib – a binding obligation, though not at the level of fard. The author presents the proof from the Prophet's action and then details a series of practical rulings: where to pray, when to pray, what to do if forgotten, and how to handle multiple tawafs. These details are essential for every Hanafi performing Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled on? The two rak'ahs after each tawaf. The ruling is 'wajib' (obligatory) according to the correct view in the Hanafi school.
The author explicitly says 'فواجبة على الصحيح' (so it is wajib on the correct view).
2
Examine the dalil (proof)
The proof is the long hadith of Jabir where the Prophet recited 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (2:125) and then prayed. This indicates his prayer was a response to the command, thus establishing obligation.
The Qur'anic verse is qat'i in transmission but its command (amr) is interpreted as indicating obligation (wujub) through the Prophet's practical implementation.
3
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf differs on the issue of connecting multiple tawafs without the intervening prayer. He holds it is not disliked if one ends on an odd number (like witr). Abū Hanīfa and Muhammad consider it makruh tahrimi.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that connecting tawafs is makruh tahrimi, as stated by the author's phrase 'ala al-sahih'.
4
Apply the place and time rulings
The prayer is valid anywhere, even outside the Haram or after returning home. The most virtuous place is behind Maqam Ibrahim, then inside the Ka'bah, then the Hijr, etc. It is disliked to delay it without reason, and it should not be prayed at disliked times (e.g., after 'Asr without a prior Maghrib).
If delayed, the prayer remains due; it is not compensated by a blood sacrifice (dam).
5
Work through the subsidiary rulings (furu')
The passage covers: forgetting the rak'ahs and starting another tawaf, performing eight circuits by mistake, multiple tawafs, doubt in number of circuits, accepting testimony, and the perpetual excuse case. Each has specific rules that build on the core obligation.
These rulings demonstrate how the wajib nature of the prayer interacts with practical scenarios during Hajj/Umrah.

Source Text

السلام كذلك في حجة الوداع، وأما صلاة ركعتي الطواف بعد كل أسبوع فواجبة على الصحيح لما ثبت في حديث جابر الطويل أنه عليه السلام لما انتهى إلى مقام إبراهيم عليه السلام قرأ واتخذوا من مقام إبراهيم مصلى) والألف عوض من ياء النسب فلا يجتمعان قال سيبويه : وبعضهم يقول يماني بالتشديد ا هـ . فقول المؤلف ثم حذفوا إحدى ويأتي النسبة يعني من يمني فقط وكذا قوله «بالتخفيف» راجع إلى اليماني قوله : ( فواجبة على الرزاق. ولو صلى أكثر من ركعتين جاز، ولا تجزئ المنذورة والمكتوبة عنها، ولا يجوز اقتداء مصلي ركعتي الطواف بمثله لأن طواف هذا غير طواف الآخر، ويكره تأخيرها عن الطواف إلا في وقت مكروه أي لأن الموالاة سنة
