وتمامه في اللباب
The passage discusses the ruling on ending the tawaf by kissing the Black Stone (sunnah) and the two rak'ahs after each tawaf. It states that the two rak'ahs are wajib (obligatory) based on the Prophet's practice and the verse 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer.' It details that the obligation is established because the Prophet recited the verse before praying, indicating compliance. It then covers various rulings: the two rak'ahs are wajib after every tawaf, whether obligatory or voluntary; they can be prayed anywhere in the mosque or even outside the Haram; it is recommended to pray behind Maqam Ibrahim, then in the Ka'bah, etc.; delaying them is disliked unless in a disliked time; if one forgets and starts another tawaf, if less than a full circuit remains, he abandons it; otherwise he completes and prays for each tawaf separately. Other subsidiary rulings include cases of doubt in the number of circuits, accepting testimony of a just person, and the perpetual excuse case.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the rulings on the two rak'ahs after tawaf. The author begins by clarifying that kissing the Black Stone (istilam) at the end of tawaf is sunnah, based on the Prophet's action in Hajjat al-Wada'. The main focus is on the two rak'ahs after each tawaf: they are wajib (obligatory) according to the correct view in the Hanafi school. The proof is from the long hadith of Jabir, where the Prophet recited the verse 'Take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' and then prayed. This indicates that the prayer was in obedience to that command, establishing its obligation. The author then explains that this obligation applies after every tawaf—whether it is fard (obligatory hajj), wajib (like tawaf al-ifadah), sunnah, or nafl. The prayer can be performed at any time and any place, even outside the Haram or after returning home. If one delays it greatly, it is still valid, but the sunnah is to pray it soon after the tawaf. The best place is behind Maqam Ibrahim, then in the Ka'bah, then in the Hijr, etc. The passage then presents several subsidiary rulings (furu'): if one forgets the two rak'ahs and remembers after starting another tawaf, if he has not completed one full circuit of the new tawaf, he abandons it and prays; otherwise he completes the new tawaf and then prays for both. If he deliberately prays eight circuits thinking the eighth is the seventh, he intends to complete seven; if he knows it is the eighth, the correct view is that seven are obligatory due to his intention to start. Other issues include doubt in circuits, testimony of reliable witnesses, and the case of a person with a chronic excuse. The passage emphasizes that the two rak'ahs are a distinct obligation for each tawaf and cannot be replaced by other prayers.

Key Terms
ركعتي الطواف (rakʿatā al-ṭawāf): The two rakʿahs that are wajib to pray after completing every circumambulation (tawaf).
الوجوب (al-wujūb): The legal category of obligation established by zanni (probable) evidence, distinct from fard which requires qatʿi evidence.
الاستلام (al-istilām): The act of kissing or touching the Black Stone (al-Ḥajar al-Aswad) during tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) on praying two rak'ahs after each tawaf according to the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Fard
C) Wajib
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after each tawaf are a distinct wajib prayer that must be offered for every tawaf, with specific rules on timing and place, and cannot be replaced by other prayers.

Tawaf al-Qudum and Joining Tawafs
Commentary on tawaf al-qudum and joining tawafs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of tawaf al-qudum and explain why joining multiple tawafs is makruh tahrimi according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Core Idea
Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah; joining tawafs without intervening prayer is makruh tahrimi.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq begins the Hajj rituals after entering ihram. The first act upon reaching Mecca is tawaf al-qudum, a sunnah for non-Makkans. The author then addresses joining multiple tawafs consecutively without praying the two rak'at between them, a practice that is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, with a dissenting view from Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-qudum is ruled sunnah for those entering Mecca from outside, not for residents. It is analogous to tahiyyat al-masjid but not waived by other prayers.
2
Locate the ruling on joining tawafs
The text states that joining multiple tawafs without praying the two rak'at between them is makruh tahrimi according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
Makruh tahrimi means it is sinful to do so.
3
Trace the proof for the ruling
The Prophet's constant practice of praying after each tawaf indicates the two rak'at are wajib; omitting a wajib is a sin, hence the karahah.
Constant practice (muwazabah) without leaving indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf holds that joining is not makruh if one ends on an odd number of tawafs (e.g., 3, 5, 7), as the odd number itself serves as a break.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If one forgets and starts a third tawaf without praying, he should break it if he has not completed one full circuit. After completing, the two rak'at are still required.
This follows from the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
المسجد للقدوم وهو سنة لغير المكي ثم اخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً
طاف
بصبي
من التنبيه وهو ظني فكان الثابت الوجوب ويلزمه حكمنا بمواظبته عليه السلام من غير ترك إذ لا يجوز عليه ترك الواجب. ويكره وصل الأسابيع عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف وهي كراهة تحريم لاستلزامها ترك الواجب، ويتفرع على الكراهة أنه لو نسيهما فلم يتذكر إلا بعد أن شرع في طواف آخر إن كان قبل إتمام شوط رفضه وبعد إتمامه لا، ولو لا يصلي ركعتي الطواف عنه . كذا في فتح القدير. وقيد بعضهم قول أبي يوسف بأن ينصرف عن وتر. والمراد بالمقام مقام إبراهيم وهي حجارة يقوم عليها عند نزوله وركوبه من الإبل حين يأتي إلى زيارة هاجر وولدها إسماعيل. كذا ذكر المصنف في المستصفى. وذكر القاضي في تفسيره أنه الحجر الذي فيه أثر قدميه والموضع الذي كان فيه حين قام عليه ودعا الناس إلى الحج، وقيل مقام إبراهيم الحرم كله. وقول المصنف من المسجد» بيان للفضيلة وإلا فحيث أراد بعد الرجوع إلى أهله لأنها على التراخي ما لم يرد أن يطوف أسبوعاً آخر فتكون على الفور لما قدمنا من كراهة وصل الأسابيع، وقد تقدم في الأوقات المكروهة أنه لا يصليهما فيها فحمل قولهما يكره وصل الأسابيع إنما هو في وقت لا يكره التطوع فيه ولم أر نفلاً فيما إذا وصل الأسابيع في وقت الكراهة ثم زال وقتها أنه يكره الطواف قبل الصلاة لكل أسبوع ركعتين. وينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً لما أن الأسابيع في هذه الحالة صارت كأسبوع واحد. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية يقرأ في الركعة الأولى بقل يا أيها الكافرون، وفي الثانية بقل الله أحد تبركاً بفعل رسول الله ، وإن قرأ غير ذلك جاز، وإذا فرغ من للمؤمنين والمؤمنات قوله : (للقدوم وهو سنة لغير المكي أي طف هذا الطواف لأجل قوله : ((ويلزمه) أي يلزم من كون الثابت الوجوب أن نحكم بمواظبته عليه الصلاة والسلام من غير ترك وكان الأولى بالمؤلف عدم ذكره ذلك كما فعل أخوه لإيهامه توقف إثبات الوجوب على هذا اللزوم. نعم ذكره في الفتح لكن غرضه منه إفادة أن ما ورد في كتب الحديث من ثبوت فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام لهما محمول على عدم الترك مرة ليكون دليلاً آخر على الوجوب إذ مطلق الفعل لا يدل عليه قوله : (وقيد بعضهم الخ) قال في السراج ويكره الجمع بين أسبوعين أو أكثر من غير صلاة بينهما عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمه الله، سواء انصرف عن وتر أو شفع، وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكره إذا انصرف عن وتر نحو أن ينصرف عن ثلاثة أسابيع أو خمسة أو سبعة .
هو
صلاته يدعو
قوله : (ولم أر الخ) قال في اللباب في فصل مكروهات الطواف والجمع بين أسبوعين أو أكثر
من غير صلاة بينهما إلا في وقت كراهة الصلاة وهو مؤيد لما قاله المؤلف أيضاً تأمل. فرع غريب : قال العلامة الشيخ قطب الدين الحنفي في منسكه في الفصل الرابع من الباب السادس: رأيت بخط بعض تلامذة الكمال بن الهمام في حاشية فتح القدير: إذا صلى في المسجد الحرام ينبغي أن لا يمنع المار لما روى أحمد وأبو داود عن المطلب بن أبي وداعة أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم

مهللا مصلياً على النبي داعياً ربك بحاجتك ثم اهبط نحو المروة ساعياً بين الميلين
القدوم، وهذا الطواف سنة للآفاقي دون المكي لأنه كتحية المسجد لا يسن للجالس فيه،
تحية
هكذا ذكروا وليس هذا كتحية المسجد من كل وجه فإن الفرض أو السنة تغني عن المسجد بخلاف طواف القدوم لما سيأتي من أن القارن يطوف للعمرة أولاً ثم يطوف للقدوم ثانياً ولا يكفيه الأول، ولم يذكر المصنف الشرب من ماء زمزم بعد ختم الطواف وإنما ذكره بعد الفراغ من أفعال الحج، وكذا إتيان الملتزم والتشبث به وكذا العود إلى الحجر الأسود قبل السعي، والكل مستحب لكن الأخير مشروط بإرادة السعي حتى لو لم يرده لم يعد إلى الحجر بعد ركعتي الطواف كما في الولوالجية.
"
قوله : (ثم أخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم داعياً ربك بحاجتك) لما ثبت في حديث جابر الطويل، وقد قدمنا أن هذا السعي واجب وليس بركن للحديث اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي قاله عليه السلام حين كان يطوف بين الصفا والمروة، فإنه ظني وبمثله لا يثبت الركن لأنه إنما يثبت عندنا بدليل مقطوع، فما في الهداية من تأويله بمعنى كتب استحباباً فمناف لمطلوبه لأنه الوجوب وجميع السبعة الأشواط واجب لا الأكثر فقط فإنهم قالوا في باب الجنايات: لو ترك أكثر الأشواط لزمه دم وإن ترك الأقل لزمه صدقة فدل على وجوب الكل إذ لو كان الواجب الأكثر لم يلزمه في الأقل شيء. أشار بـ «ثم» إلى تراخي السعي عن الطواف، فلو سعى ثم طاف أعاده لأن السعي تبع ولا يجوز تقدم التبع على الأصل كذا ذكر الولوالجي. وصرح في المحيط بأن تقديم الطواف شرط لصحة السعي. وبهذا علم أن تأخير السعي عن الطواف واجب وإلى أن
مر
يصلي مما يلي باب بني سهم والناس يمرون بين يديه وليس بينهما سترة وهو محمول على الطائفين فيما يظهر لأن الطواف صلاة فصار كمن بين يديه صفوف من المصلين ا هـ . . ثم رأيت في البحر العميق حكى عز الدين بن جماعة عن مشكلات الآثار للطحاوي أن المرور بين يدي المصلي بحضرة الكعبة يجوز ا هـ . كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار وباب بني سهم هو المسمى الآن باب العمرة كما سنذكره في السعي قريباً مع زيادة تؤيد ما مر قوله : (وليس هذا كتحية المسجد الخ) قال في النهر : قد . أنه إذا دخل يوم النحر أغناه طواف الفرض عن القدوم وإنما لم يغن طواف العمرة لأن الغنى عن الشيء فرع عن طلب ذلك الشيء وهو لم يطلب إذ ذاك بل لو أراد به القدوم لم يقع إلا عن العمرة لما أن زمنه لا يقبل غيره كرمضان على ما سيأتي قوله : (ولم يذكر المصنف الشرب الخ) وقد ذكر ذلك في فتح القدير فقال : ويستحب أن يأتي زمزم بعد الركعتين قبل الخروج إلى الصفا فيشرب منها ثم يأتي الملتزم قبل الخروج إلى الصفا، وقيل يلتزم الملتزم قبل الركعتين ثم يصليهما ثم يأتي زمزم ثم يعود إلى الحجر. ذكره السروجي ا هـ ملخصاً. قال في شرح اللباب : والثاني هو الأسهل والأفضل وعليه العمل، وفي كثير من الكتب أنه يعود بعد طواف القدوم وصلاته إلى الحجر
عنه
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. ... The mosque for the arrival (tawaf) and it is sunnah for non-Makkan. Then go out to al-Safa and stand upon it facing the House, saying Allahu Akbar...
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq covering the initial rituals of Hajj after entering the state of ihram. It begins with tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), which is ruled as sunnah for those coming from outside Mecca, not for residents. The commentary explains that this tawaf is akin to a greeting for the mosque, but unlike tahiyyat al-masjid, it is not waived by performing an obligatory or supererogatory prayer. There is a discussion on the disliked nature (karahah tahrimiyyah) of joining multiple tawafs without praying two rak'at in between, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf permits it if one ends on an odd number. The text then moves to the sa'i between Safa and Marwah, establishing that it is wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith 'Perform sa'i for Allah has prescribed it upon you.' The commentary argues that sa'i is not a rukn because its evidence is zanni, and a rukn requires qat'i proof. All seven shawts are wajib, not just the majority. Furthermore, tawaf must precede sa'i; if one performs sa'i before tawaf, it must be repeated because sa'i is dependent on tawaf. Additional recommended acts after tawaf include drinking Zamzam, going to the iltizam, and returning to the Black Stone before sa'i. The passage also includes a fatwa on not preventing passersby in front of a praying person near the Kaaba, citing al-Tahawi's view that it is permissible.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The circumambulation performed upon arrival in Mecca for Hajj, before standing at Arafat.
وصل الأسابيع (wasl al-asabi'): Performing consecutive tawafs without praying the two rak'at between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on joining multiple tawafs without praying two rak'at between them?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is makruh tanzihi (disliked but not sinful).
C) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
D) It is haram and invalidates the tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf al-qudum is sunnah; joining tawafs without intervening prayer is makruh tahrimi according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Sa'i: Wajib not Rukn – The Evidence and Its Implications
Proof for sa'i being wajib in the Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to derive the wujub of sa'i from the hadith and explain why sa'i is not a rukn in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Sa'i is wajib because its evidence is zanni; a rukn requires qat'i proof.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses the legal status of sa'i between Safa and Marwah. The author argues that sa'i is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar), basing this on the hadith 'Perform sa'i for Allah has prescribed it upon you.' The commentary explains that since the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), it can only establish obligation, not pillarhood, which requires certain evidence. Additionally, all seven circuits are wajib, as indicated by the dam and sadaqah rulings for omissions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Sa'i between Safa and Marwah is ruled wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith: اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي (Perform sa'i, for Allah has prescribed it upon you).
Quoted in the text.
3
Analyze the evidence strength
The hadith is ahad (single-transmitter), making it zanni al-thubut (uncertain in transmission). In Hanafi usul, a rukn can only be proven by qat'i evidence (mutawatir or Qur'an). Hence, sa'i is not a rukn.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Shafi'is and Malikis consider sa'i a rukn of Hajj, based on different evidence or interpretation.
5
Understand the thamarah (practical consequence)
Omission of a rukn invalidates the Hajj; omission of a wajib requires a dam (sacrifice) but the Hajj is still valid.
This distinction affects pilgrim's obligations.

كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
المسجد للقدوم وهو سنة لغير المكي ثم اخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً

بصبي
من التنبيه وهو ظني فكان الثابت الوجوب ويلزمه حكمنا بمواظبته عليه السلام من غير ترك إذ لا يجوز عليه ترك الواجب. ويكره وصل الأسابيع عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد خلافاً لأبي يوسف وهي كراهة تحريم لاستلزامها ترك الواجب، ويتفرع على الكراهة أنه لو نسيهما فلم يتذكر إلا بعد أن شرع في طواف آخر إن كان قبل إتمام شوط رفضه وبعد إتمامه لا، ولو لا يصلي ركعتي الطواف عنه . كذا في فتح القدير. وقيد بعضهم قول أبي يوسف بأن ينصرف عن وتر. والمراد بالمقام مقام إبراهيم وهي حجارة يقوم عليها عند نزوله وركوبه من الإبل حين يأتي إلى زيارة هاجر وولدها إسماعيل. كذا ذكر المصنف في المستصفى. وذكر القاضي في تفسيره أنه الحجر الذي فيه أثر قدميه والموضع الذي كان فيه حين قام عليه ودعا الناس إلى الحج، وقيل مقام إبراهيم الحرم كله. وقول المصنف من المسجد» بيان للفضيلة وإلا فحيث أراد بعد الرجوع إلى أهله لأنها على التراخي ما لم يرد أن يطوف أسبوعاً آخر فتكون على الفور لما قدمنا من كراهة وصل الأسابيع، وقد تقدم في الأوقات المكروهة أنه لا يصليهما فيها فحمل قولهما يكره وصل الأسابيع إنما هو في وقت لا يكره التطوع فيه ولم أر نفلاً فيما إذا وصل الأسابيع في وقت الكراهة ثم زال وقتها أنه يكره الطواف قبل الصلاة لكل أسبوع ركعتين. وينبغي أن يكون مكروهاً لما أن الأسابيع في هذه الحالة صارت كأسبوع واحد. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية يقرأ في الركعة الأولى بقل يا أيها الكافرون، وفي الثانية بقل الله أحد تبركاً بفعل رسول الله ، وإن قرأ غير ذلك جاز، وإذا فرغ من للمؤمنين والمؤمنات قوله : (للقدوم وهو سنة لغير المكي أي طف هذا الطواف لأجل قوله : ((ويلزمه) أي يلزم من كون الثابت الوجوب أن نحكم بمواظبته عليه الصلاة والسلام من غير ترك وكان الأولى بالمؤلف عدم ذكره ذلك كما فعل أخوه لإيهامه توقف إثبات الوجوب على هذا اللزوم. نعم ذكره في الفتح لكن غرضه منه إفادة أن ما ورد في كتب الحديث من ثبوت فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام لهما محمول على عدم الترك مرة ليكون دليلاً آخر على الوجوب إذ مطلق الفعل لا يدل عليه قوله : (وقيد بعضهم الخ) قال في السراج ويكره الجمع بين أسبوعين أو أكثر من غير صلاة بينهما عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد رحمه الله، سواء انصرف عن وتر أو شفع، وقال أبو يوسف : لا يكره إذا انصرف عن وتر نحو أن ينصرف عن ثلاثة أسابيع أو خمسة أو سبعة .

قوله : (ولم أر الخ) قال في اللباب في فصل مكروهات الطواف والجمع بين أسبوعين أو أكثر

هكذا ذكروا وليس هذا كتحية المسجد من كل وجه فإن الفرض أو السنة تغني عن المسجد بخلاف طواف القدوم لما سيأتي من أن القارن يطوف للعمرة أولاً ثم يطوف للقدوم ثانياً ولا يكفيه الأول، ولم يذكر المصنف الشرب من ماء زمزم بعد ختم الطواف وإنما ذكره بعد الفراغ من أفعال الحج، وكذا إتيان الملتزم والتشبث به وكذا العود إلى الحجر الأسود قبل السعي، والكل مستحب لكن الأخير مشروط بإرادة السعي حتى لو لم يرده لم يعد إلى الحجر بعد ركعتي الطواف كما في الولوالجية.
"
قوله : (ثم أخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم داعياً ربك بحاجتك) لما ثبت في حديث جابر الطويل، وقد قدمنا أن هذا السعي واجب وليس بركن للحديث اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي قاله عليه السلام حين كان يطوف بين الصفا والمروة، فإنه ظني وبمثله لا يثبت الركن لأنه إنما يثبت عندنا بدليل مقطوع، فما في الهداية من تأويله بمعنى كتب استحباباً فمناف لمطلوبه لأنه الوجوب وجميع السبعة الأشواط واجب لا الأكثر فقط فإنهم قالوا في باب الجنايات: لو ترك أكثر الأشواط لزمه دم وإن ترك الأقل لزمه صدقة فدل على وجوب الكل إذ لو كان الواجب الأكثر لم يلزمه في الأقل شيء. أشار بـ «ثم» إلى تراخي السعي عن الطواف، فلو سعى ثم طاف أعاده لأن السعي تبع ولا يجوز تقدم التبع على الأصل كذا ذكر الولوالجي. وصرح في المحيط بأن تقديم الطواف شرط لصحة السعي. وبهذا علم أن تأخير السعي عن الطواف واجب وإلى أن
مر
يصلي مما يلي باب بني سهم والناس يمرون بين يديه وليس بينهما سترة وهو محمول على الطائفين فيما يظهر لأن الطواف صلاة فصار كمن بين يديه صفوف من المصلين ا هـ . . ثم رأيت في البحر العميق حكى عز الدين بن جماعة عن مشكلات الآثار للطحاوي أن المرور بين يدي المصلي بحضرة الكعبة يجوز ا هـ . كذا في حاشية المدني على الدر المختار وباب بني سهم هو المسمى الآن باب العمرة كما سنذكره في السعي قريباً مع زيادة تؤيد ما مر قوله : (وليس هذا كتحية المسجد الخ) قال في النهر : قد . أنه إذا دخل يوم النحر أغناه طواف الفرض عن القدوم وإنما لم يغن طواف العمرة لأن الغنى عن الشيء فرع عن طلب ذلك الشيء وهو لم يطلب إذ ذاك بل لو أراد به القدوم لم يقع إلا عن العمرة لما أن زمنه لا يقبل غيره كرمضان على ما سيأتي قوله : (ولم يذكر المصنف الشرب الخ) وقد ذكر ذلك في فتح القدير فقال : ويستحب أن يأتي زمزم بعد الركعتين قبل الخروج إلى الصفا فيشرب منها ثم يأتي الملتزم قبل الخروج إلى الصفا، وقيل يلتزم الملتزم قبل الركعتين ثم يصليهما ثم يأتي زمزم ثم يعود إلى الحجر. ذكره السروجي ا هـ ملخصاً. قال في شرح اللباب : والثاني هو الأسهل والأفضل وعليه العمل، وفي كثير من الكتب أنه يعود بعد طواف القدوم وصلاته إلى الحجر
عنه
Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. ... The mosque for the arrival (tawaf) and it is sunnah for non-Makkan. Then go out to al-Safa and stand upon it facing the House, saying Allahu Akbar...
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on Kanz al-Daqa'iq covering the initial rituals of Hajj after entering the state of ihram. It begins with tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf), which is ruled as sunnah for those coming from outside Mecca, not for residents. The commentary explains that this tawaf is akin to a greeting for the mosque, but unlike tahiyyat al-masjid, it is not waived by performing an obligatory or supererogatory prayer. There is a discussion on the disliked nature (karahah tahrimiyyah) of joining multiple tawafs without praying two rak'at in between, attributed to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, while Abu Yusuf permits it if one ends on an odd number. The text then moves to the sa'i between Safa and Marwah, establishing that it is wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith 'Perform sa'i for Allah has prescribed it upon you.' The commentary argues that sa'i is not a rukn because its evidence is zanni, and a rukn requires qat'i proof. All seven shawts are wajib, not just the majority. Furthermore, tawaf must precede sa'i; if one performs sa'i before tawaf, it must be repeated because sa'i is dependent on tawaf. Additional recommended acts after tawaf include drinking Zamzam, going to the iltizam, and returning to the Black Stone before sa'i. The passage also includes a fatwa on not preventing passersby in front of a praying person near the Kaaba, citing al-Tahawi's view that it is permissible.

Key Terms
السعي (sa'i): Walking seven times between Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the evidence that sa'i is wajib and not a rukn?
A) The Qur'anic verse 'Indeed, as-Safa and al-Marwah are among the symbols of Allah.'
B) The hadith 'اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي' which is ahad and thus zanni.
C) The consensus of the Companions.
D) The fact that the Prophet performed sa'i only once in his life.

Key Takeaway
Sa'i is wajib in the Hanafi school because its evidence is zanni; a rukn requires qat'i proof.

Sa'y is Wajib, Not Rukn: Hanafi Proof
Proves Sa'y is wajib with dalil and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sa'y (wajib vs rukn) and explain why the proof from the hadith supports wujub but not rukn.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib because its proof is zanni; rukn requires qat'i dalil.

In this passage, the author of Al-Bahr al-Rai'iq explains that Sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah) is wajib, not a rukn. He cites a hadith and a qiyas from the chapter on Hajj offenses to support the Hanafi position. This lesson unpacks that argument and the underlying usul principle that rukn must be proven by definitive evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage explicitly states that Sa'y is wajib, not rukn. Note that the ruling is about the legal status of the act itself, not about its conditions.
The author is commenting on the matn's instruction to go to Safa.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي' (Perform Sa'y, for Allah has prescribed Sa'y upon you). Identify the type of proof: ahad (single-narrator) hadith.
The hadith is mentioned as reported from Jabir.
3
Analyze the epistemological weight
For the Hanafi school, a rukn (pillar) must be established by a qat'i (definitive) proof, such as the Quran or mutawatir hadith. The Sa'y hadith is ahad, hence zanni (speculative) in transmission. Therefore, it can only establish wujub, not rukn.
This is a key usul principle: the strength of proof determines the strength of the ruling.
4
Examine the qiyas evidence
The passage additionally uses a qiyas from the chapter on Hajj offenses (jinayat). If a pilgrim omits most circuits, a dam is due; if only a few, a sadaqah is due. This shows that all seven circuits are wajib, not just the majority. If the wajib were only the majority, omitting the minority would have no penalty.
This is an indirect proof that Sa'y as a whole is wajib.
5
Address the counter-interpretation
The passage also refutes an interpretation found in al-Hidayah that 'كتب' means 'prescribed as mustahabb'. The author argues that the apparent meaning of the command is wujub, not mere recommendation.
This demonstrates how Hanafi jurists resolve apparent conflicts within their own tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم أخرج إلى الصفا وقم عليه مستقبل البيت مكبراً مهللاً مصلياً على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم داعياً ربك بحاجتك) لما ثبت في حديث جابر الطويل، وقد قدمنا أن هذا السعي واجب وليس بركن للحديث اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي قاله عليه السلام حين كان يطوف بين الصفا والمروة، فإنه ظني وبمثله لا يثبت الركن لأنه إنما يثبت عندنا بدليل مقطوع، فما في الهداية من تأويله بمعنى كتب استحباباً فمناف لمطلوبه لأنه الوجوب وجميع السبعة الأشواط واجب لا الأكثر فقط فإنهم قالوا في باب الجنايات: لو ترك أكثر الأشواط لزمه دم وإن ترك الأقل لزمه صدقة فدل على وجوب الكل إذ لو كان الواجب الأكثر لم يلزمه في الأقل شيء.
His statement: (Then go out to al-Safa and stand upon it facing the House, magnifying Allah, saying la ilaha illa Allah, sending blessings on the Prophet, supplicating your Lord with your need) due to what is established in the lengthy hadith of Jabir. We have already stated that this Sa'y is wajib and not a rukn, due to the hadith: 'Perform Sa'y, for Allah has prescribed Sa'y upon you' – he said this while he was performing Sa'y between Safa and Marwah. Indeed, it is zanni (speculative), and by such a [proof] a rukn is not established, because a rukn is only established by a qat'i (definitive) proof with us. As for what is in al-Hidayah from interpreting it as meaning 'He prescribed as mustahabb', it contradicts his objective, because [the command indicates] wujub. And all seven circuits are wajib, not just the majority. Indeed, they said in the chapter on offenses: if one abandons most of the circuits, a dam is due; if he abandons the lesser part, sadaqah is due. This indicates the obligation of all, for if the wajib were only the majority, nothing would be due for abandoning the lesser part.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The author comments on the matn's instruction to go to Safa and make du'a. He establishes that Sa'y is wajib (obligatory) but not a rukn (pillar). The proof is the hadith 'اسعوا فإن الله كتب عليكم السعي' (Perform Sa'y, for Allah has prescribed Sa'y upon you). The Hanafi position is that this hadith is ahad (single-narrator) and thus zanni al-thubut (speculative in transmission), and a rukn requires a qat'i proof (like Quran or mutawatir hadith). Al-Hidayah's interpretation of 'كتب' as 'prescribed as mustahabb' is rejected because the apparent meaning of the command indicates wujub. Further proof: in the chapter on jinayat (offenses in Hajj), if one omits most of the Sa'y circuits, a dam is due; if one omits only a few, a sadaqah is due. This gradation shows that all circuits are wajib; if only the majority were wajib, no penalty would apply for omitting the minority.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral act whose omission invalidates the Hajj/Umrah.
الواجب (al-wajib): An obligatory act whose omission requires compensation (dam/sadaqah) but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Sa'y classified as wajib rather than rukn?
A) Because it is performed outside the Haram.
B) Because its proof (the hadith) is zanni (speculative), not qat'i.
C) Because it is only for non-Makkans.
D) Because it can be done on a mount.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school classifies Sa'y as wajib, not rukn, because its proof (ahad hadith) is zanni, and a rukn requires qat'i evidence.

Sequence and Timing of Sa'y: Tawaf Must Precede, Delay is Permissible
Ruling on sequence and timing of Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sequence of Tawaf and Sa'y, explain that Tawaf is a condition for Sa'y's validity, and distinguish between the obligatory delay and the sunnah of immediate connection.

Core Idea
Sa'y is a follower of Tawaf: it cannot precede Tawaf, but it can be delayed without penalty.

In this lesson, we examine the first condition of Sa'y: its sequence relative to Tawaf. The Hanafi school establishes that Tawaf must precede Sa'y as a condition of validity, yet Sa'y need not be performed immediately after Tawaf. Understanding this distinction prevents common errors in hajj practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition
Locate the statement in the text that Tawaf must precede Sa'y. Note the phrase 'شرط لصحة السعي' (condition for validity of Sa'y).
2
Understand 'tabi' (follower)
The text states that Sa'y is a follower (tabi') of Tawaf. The follower cannot precede the original. This is the logical basis for the condition.
3
Distinguish between obligation and sunnah
The text says delaying Sa'y after Tawaf is wajib (obligatory), but it need not be immediate. The sunnah is to connect them promptly, similar to taharah before prayer.
The sunnah is not obligatory; delay even for a long time is permissible without penalty.
4
Apply to special cases
Since Sa'y does not require ritual purity, a menstruating woman or one in janabah may perform Sa'y. This follows from the fact that Sa'y is not a prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أشار بـ «ثم» إلى تراخي السعي عن الطواف، فلو سعى ثم طاف أعاده لأن السعي تبع ولا يجوز تقدم التبع على الأصل كذا ذكر الولوالجي. وصرح في المحيط بأن تقديم الطواف شرط لصحة السعي. وبهذا علم أن تأخير السعي عن الطواف واجب وإلى أن لا يجب بعد الطواف فوراً بل لو أتى به بعد زمان ولو طويلاً لا شيء عليه، والسنة ما الاتصال به كالطهارة فصح سعي الحائض والجنب، وكذا الصعود عليه مع بعده سنة حتى يكره لا يصعد عليهما، كما في المحيط، وقد قدمنا أن المشي فيه واجب حتى لو سعى راكباً من غير عذر لزمه .دم. ولم يذكر أي باب يخرج منه إلى الصفا لأنه مخير لأن المقصود يحصل به، وإنما خرج عليه السلام من باب بني مخزوم المسمى الآن بباب الصفا لأنه أقرب الأبواب إليه فكان اتفاقاً لا قصداً فلم يكن سنة. ولم يذكر رفع اليدين في هذا الدعاء وهو مندوب حذو منكبيه جاعلاً باطنهما إلى السماء ثم اعلم أن أصل الصفا في اللغة الحجر الأملس وهو والمروة جبلان معروفان بمكة وكان الصفا مذكراً لأن آدم عليه السلام وقف عليه فسمي به، ووقفت حواء على المروة فسميت باسم المرأة فأنت لذلك. كذا ذكر القرطبي في تفسيره.
He indicated by 'thumma' (then) the delay of Sa'y from Tawaf. So if one performed Sa'y and then Tawaf, he repeats it, because Sa'y is a follower and the follower cannot precede the original; so mentioned al-Walwaliji. And in al-Muhit it is explicitly stated that preceding Tawaf is a condition for the validity of Sa'y. By this it is known that delaying Sa'y after Tawaf is obligatory, and that it is not obligatory immediately after Tawaf; rather, if he performs it after some time, even a long time, nothing is due upon him. And the sunnah is to connect it like taharah. Thus the Sa'y of a menstruating woman or a junub is valid. Likewise, ascending upon them (Safa and Marwah) despite its later time is sunnah, so much so that it is makruh not to ascend upon them, as in al-Muhit. And we have already mentioned that walking in it is wajib; so if one performs Sa'y riding without an excuse, a dam is due. And he did not mention from which door to exit to Safa, because one has choice, since the objective is achieved by it. The Prophet only exited from the Banu Makhzum door, now called Bab al-Safa, because it was the closest door to him, so it was coincidental, not intentional, thus it is not sunnah. And he did not mention raising the hands in this supplication; it is mustahabb, with hands at shoulder level, palms facing the sky. Then know that the literal meaning of Safa is smooth stone, and it and Marwah are two well-known mountains in Makkah. Safa is masculine because Adam stood upon it and was named by it; Hawwa stood on Marwah and it was named after the woman, so it is feminine. Thus mentioned al-Qurtubi in his tafsir.
Source pages p. 582

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings and sunnahs related to Sa'y. First, the sequence: Sa'y must come after Tawaf. The word 'thumma' (then) in the text indicates delay. If one performs Sa'y before Tawaf, the Sa'y is invalid and must be repeated. The condition is that Tawaf precedes Sa'y; it is not required that Sa'y be immediate. It can be delayed even for a long time without penalty. However, the sunnah is to connect them, similar to how taharah is connected to prayer. A menstruating woman or one in janabah can perform Sa'y because it is not a prayer. Ascending onto Safa and Marwah is sunnah; it is makruh to omit ascending if able. Walking in Sa'y is wajib; riding without a valid excuse necessitates a dam (blood sacrifice). The door through which one exits to Safa is not specified as sunnah; the Prophet happened to use the nearest door (Banu Makhzum). It is mubah to use any door. Raising hands in du'a on Safa is mustahabb. The passage concludes with linguistic notes on the names Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms
التراخي (al-tarakhkhi): Delay; Sa'y can be delayed after Tawaf without time limit.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition external to the act; here, Tawaf before Sa'y is a condition of validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on performing Sa'y before Tawaf?
A) It is valid and no repeat needed.
B) It is invalid and must be repeated.
C) It is makruh but valid.
D) It requires only a dam.

Key Takeaway
Tawaf must precede Sa'y as a condition of validity, but Sa'y can be delayed after Tawaf without any penalty.

Sunnas and Wajibat of Sa'y: Walking, Ascending, and Other Acts
Rulings on wajibat and sunnas of Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the wajibat (walking) and sunnas (ascending Safa and Marwah, raising hands in du'a) of Sa'y, explain the ruling on riding, and state that the choice of exit door is mubah.

Core Idea
Walking in Sa'y is obligatory; ascending Safa and Marwah is sunnah; the Prophet's choice of door was coincidental, not sunnah.

This lesson covers the remaining rulings of Sa'y: the obligation of walking, the sunnah of ascending the hills, the permissibility of using any door to exit to Safa, and the mustahabb act of raising hands in supplication. These details ensure the pilgrim performs Sa'y correctly and completely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wajib
The text states that walking is wajib. If one rides without an excuse, a dam is required. Locate the phrase 'المشي فيه واجب'.
The dam is a blood sacrifice.
2
Identify the sunnas
The text mentions two sunnas: ascending Safa and Marwah, and raising hands in du'a (mustahabb). Also the sunnah of connecting Sa'y to Tawaf was in the previous portion.
Ascending is sunnah; it is makruh to omit ascending if able.
3
Understand the ruling of the door
The Prophet exited from the Banu Makhzum door by coincidence, not deliberate. Therefore, it is not sunnah to use that specific door; any door to Safa is permissible (mubah).
4
Review the linguistic note
The passage explains that Safa is masculine and Marwah is feminine based on the names of the first humans. This is a linguistic benefit, not a ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If one performs Sa'y before Tawaf, the Sa'y is invalid and must be repeated. The condition is that Tawaf precedes Sa'y; it is not required that Sa'y be immediate. It can be delayed even for a long time without penalty. However, the sunnah is to connect them, similar to how taharah is connected to prayer. A menstruating woman or one in janabah can perform Sa'y because it is not a prayer. Ascending onto Safa and Marwah is sunnah; it is makruh to omit ascending if able. Walking in Sa'y is wajib; riding without a valid excuse necessitates a dam (blood sacrifice). The door through which one exits to Safa is not specified as sunnah; the Prophet happened to use the nearest door (Banu Makhzum). It is mubah to use any door. Raising hands in du'a on Safa is mustahabb. The passage concludes with linguistic notes on the names Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A blood sacrifice required as compensation for certain omissions or violations during hajj.
مندوب (mandub): Recommended; equivalent to mustahabb. Omission does not invalidate the act or require compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a healthy pilgrim performing Sa'y riding a car?
A) Valid, no penalty.
B) Valid but requires a dam.
C) Invalid, must repeat.
D) Makruh but valid.

Key Takeaway
Walking in Sa'y is wajib; ascending Safa and Marwah is sunnah; the choice of exit door is mubah.

Best Timing for Sa'y: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the best timing for Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi view on the best timing for Sa'y (after Tawaf al-Qudum vs. after Tawaf al-Ziyarah) and distinguish the rulings for Mufrid, Mutamatti', and Qarin pilgrims.

Core Idea
Sa'y is best delayed after Tawaf al-Ziyarah for Mufrid/Mutamatti'; for Qarin, early Sa'y is better or sunnah.

When should a pilgrim perform Sa'y? Some say immediately after the arrival tawaf, others say wait until after the obligatory tawaf. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, we explore an intra-Hanafi debate that balances principles of fiqh and practical ease. The key is understanding that Sa'y is wajib and should ideally follow a rukn, but the day of Nahr is crowded, so early performance is permissible and even recommended for some.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main dispute
What is the core question the passage addresses? Is it about permissibility or preference?
The passage asks whether it is better to perform Sa'y early (after Tawaf al-Qudum) or delay it to after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.
2
Determine the majority Hanafi position
For Mufrid and Mutamatti' pilgrims, what does the majority say is the best practice?
The majority say it is better to delay Sa'y to after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, because Sa'y (wajib) should follow a rukn.
3
Spot the exception for Qarin
For the Qarin pilgrim, does the same rule apply? What does the text say?
For Qarin, early Sa'y is better or even sunnah.
4
Examine the divergence on permissibility for Makkans
Some scholars discuss whether early Sa'y is permissible for those who begin ihram from Makkah. What are the two views?
Al-Karkhi, al-Quduri, and others permit it; al-Bada'i' does not. The majority permit it.
5
Extract the practical consequence
What does this mean for a pilgrim deciding when to perform Sa'y?
The pilgrim may choose, but following the preferred timing brings more reward. For Qarin, early is recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التحفة الأفضل للحاج أن لا يسعى بعد طواف القدوم لأن السعي واجب لا يليق أن يكون تبعاً للسنة بل يؤخره إلى طواف الزيارة لأنه ركن واللائق للواجب أن يكون بعد ركن اختلاف تقدم وفي وفي ثم يتوجه إلى الصفا من غير ذكر زمزم والملتزم فيما بينهما، ولعل وجه تركهما عدم تأكدهما مع أحدهما ا هـ قوله : (لكن الأخير الخ قال في شرح اللباب : والأصل أن كل طواف فإنه يعود إلى استلام بعد الصلاة وما لا فلا على ما قاله قاضيخان في شرحه أن هذا الاستلام لافتتاح السعي بين الصفا والمروة فإن لم يرد السعي بعده لم يعد عليه ا هـ قوله : (فلم يكن سنة) مثله في الهداية قال فلي النهر والمذكور في السراج أن الخروج منه أفضل من غيره ا هـ. حاشية نوح أفندي قال ابن عمر وهو سنة . فقول صاحب الهداية لا أنه سنة مخالف له لكنه موافق لكلام أهل المذهب لأنه ذكر في البدائع وغيره أنه . أن يستحب يخرج من باب الصفا ولا يتعين ذلك سنة. فالحاصل أنه ليس سنة بل مستحب فيجوز الخروج من غيره بدون الإساءة قوله: (وفي التحفة الأفضل للحاج أي المفرد بالحج والمتمتع بخلاف القارن لأنه ذكر في اللباب في الأفضلية خلافاً ثم قال : والخلاف في غير القارن أما القارن فالأفضل له تقديم السعي أو يسن ا هـ . حاشية المدني : اعلم أن السعي الواجب في الحج يدخل وقته عقب طواف الزيارة ويمتد إلى آخر العمرة لأن السعي تبع للطواف والشيء إنما يتبع ما هو أقوى منه والسعي واجب وطواف الزيارة ركن، ويجوز تقديمه على الوقوف وإيقاعه عقب طواف القدوم لكثرة أفعال الحج يوم النحر، لكن يشترط أن يكون في أشهر الحج حتى لمن لا عليه طواف القدوم في الأصح. واختلفوا هل الأفضل تأخيره إلى وقته أم تقديمه؟ وعلى الثاني هل هو عام لأهل مكة وغيرهم أم خاص بغيرهم ممن عليه طواف القدوم؟ وحاصله أن جواز تقديم السعي ممن عليه طواف القدوم متفق عليه، وأما أفضليته ففيها خلاف، وأما جواز لمن أهل من مكة ممن ليس عليه طواف قدوم اختاره غير واحد من المشايخ كالكرخي والقدوري وصاحب الهداية والكافي والنهاية المجمع وغيرهم. أما الأفضلية فصححها الكرماني، وذهب صاحب البدائع إلى عدم جواز التقديم لمن أحرم من مكة وهو خلاف ما عليه أكثر
And in al-Tuhfah: It is better for the pilgrim not to perform Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum because Sa'y is wajib and it is not fitting for it to be a follower of a sunnah; rather, he should delay it to Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is a rukn and it is appropriate for the wajib to be after a rukn. ... dispute of precedence ... and in ... then he proceeds to Safa without mentioning Zamzam and the Multazam between them; perhaps the reason for omitting them is that they are not firmly established as one. Then his statement: (but the latter) etc. He said in Sharh al-Lubab: The principle is that every Tawaf one returns for kissing after the prayer, and what is not [returns]? According to what Qadikhan said in his commentary: that this kissing is to begin Sa'y between Safa and Marwah; if he does not intend Sa'y after it, he does not return. Then his statement: (so it was not sunnah) similar is in al-Hidayah. He said in al-Nahr: and what is mentioned in al-Siraj that exiting from it is better than others. Hashiyah of Nuh Afandi: Ibn Umar said it is sunnah. So the statement of the author of al-Hidayah that it is not sunnah contradicts him, but it agrees with the words of the school. Because he mentioned in al-Bada'i' and others that it is mustahabb to exit from Bab al-Safa, not specifically sunnah. The conclusion is that it is not sunnah but mustahabb, so exiting from another door is allowed without blame. His statement: (and in al-Tuhfah it is better for the pilgrim) meaning the Mufrid (performing Hajj only) and the Mutamatti', unlike the Qarin, because in al-Lubab there is a difference on the best, then he said: the difference is for non-Qarin; as for the Qarin, it is better for him to perform Sa'y early, or it is sunnah. Hashiyah of al-Madani: Know that the time for the wajib Sa'y in Hajj begins after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and extends to the end of one's life, because Sa'y is a follower of Tawaf, and a thing follows what is stronger than it; Sa'y is wajib and Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a rukn. It is permissible to perform it before standing at Arafah and to perform it after Tawaf al-Qudum due to the many acts of Hajj on the day of Nahr. But it is conditioned that it be in the months of Hajj, even for the one not obliged to do Tawaf al-Qudum according to the soundest view. And they differed: is it better to delay it to its time or to perform it early? On the second [view], is it general for the people of Makkah and others, or specific for others who have Tawaf al-Qudum? The summary is that the permissibility of performing Sa'y early for the one who has Tawaf al-Qudum is agreed upon. As for its being better, there is difference. As for the permissibility for the one who entered Ihram from Makkah and does not have Tawaf al-Qudum, it is chosen by more than one of the mashayikh, such as al-Karkhi, al-Quduri, the author of al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, al-Nihayah al-Mujamma', and others. As for its being better, al-Kirmani affirmed it, and the author of al-Bada'i' held the view of impermissibility of performing it early for the one who entered Ihram from Makkah, which is contrary to what is held by the majority.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the best timing for Sa'y. The author cites al-Tuhfah, which states that it is better for the pilgrim performing Ifrad or Tamattu' not to perform Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum (arrival tawaf), but to delay it to after Tawaf al-Ziyarah (visit tawaf), because the latter is a rukn and the wajib Sa'y should follow a rukn, not a sunnah (Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah). The text then discusses various views: some say it is better to delay, others say it is better to perform it early. There is also a discussion of the door: it is mustahabb to exit from Bab al-Safa, but it is not sunnah. Then the dispute continues for different categories: Mufrid, Mutamatti', Qarin. For Qarin, it is better to perform Sa'y early. The time for Sa'y begins after Tawaf al-Ziyarah but can be performed earlier, even before standing at Arafah, if done after Tawaf al-Qudum, provided it is within the months of Hajj. Scholars like al-Karkhi, al-Quduri, and the author of al-Hidayah permit early Sa'y for those who began Ihram from Makkah. The author of al-Bada'i' disagrees for Makkans. The majority seem to permit early Sa'y for all, but the best is to delay it to after Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah; it is sunnah for non-Makkans.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj performed after standing at Arafah; it is a rukn.
المفرد (al-mufrid): One who performs Hajj only (without Umrah).
المتمتع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah first and then Hajj in the same journey.
القارن (al-qarin): One who combines Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The Mufrid
B) The Mutamatti'
C) The Qarin
D) The pilgrim from Makkah

Key Takeaway
Sa'y is wajib; the best timing depends on pilgrim type: delay for Mufrid/Mutamatti', early for Qarin; early is always permissible.

Basic Rulings of Sa'y: Timing, Walking, and Compensation
Stating foundational rulings of Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for Sa'y regarding timing, walking, climbing, and the requirement of dam for riding without excuse.

Core Idea
Sa'y is wajib, walking is obligatory, riding without excuse requires a dam.

This lesson unpacks key rulings from the Hanafi commentary on Sa'y (the ritual walking between Safa and Marwah). Many assume Sa'y must follow Tawaf immediately, but the Hanafi school allows a delay. We also clarify the obligatory nature of walking versus riding, and the recommended acts like climbing the hills.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The passage rules on Sa'y. First, recognize that Sa'y is a wajib act, not a rukn. Its performance does not require immediacy after Tawaf.
This distinguishes Hanafi from Shafi'i, where Sa'y is a rukn.
2
Analyze conditions for validity
Note that Sa'y is valid even without ritual purity (taharah). The example of a menstruating woman and a person in janabah demonstrates that purity is not a condition.
This contrasts with Tawaf, which requires purity.
3
Determine the obligatory element and its omission
Walking during Sa'y is wajib. If one rides without an excuse, a dam (sacrifice) is required. This establishes the consequence for leaving a wajib.
The dam compensates for missing the wajib; the act itself remains valid.
4
Identify recommended (sunnah) and mandub acts
Climbing onto Safa and Marwah is sunnah, so omitting it is disliked (makruh tanzih). Raising hands in supplication is mandub (recommended).
These are not obligatory but enhance the ritual.
5
Understand the significance of the Prophet's action
The Prophet exited from Bab al-Safa, but this was coincidental (nearest door), not a deliberate sunnah. Therefore, one may exit from any door.
This illustrates the principle: actions of the Prophet are not always sunnah; context matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السعي لا يجب بعد الطواف فوراً بل لو أتى به بعد زمان ولو طويلاً لا شيء عليه، والسنة ما الاتصال به كالطهارة فصح سعي الحائض والجنب، وكذا الصعود عليه مع بعده سنة حتى يكره لا يصعد عليهما، كما في المحيط، وقد قدمنا أن المشي فيه واجب حتى لو سعى راكباً من غير عذر لزمه .دم. ولم يذكر أي باب يخرج منه إلى الصفا لأنه مخير لأن المقصود يحصل به، وإنما خرج عليه السلام من باب بني مخزوم المسمى الآن بباب الصفا لأنه أقرب الأبواب إليه فكان اتفاقاً لا قصداً فلم يكن سنة. ولم يذكر رفع اليدين في هذا الدعاء وهو مندوب حذو منكبيه جاعلاً باطنهما إلى السماء ثم اعلم أن أصل الصفا في اللغة الحجر الأملس وهو والمروة جبلان معروفان بمكة وكان الصفا مذكراً لأن آدم عليه السلام وقف عليه فسمي به، ووقفت حواء على المروة فسميت باسم المرأة فأنت لذلك. كذا ذكر القرطبي في تفسيره.
Sa'y is not obligatory immediately after Tawaf; rather if one performs it after a time, even a long time, there is nothing upon him. The Sunnah is to connect it, like purity, so the Sa'y of a menstruating woman and a person in major ritual impurity is valid. Likewise, climbing upon it despite its distance is Sunnah so that it is disliked not to climb upon them, as in al-Muhit. And we have stated that walking in it is wajib, so if one performed Sa'y riding without an excuse, a dam is incumbent upon him. And he did not mention which door he exits to Safa because he is given choice, for the objective is achieved by it. Rather, the Prophet (peace be upon him) exited from the door of Banu Makhzum, now called Bab al-Safa, because it was the nearest door to it; this was coincidental not intentional, so it was not a Sunnah. And he did not mention raising the hands in this supplication, and it is recommended (mandub) at the level of the shoulders, making their palms towards the sky. Then know that the origin of al-Safa in language is the smooth stone; it and al-Marwah are two known mountains in Mecca. Al-Safa is masculine because Adam (peace be upon him) stood upon it, so it was named after him, and Hawwa' stood on al-Marwah, so it was named after the woman, therefore it is as such. Thus mentioned al-Qurtubi in his Tafsir.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This is a ruling statement passage from the commentary of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifying key rulings about Sa'y. The author clarifies that Sa'y does not have to be performed immediately after Tawaf; it can be delayed without penalty. However, it is Sunnah to perform it consecutively after Tawaf, similar to how ritual purity (taharah) is sunnah for Tawaf. Consequently, Sa'y is valid from a menstruating woman or someone in janabah, even though their Tawaf would not be valid. Climbing onto Safa and Marwah is Sunnah, and it is disliked to omit it. Walking (not riding) during Sa'y is wajib according to the Hanafi school; if one rides without an excuse, a dam (sacrifice) is required. The Prophet's exiting through Bab al-Safa was simply because it was the nearest, not an established Sunnah, so one may exit from any door. Raising hands in supplication during Sa'y is mandub (recommended). The passage also explains the linguistic and historical origins of the names: Safa from Adam, Marwah from Eve.

Key Terms
السعي (al-sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times, a wajib act of Hajj and Umrah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for certain omissions or violations during Hajj/Umrah.

Preferred Time for Sa'y: Delaying or Early? The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the preferred timing of Sa'y.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the preferred timing of Sa'y for mufrid, mutamatti', and qarin pilgrims, and identify the key authorities supporting each view.

Core Idea
The timing of Sa'y depends on the pilgrim's type: delaying is better for mufrid/mutamatti', but early Sa'y is sunnah for the qarin.

This passage examines an intra-Hanafi debate about whether it is better to perform Sa'y immediately after Tawaf al-Qudum or to delay it until after the obligatory Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The ruling varies based on the pilgrim's type – mufrid, mutamatti', or qarin – and also on whether the pilgrim has performed Tawaf al-Qudum. We will explore the reasoning and the authorities that support each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of pilgrims
Recognize the three types: mufrid (Hajj only), mutamatti' (Umrah then Hajj), and qarin (Hajj and Umrah combined). The ruling differs for each.
The qarin is treated differently – early Sa'y is recommended without dispute.
2
Understand the rationale
Sa'y is wajib, Tawaf al-Ziyarah is rukn. The principle is that a wajib should follow a rukn, not a sunnah. Therefore, delaying Sa'y to after Tawaf al-Ziyarah is logically sound.
Tawaf al-Qudum is sunnah; Tawaf al-Ziyarah is rukn.
3
Recognize the intra-madhhab dispute
Some scholars (e.g., al-Kirmani) prefer early Sa'y for all; others (e.g., author of al-Bada'i') prohibit early Sa'y for those without Tawaf al-Qudum. The majority of ashab allow it but consider delaying better.
The permissibility of early Sa'y is agreed upon for those who have Tawaf al-Qudum; the dispute is about superiority.
4
Note the consensus for the qarin
For the qarin, there is no dispute: early Sa'y is best and even sunnah. The text states: 'as for him, we do not know of any difference'.
This is a key distinguishing point.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that early Sa'y is permissible for all, but for mufrid and mutamatti', delaying is better. The majority of authorities like al-Karkhi, al-Quduri, and the author of al-Hidayah support this.
The mufta bihi balances permissibility and preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي التحفة : الأفضل للحاج أن لا يسعى بعد طواف القدوم لأن السعي واجب لا يليق أن يكون تبعاً للسنة بل يؤخره إلى طواف الزيارة لأنه ركن واللائق للواجب أن يكون تبعاً للفرض. ... وفي التحفة الأفضل للحاج أي المفرد بالحج والمتمتع بخلاف القارن لأنه ذكر في اللباب في الأفضلية خلافاً ثم قال : والخلاف في غير القارن أما القارن فالأفضل له تقديم السعي أو يسن ا هـ . حاشية المدني : اعلم أن السعي الواجب في الحج يدخل وقته عقب طواف الزيارة ويمتد إلى آخر العمرة لأن السعي تبع للطواف والشيء إنما يتبع ما هو أقوى منه والسعي واجب وطواف الزيارة ركن، ويجوز تقديمه على الوقوف وإيقاعه عقب طواف القدوم لكثرة أفعال الحج يوم النحر، لكن يشترط أن يكون في أشهر الحج حتى لمن لا عليه طواف القدوم في الأصح. واختلفوا هل الأفضل تأخيره إلى وقته أم تقديمه؟ وعلى الثاني هل هو عام لأهل مكة وغيرهم أم خاص بغيرهم ممن عليه طواف القدوم؟ وحاصله أن جواز تقديم السعي ممن عليه طواف القدوم متفق عليه، وأما أفضليته ففيها خلاف، وأما جواز لمن أهل من مكة ممن ليس عليه طواف قدوم اختاره غير واحد من المشايخ كالكرخي والقدوري وصاحب الهداية والكافي والنهاية المجمع وغيرهم. أما الأفضلية فصححها الكرماني، وذهب صاحب البدائع إلى عدم جواز التقديم لمن أحرم من مكة وهو خلاف ما عليه أكثر الأصحاب، وهذا الاختلاف كله في غير القارن، وأما هو فلا نعلم خلافاً في أفضلية تقديم السعي الجواز لأنهم ما ذكروا له إلا التقديم من غير ذكر خلاف بل الآثار تدل على استنان تقديم قول المصنف : ساعياً بين الميلين الأخضرين) يستحب السعي له . كذا في المرشدي وغيره ا هـ .
And in al-Tuhfah: It is better for the pilgrim (i.e., the one performing Hajj ifrad and the mutamatti') not to perform Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum, because Sa'y is wajib and it is not appropriate for it to be subordinate to a sunnah; rather he should delay it until Tawaf al-Ziyarah because it is a rukn, and it is fitting for the wajib to be subordinate to the fard. ... And in al-Tuhfah: The best for the pilgrim, i.e., the mufrid and the mutamatti', contrary to the qarin, because he mentioned in al-Lubab regarding superiority a difference. Then he said: The difference is for other than the qarin; as for the qarin, the best for him is to perform Sa'y early or it is sunnah. End. Hashiyah al-Madani: Know that the time for the obligatory Sa'y in Hajj enters after Tawaf al-Ziyarah and extends to the end of one's lifetime, because Sa'y is subordinate to Tawaf, and a thing follows what is stronger than it; Sa'y is wajib and Tawaf al-Ziyarah is rukn. It is permissible to perform it before standing at Arafah and after Tawaf al-Qudum due to the many acts of Hajj on the Day of Sacrifice, but it is a condition that it be in the months of Hajj, even for one who does not have Tawaf al-Qudum, according to the most sound opinion. They differed: is it better to delay it to its time or to perform it early? And on the second view, is it general for the people of Mecca and others or specific to others who have Tawaf al-Qudum? The summary is that permissibility of performing Sa'y early for one who has Tawaf al-Qudum is agreed upon; as for its superiority, there is difference. As for permissibility for one who entered ihram from Mecca who does not have Tawaf al-Qudum, more than one of the mashayikh chose it, such as al-Karkhi, al-Quduri, the author of al-Hidayah, al-Kafi, al-Nihayah al-Mujma', and others. As for superiority, al-Kirmani declared it correct, and the author of al-Bada'i' went to the impermissibility of early Sa'y for one who entered ihram from Mecca, which is contrary to what most of the ashab hold. This difference is all for other than the qarin; as for him, we do not know of any difference regarding the superiority of early Sa'y for permissibility, because they only mentioned early Sa'y for him without mentioning any difference; rather the athar indicate that early Sa'y is sunnah. The words of the author: "Walking quickly between the two green markers"—it is recommended to walk quickly in it. Thus in al-Murshidi and others.
Source pages p. 583

Commentary
This passage deals with the preferred timing of Sa'y. The author of al-Tuhfah argues that it is better for a mufrid or mutamatti' not to perform Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum (the arrival Tawaf), because Sa'y is wajib and should follow a rukn (Tawaf al-Ziyarah) rather than a sunnah act. For the qarin (who combines Hajj and Umrah), the best is to perform Sa'y early, and it is even considered sunnah. The hashiah of al-Madani explains that the time for Sa'y technically begins after Tawaf al-Ziyarah, but it is permissible to perform it earlier (after Tawaf al-Qudum) provided it is within the months of Hajj, even for those who do not have Tawaf al-Qudum (like residents of Mecca who do not perform a separate arrival Tawaf). There is ikhtilaf among scholars: some prioritize delaying Sa'y to its original time, others prioritize early Sa'y. For those entering ihram from Mecca (who have no Tawaf al-Qudum), many authorities like al-Karkhi and al-Quduri allow early Sa'y, while the author of al-Bada'i' prohibits it for them, but the majority allow it. For the qarin, there is no dispute that early Sa'y is recommended.

Key Terms
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The arrival Tawaf performed upon entering Mecca, which is sunnah for those coming from outside.
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory Tawaf of Hajj performed on the Day of Sacrifice or subsequent days, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For which type of pilgrim is early Sa'y (after Tawaf al-Qudum) considered best or sunnah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Mufrid
B) Mutamatti'
C) Qarin
D) A pilgrim who entered ihram from Mecca

Key Takeaway
For mufrid and mutamatti', delaying Sa'y until after Tawaf al-Ziyarah is better; for the qarin, early Sa'y is sunnah.

Method of Sa'y and Ruling on Starting with Marwah
Describing the proper method of Sa'y and the dispute when one starts with Marwah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi views on starting Sa'y with Marwah and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Starting Sa'y with Marwah is a condition (shart) for validity according to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

The Prophet ﷺ began Sa'y from Safa and commanded us to begin with what Allah began with. Hanafi scholars agree on the importance of starting from Safa, but they differ on the consequence of beginning with Marwah. Some say it invalidates the Sa'y, others say it is sinful but valid, and a third group considers it merely sunnah. This lesson unpacks this intra-Hanafi dispute and the evidence behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
Confirm that Sa'y must start from Safa and that this is wajib based on the hadith 'Begin with what Allah began with.'
2
List the three scholarly positions
State the three views: (1) condition (shart) – invalid if violated, (2) wajib – valid but sinful, (3) sunnah – no sin.
These are all within the Hanafi school.
3
Analyze the evidence for each view
The hadith imperative indicates wujub in Hanafi usul, but some scholars consider the imperative strong enough to make it a condition; others see it as merely recommended.
The text notes that the correct view (according to the commentator) is that it is wajib, but the author of al-Lubab treats it as a condition.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
Identify that al-Lubab and al-Bada'i' consider it a condition, meaning if one starts with Marwah, the Sa'y is invalid.
The commentator of al-Lubab prefers the wajib view, but the text does not give a final tarjih; however, the mufta bihi is often taken as the condition view.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Practice: If a pilgrim begins Sa'y at Marwah, what is the effect under each view? Under the mufta bihi, the Sa'y must be restarted from Safa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اهبط نحو المروة ساعياً بين الميلين الأخضرين وافعل عليها فعلك على الصفا) أي على المروة من الصعود والتكبير والتهليل والصلاة والدعاء، والكل سنة . لو ترك الهرولة بين الميلين لا شيء عليه وهما شيئان على شكل الميلين منحوتان من نفس جدار المسجد الحرام إلا أنهما منفصلان عنه، وهما علامتان لموضع الهرولة في ممر بطن الوادي بين الصفا والمروة. كذا في المغرب قوله : (وطف) بينهما سبعة أشواط تبدأ بالصفا وتختم بالمروة) صح في حديث جابر الطويل. وقوله تبدأ بالصفا» بيان للواجب حتى لو بدأ بالمروة لا يعتد بالأول الصحيح لمخالفة الأمر وهو قوله عليه السلام «ابدؤوا بما بدأ الله به»(۱). وإشارة إلى أن الذهاب إلى المروة شوط والعود منها إلى الصفا شوط آخر وهو الصحيح لما صح في حديث جابر أنه قال : فلما كان آخر طوافه على المروة. ولو كان من الصفا إلى الصفا شوطاً لكان آخر طوافه الصفا. ونقل الشارح عن الطحاوي أن الذهاب من الصفا إلى المروة شوط. قوله : (بدأ بالمروة لا يعتد بالأول هذا يفيد أن البداءة بالمروة شرط لا أنه واجب وهو أحد أقوال ثلاثة فإنه قيل إنه شرط، وقيل واجب، وقيل سنة، ومشى في اللباب على الأول. وقال : شارحه : الأعدل المختار من حيث الدليل الوجوب فيصح أداؤه لكن يعاقب عليه دون عقاب ترك الفرض، وعلى الأولى لا يصح وتمام تحقيقه هناك . تنبيه : عد في اللباب تبعاً للبدائع من شرائط السعي كونه بعد طواف كائن على طهارة من الجنابة والحيض فإن لم يكن طاهراً عنهما وقت الطواف لم يجز سعيه رأساً. واستشكاه شارحه بأن الطهارة ليست من شرائط صحة الطواف فكيف تكون شرطاً فيه بل الشرط وقوعه عقيب طواف بعد طواف كامل مشتمل على أداء واجباته وتمامه فيه فراجعه .
Then descend towards al-Marwah, walking quickly between the two green markers, and do upon it (al-Marwah) the same as you did upon al-Safa (i.e., of climbing, takbir, tahlil, prayer, and supplication). All of it is sunnah. If one omits the hastening between the two markers, there is nothing upon him. They are two things in the shape of two markers carved from the same wall of the Sacred Mosque but separate from it, and they are markers for the place of hastening in the path of the valley bottom between Safa and Marwah. Thus in al-Mughrib. His saying: "And perform" (i.e., the circumambulation) between them seven circuits, beginning with Safa and ending with Marwah. It is confirmed in the lengthy hadith of Jabir. His saying "beginning with Safa" is a statement of the obligatory (wajib), such that if one begins with Marwah, the first (circuit) is not counted according to the correct view, due to opposing the command: the Prophet's saying, "Begin with what Allah began with." And it indicates that going to Marwah is one circuit and returning from it to Safa is another circuit—this is the correct view, as confirmed in the hadith of Jabir where he said: "When his last circuit was upon Marwah." If going from Safa to Safa were a circuit, his last circuit would have been Safa. The commentator narrated from al-Tahawi that going from Safa to Marwah is one circuit. His saying: "If he begins with Marwah, the first (circuit) is not counted"—this indicates that beginning with Marwah is a condition (shart), not just wajib. This is one of three statements: it is said it is a condition, it is said it is wajib, and it is said it is sunnah. The author of al-Lubab proceeded on the first view. His commentator said: The most just and chosen view in light of the evidence is that it is wajib, so the deed is valid but he is punished, unlike the punishment for leaving a fard. On the first view, it is not sound. The full investigation is there. Caution: In al-Lubab, following al-Bada'i', it is counted among the conditions of Sa'y that it be after a Tawaf that occurred in a state of purity from major impurity (janabah) and menstruation. If he was not pure from them at the time of Tawaf, his Sa'y is not valid at all. His commentator objected that purity is not a condition for the validity of Tawaf itself, so how can it be a condition for Sa'y? Rather, the condition is that the Sa'y occur after a complete Tawaf that includes fulfilling its obligations, and its completion is there. So refer to it.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed method of Sa'y. After reaching Marwah, one does the same as on Safa (climbing, takbir, etc.)—all sunnah. The hastening (harwalah) between the two green markers is sunnah; leaving it incurs no penalty. The markers are physical indicators in the valley. The text emphasizes that Sa'y consists of seven circuits starting at Safa and ending at Marwah. The command to begin with Safa is wajib; if one starts with Marwah, the first circuit is not counted according to the correct view. This is supported by the hadith "Begin with what Allah began with." There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say starting with Marwah is a condition (if violated, Sa'y is invalid), some say it is wajib (valid but sinful), and some say it is sunnah (no sin). The author of al-Lubab considers it a condition, but the commentator prefers the view of wajib. Finally, a note from al-Lubab adds that a condition for Sa'y is that the preceding Tawaf be performed in a state of purity from janabah and menstruation. However, the commentator objects that purity is not a condition for Tawaf itself, so it cannot be a condition for Sa'y. The correct condition is simply that Sa'y be after a complete Tawaf fulfilling its obligations, not necessarily with purity.

Key Terms
هرولة (harwalah): A brisk walking pace between the two green markers during Sa'y; it is sunnah.
الميلين الأخضرين (al-milayn al-akhdarayn): Two green markers set in the wall of the Sacred Mosque indicating where hastening occurs in the valley bottom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the view that starting with Marwah is a condition, what is the effect on the Sa'y?
A) The Sa'y is valid but sinful
B) The first circuit is invalid, but the rest are valid
C) The entire Sa'y is invalid
D) No effect, it is merely disliked

Key Takeaway
The correct view in the Hanafi school is that beginning Sa'y with Marwah invalidates the Sa'y, as it is a condition (shart) for validity.

Rulings of Sa'y: Laps, Starting Point, and Walking Between Markers
Explains obligations and sunan of sa'y, including lap definition and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the definition of a sa'y lap, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the correct counting method.

Core Idea
A sa'y lap is each half-trip between Safa and Marwah, not a full round-trip like tawaf.

The ritual sa'y between Safa and Marwah is a wajib component of Hajj and Umrah. While the basic sequence is well-known, there is a subtle but important dispute within the Hanafi school about what constitutes a 'lap' (shawi) and about the nature of beginning at Safa. This lesson examines these disputes, the supporting evidence, and the practical implications for a pilgrim's performance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on lap definition
Identify the relied-upon view that each half-trip (Safa→Marwah or Marwah→Safa) counts as one lap. Note that seven laps are required, ending at Marwah.
This is based on the hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) ended his sa'y on Marwah.
2
Identify the opposing intra-Hanafi view
State that al-Tahawi and some others consider only the trip from Safa to Marwah as a lap; the return is not counted separately.
This view is recorded in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya and relies on qiyas with tawaf.
3
Analyse the opposing proof
Examine the qiyas argument: tawaf has laps that start and end at the Black Stone, so sa'y should have laps that start and end at Safa.
The opposing school uses the analogy of tawaf for the definition of a lap.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand Ibn al-Humam's linguistic distinction: tawaf is circular (dawaran), so a lap must return to the start; sa'y is linear (qat' masafa), so each straight leg is a complete lap. The hadith confirms this.
The Hanafi response highlights the difference between rotational and linear movement.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if one counts only Safa→Marwah trips, he would perform only 3.5 laps. The correct, mufta bihi view is each half-trip is a lap.
Also, beginning with Safa is wajib (not shart) per the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فوق الرمل دون العدو أي الجري الشديد، وهو سنة في كل شوط بخلاف الرمل في الطواف خلافاً لمن خصه أيضاً بالثلاثة الأول، ولا اضطباع في السعي مطلقاً عندنا. ولو ترك السعي بين الميلين أو هرول في جميع السعي فقد أساء ولا شيء عليه ويلبي في السعي الحاج أي إن وقع سعيه بعد طواف القدوم لا المعتمر ولو كان متمتعاً لأن تلبيته تنقطع بالشروع في طوافه ولا الحاج إذا سعى بعد طواف الإفاضة لانقطاع تلبيته بأول رمي جمرة. وإن
