صحيح
(۱) رواه أبو داود في كتاب المناسك باب ٥٦ الترمذي في كتاب الحج باب ۳۸. النسائي في كتاب الحج باب ١٦١، ١٦٦. الموطأ في كتاب الحج حديث ١٢٦.

كتاب الحج باب الإحرام
بالمروة ثم أقم بمكة حراماً لأنك محرم بالحج فطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك ثم اخطب قبل والرجوع منها إلى الصفا شوط قياساً على الطواف فإنه من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية ما يخالفه فإنه قال : لا خلاف بين أصحابنا أن الذهاب من الصفا إلى المروة شوط محسوب من الأشواط السبعة فأما الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا هل هو شوط آخر؟ قال الطحاوي : لا يعتبر الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا شوطاً آخر والصحيح أنه شوط آخر وفرق المحقق ابن الهمام بين الطوافين بالفرق لغة بين طاف كذا وكذا سبعاً الصادق بالتردد من كل من الغايتين إلى الأخرى سبعاً وبين طاف بكذا فإن حقيقته متوقفة على أن يشمل بالطواف ذلك الشيء، فإذا قال طاف به سبعاً كان بتكرير تعميمه بالطواف سبعاً فمن هنا افترق الحال بين الطواف بالبيت حيث لزم في شوطه كونه من المبدأ إلى المبدأ والطواف
اهـ.
مما
قوله : (وفرق المحقق الخ) وفي العناية : فإن قيل ما الفرق بين الطواف والسعي حتى كان مبدأ الطواف هو المنتهى دون السعي؟ أجيب بأن الطواف دوران لا يتأتى إلا بحركة دورية فيكون المبدأ والمنتهى واحداً بالضرورة، وأما السعي فهو قطع مسافة بحركة مستقيمة وذلك لا يقتضي عوده على بدئه
The two green markers, and do upon it what you did on Safa, and perform seven laps between them beginning with Safa and ending with Marwah, following the obligatory. Then He said: (then descend towards Marwah walking quickly between the two green markers and do upon it what you did on Safa) meaning on Marwah of ascending, takbir, tahlil, prayer, and supplication, and all are sunnah. If he leaves the quick walking between the two markers, nothing is upon him. They are two things shaped like two mile markers carved from the wall of the Sacred Mosque but separate from it, and they are markers for the place of quick walking in the path of the valley bottom between Safa and Marwah. Thus in al-Mughrib. He said: (and perform seven laps between them beginning with Safa and ending with Marwah) is sound in the long hadith of Jabir. And His saying 'begin with Safa' is an explanation of the obligatory, such that if he began with Marwah, the first is not counted according to the correct view due to opposing the command, which is his saying peace be upon him: 'Begin with what Allah began with.' And it is an indication that going to Marwah is a lap and returning from it to Safa is another lap, and that is the correct view because of the hadith of Jabir where he said: 'When his last lap was on Marwah.' Were it that from Safa to Safa was a lap, his last lap would be Safa. The commentator narrated from al-Tahawi that going from Safa to Marwah is [incomplete], let alone from the companions, and this difference all is for other than the qarin. As for him, we know no disagreement on the preferability of delaying the sa'y for permissibility because they only mentioned for him the delay without mention of disagreement, rather the traditions indicate the recommendation of delay. The author's saying: 'walking quickly between the two green markers' indicates that sa'y is recommended for him? Thus in al-Murshidi and others. And it is that the sa'y is above walking and below running, i.e., intense jogging, and it is sunnah in every lap, contrary to ramal in tawaf, contrary to those who also specified it for the first three, and there is no idtiba' in sa'y absolutely according to us. If he leaves the walking between the two markers or jogs in the entire sa'y, he has done wrong and nothing is upon him. And he makes talbiyah during sa'y, the pilgrim, i.e., if his sa'y occurs after tawaf al-qudum, not the mu'tamir, even if he is mutamatti', because his talbiyah is cut by beginning his tawaf, nor the pilgrim if he performs sa'y after tawaf al-ifadah because his talbiyah is cut by the first stone's throw. If he is unable to walk between the two markers, he waits until he finds a gap, otherwise he mimics the walker in his movement. If he is on a mount for an excuse, he moves it without harming anyone. The chapter and its commentary: His saying: (if he begins with Marwah, the first is not counted) this indicates that beginning with Marwah is a condition, not obligatory, and it is one of three opinions: it is said it is a condition, obligatory, or sunnah. In al-Lubab he followed the first. Its commentator said: the most just and chosen from the proof is obligation, so it is validly performed but he is punished without punishment of leaving a fard. According to the first, it is not valid. Its full investigation is there. Note: In al-Lubab he counted, following al-Bada'i', among the conditions of sa'y that it be after tawaf that was performed in a state of purity from major impurity and menstruation. If he was not pure from them at the time of tawaf, his sa'y is not valid at all. Its commentator objected that purity is not a condition for the validity of tawaf, so how can it be a condition for it? Rather the condition is that it occurs after a tawaf that is complete and includes the performance of its obligations. Its completion is in it, so refer to it. Sound. (1) Reported by Abu Dawud in Kitab al-Manasik, Bab 56; al-Tirmidhi in Kitab al-Hajj, Bab 38; al-Nasa'i in Kitab al-Hajj, Bab 161, 166; al-Muwatta' in Kitab al-Hajj, Hadith 126. Book of Hajj, Chapter of Ihram. By Marwah then remain in Mecca as a muhrim because you are muhrim for Hajj, so perform tawaf of the House whenever you wish, then deliver a sermon before, and return from it to Safa is a lap by analogy to tawaf, because it is from the Black Stone to the Black Stone (for a lap). In al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, something contrary, for he said: There is no disagreement among our companions that going from Safa to Marwah is a lap counted among the seven laps. As for returning from Marwah to Safa, is it another lap? Al-Tahawi said: The return from Marwah to Safa is not considered another lap. The correct view is that it is another lap. And the investigator Ibn al-Humam distinguished between the two tawafs by the linguistic difference between 'he performed tawaf of such-and-such seven times' which applies to the back-and-forth from each endpoint to the other seven times, and 'he performed tawaf of something' whose reality depends on encompassing that thing with tawaf. So if he says 'he performed tawaf around it seven times', it is by repeating his encompassing of it by tawaf seven times. Hence the distinction arises between tawaf of the House where it is necessary in its lap that it be from the start to the start, and tawaf... end. He said: (And the investigator differentiated...) In al-'Inayah: If it is said: What is the difference between tawaf and sa'y such that the start of tawaf is the finish, unlike sa'y? The answer: Tawaf is a rotation that cannot occur except by circular movement, so the start and finish are necessarily the same. As for sa'y, it is traversing a distance by straight movement, and that does not require returning to its start.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains the rulings of sa'y in detail. The text begins by explaining the acts performed on Safa and Marwah (ascending, takbir, tahlil, prayer, supplication) and states that all are sunnah. It then discusses the two green markers (al-milayn al-akhdarayn) that indicate the area where quick walking (harwalah) is prescribed. The ruling: if one leaves the harwalah, there is no penalty; it is a sunnah, not obligatory. The markers are physically carved from the wall of the Masjid al-Haram but separate, marking the path in the bottom of the valley. The core of the passage addresses the obligation of beginning sa'y with Safa and the definition of a lap (shawi). The matn states that one must perform seven laps beginning with Safa and ending with Marwah. The commentary clarifies that beginning with Safa is wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith 'Begin with what Allah began with' (referring to the Quranic order mentioning Safa first). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars consider beginning with Marwah a condition (shart) that invalidates the lap if violated, while others say it is wajib (so the lap is valid but sinful), and a third view considers it sunnah. The preferred view (as per the commentator of al-Lubab) is wajib. Another dispute concerns the definition of a lap: Is each trip from Safa to Marwah a lap, or does a lap include the return trip as well? The correct Hanafi position, based on the hadith that the Prophet ended his sa'y on Marwah, is that each half-trip (Safa to Marwah and Marwah to Safa) counts as one lap, making seven total. This is supported by Ibn al-Humam's linguistic distinction: tawaf (circumambulation) is circular, so a lap returns to the start; sa'y is straight-line movement, so each leg is a lap. The text also discusses related issues: the speed of sa'y (above normal walking, below running, sunnah in every lap), prohibition of idtiba' (wrapping the upper garment under the right armpit) in sa'y, talbiyah during sa'y (applicable only for the pilgrim after tawaf al-qudum, not for mu'tamir or after tawaf al-ifadah), and the conditional purity requirement for the preceding tawaf (a condition for sa'y per al-Bada'i', disputed by the commentator). The passage is a thorough exposition of the legal details of sa'y, including evidence and disagreements within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times as part of Hajj or Umrah.
هرولة (harwalah): A brisk walking pace between the two green markers, faster than normal walking but less than running.
ميلين (al-milayn): Two markers shaped like mile pillars, carved from the mosque wall, indicating the area for harwalah.
شوط (shawi): A lap or single leg of the sa'y between Safa and Marwah (or vice versa).
اضطباع (idtiba'): Wrapping the upper garment under the right armpit, leaving the right shoulder bare.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim begins the sa'y at Marwah instead of Safa, what is the ruling according to the preferred view in the passage?
A) The sa'y is invalid and must be restarted from Safa.
B) The first lap is not counted, but the sa'y is valid and he must repeat that lap.
C) It is permissible and no penalty.
D) He must offer a sacrifice (dam).

Key Takeaway
A sa'y lap is each half-trip between Safa and Marwah; the correct performance begins at Safa, ends at Marwah, and includes seven laps, with quick walking between the green markers as sunnah.

Prayer After Sa'y and the Distance of the Sa'y
Dispute over prayer after sa'y and dimensions of the Mas'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the prayer after sa'y and identify the historical measurements of the sa'y path.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer after sa'y was tahiyyah al-masjid, not a specific sunnah; the Mas'a measured 750 cubits in length.

This lesson examines two distinct but related issues from the sa'y rituals: the debated prayer after sa'y and the physical dimensions of the Mas'a. Understanding these clarifies Hanafi methodology in interpreting prophetic actions and the importance of precise measurements for the validity of the ritual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the debated action
The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after completing sa'y, as narrated by al-Muttalib. The question is whether this was a specific sunnah for sa'y or a general greeting of the mosque (tahiyyah).
2
Examine the two interpretations
Some scholars, including the narrator, understood the prayer to be for sa'y. Others, like al-Qari and al-Murshidi, interpret it as tahiyyah al-masjid.
3
Analyze the Hanafi argument
The Hanafi position argues that the prayer was tahiyyah because the Prophet entered the mosque after sa'y and did not intend tawaf. The greeting of Masjid al-Haram is tawaf, but if one does not intend tawaf, tahiyyah prayer is offered.
4
Consider the narrator's perspective
The narrator assumed the prayer was for sa'y due to the timing, but the Hanafi response holds that this does not determine the ruling; the action itself is ambiguous.
5
Determine the mufta bihi view
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that there is no specific prayer for sa'y. Any prayer after sa'y should be performed with the intention of tahiyyah al-masjid, at an appropriate time.

He said: (Because Ahmad narrated - al-Fath said: al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'a narrated: I saw the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, after finishing his sa'y, came until he was parallel to the Rukn (corner) and prayed two rak'ahs on the edge of the mataf, with no one between him and the tawaf performers. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq continues the commentary on sa'y, now addressing two issues: (1) whether there is a specific recommended prayer after completing sa'y, and (2) the measured distance of the sa'y area. The author cites a hadith from al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'a that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after sa'y near the Black Stone. However, scholars debate the interpretation of this action. Al-Qari argues that this prayer is not specifically for sa'y but rather tahiyyah al-masjid (greeting the mosque), because the Prophet entered the mosque after sa'y and may have prayed to greet it. Others, like al-Murshidi, support this view, noting that the prayer is more likely tahiyyah because the specific greeting of the Masjid al-Haram is tawaf, not prayer. The author (Ibn Nujaym) seems to lean towards the view that the prayer was indeed for sa'y, citing that the narrator understood it as such. The passage notes that there is no intrinsic conflict, but caution is required. The second part provides the physical dimensions of the Mas'a (the area of sa'y). According to al-Murshidi, the length from Safa to Marwah is 750 cubits, making the total distance for seven laps 5,250 cubits. Another source (al-Shumnuni) gives 766 cubits per leg. The width is 35 cubits as per al-Fakihi. The author ends with a note about a 'great difficulty' that requires further investigation.

Key Terms
صلاة السعي (salat al-sa'y): A prayer performed after completing the sa'y, whose status is debated.
تحية المسجد (tahiyyah al-masjid): A two-rak'ah prayer performed upon entering a mosque as a greeting.
المسعى (al-Mas'a): The path between Safa and Marwah where the sa'y is performed.
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit, an ancient unit of length approximately 45-50 cm.

C) It was a prayer of thanks (shukr) for completing sa'y.
D) It is a nafl prayer with no specific ruling.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that there is no specific prayer for sa'y; any prayer after sa'y should be intended as tahiyyah al-masjid, performed at a permissible time.

The Return Lap from Marwah to Safa in Sa'y
Intra-Hanafi dispute on counting the return lap in Sa'y

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two positions within the Hanafi school on counting the return from Marwah to Safa in Sa'y, state the mufta bihi position, and explain the linguistic and analogical reasoning behind it.

Core Idea
The return from Marwah to Safa is a separate lap—Hanafi majority counts it, al-Tahawi does not, mufta bihi says yes.

This lesson examines a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the return journey from Marwah to Safa during Sa'y counts as one of the seven required laps. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correct performance of Hajj or Umrah. We will analyze the arguments from both sides and the reasoning that leads to the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the exact point of disagreement: does the return from Marwah to Safa constitute a separate lap (shaut) in the seven laps of Sa'y?
All Hanafis agree the outward (Safa to Marwah) is a lap.
2
Identify the majority position and its proof
The majority Hanafis hold that the return is a separate lap. Their proof is qiyas to Tawaf (where each lap goes from Black Stone to Black Stone) and linguistic analysis: Sa'y is linear, so each traversal is a distinct lap.
Refer to the analogy in the text: 'قياساً على الطواف'.
3
Identify al-Tahawi's opposing view
Al-Tahawi held that the return is not a separate lap; the seven laps consist only of outward journeys. The returns are merely transitional.
Al-Tahawi is an early Hanafi authority; his view is recorded but not mufta bihi.
4
Understand the linguistic distinction by Ibn al-Humam
Ibn al-Humam distinguishes between Tawaf (circular, start=end) and Sa'y (linear, each direction is a distinct motion). Hence the return is a separate lap in Sa'y.
This distinction is quoted from Al-Inayah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical difference: if a pilgrim misses a return lap, under the majority view the Sa'y is incomplete and must be corrected; under al-Tahawi's view it would be complete. The mufta bihi is the majority view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالمروة ثم أقم بمكة حراماً لأنك محرم بالحج فطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك ثم اخطب قبل والرجوع منها إلى الصفا شوط قياساً على الطواف فإنه من الحجر إلى الحجر شوط. وفي الفتاوى الظهيرية ما يخالفه فإنه قال : لا خلاف بين أصحابنا أن الذهاب من الصفا إلى المروة شوط محسوب من الأشواط السبعة فأما الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا هل هو شوط آخر؟ قال الطحاوي : لا يعتبر الرجوع من المروة إلى الصفا شوطاً آخر والصحيح أنه شوط آخر وفرق المحقق ابن الهمام بين الطوافين بالفرق لغة بين طاف كذا وكذا سبعاً الصادق بالتردد من كل من الغايتين إلى الأخرى سبعاً وبين طاف بكذا فإن حقيقته متوقفة على أن يشمل بالطواف ذلك الشيء، فإذا قال طاف به سبعاً كان بتكرير تعميمه بالطواف سبعاً فمن هنا افترق الحال بين الطواف بالبيت حيث لزم في شوطه كونه من المبدأ إلى المبدأ والطواف. قوله : (وفرق المحقق الخ) وفي العناية : فإن قيل ما الفرق بين الطواف والسعي حتى كان مبدأ الطواف هو المنتهى دون السعي؟ أجيب بأن الطواف دوران لا يتأتى إلا بحركة دورية فيكون المبدأ والمنتهى واحداً بالضرورة، وأما السعي فهو قطع مسافة بحركة مستقيمة وذلك لا يقتضي عوده على بدئه
With Marwah then reside in Makkah in ihram because you are in ihram for Hajj, so perform Tawaf around the House whenever it appears to you, then deliver a sermon before, and the return from it (Marwah) to Safa is a lap by analogy to Tawaf, for indeed from the Stone to the Stone is a lap. In Al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyyah there is something contradicting it, for it said: There is no disagreement among our companions that going from Safa to Marwah is a lap counted among the seven laps; as for the return from Marwah to Safa, is it another lap? Al-Tahawi said: The return from Marwah to Safa is not considered another lap, and the correct view is that it is another lap. And the researcher Ibn al-Humam distinguished between the two Tawafs by the linguistic difference between 'he performed Tawaf such-and-such seven times,' which is true of going back and forth from each of the two endpoints to the other seven times, and 'he performed Tawaf with something,' for its reality depends on encompassing that thing with Tawaf. So when one says 'he performed Tawaf with it seven times,' it is by repeating its encompassing with Tawaf seven times. Hence the situation differs between Tawaf of the House, where it is necessary in its lap to be from the starting point to the starting point, and Tawaf. His statement: (And the researcher distinguished, etc.) And in Al-Inayah: for if it is said: What is the difference between Tawaf and Sa'y such that the start of Tawaf is the end, unlike Sa'y? It is answered: Tawaf is a rotation that can only be achieved by circular motion, so the start and end are necessarily the same. As for Sa'y, it is covering a distance by rectilinear motion, and that does not require returning to its start.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of laps (ashwat) in Sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The base text (matn) initially rules that the return from Marwah to Safa counts as a lap, by analogy to Tawaf where each lap goes from the Black Stone back to the Black Stone. The author then cites Al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyyah, which clarifies that all Hanafis agree the outward journey (Safa to Marwah) is one lap, but they differ on the return journey. Al-Tahawi held that the return is not a separate lap, implying the seven laps consist of the outward journeys only, but the correct position (as per the author) is that the return is also a lap, making the total seven complete back-and-forth trips. The researcher Ibn al-Humam linguistic distinction between Tawaf and Sa'y is then presented: Tawaf is circular, requiring the start and end to coincide, while Sa'y is linear, so the return journey naturally counts as a distinct lap. The commentary from Al-Inayah reinforces this by contrasting circular Tawaf with rectilinear Sa'y.

Key Terms
شوط (shaut): A single lap in Sa'y or Tawaf, defined by the distance between two points.
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times, part of Hajj and Umrah.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah; each circuit from the Black Stone back to it is one shaut.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning, a method of deriving rulings by comparing a new case to an established case sharing the same effective cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It is counted only if the pilgrim is a non-Makki.
D) It is optional; one may choose to count it or not.

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position counts the return from Marwah to Safa as a separate lap, making the Sa'y seven complete traversals; al-Tahawi's minority view is not followed.

Is There a Recommended Prayer After Sa'y?
Ruling with proof and scholarly debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on praying after Sa'y and evaluate the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
The Prophet's prayer after Sa'y may be a greeting of the mosque, not a specific Sa'y prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines whether there is a mustahabb prayer after completing the Sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The author presents a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ praying two rak'ahs after Sa'y, but some scholars argue it was merely tahiyyat al-masjid. The discussion highlights how a single action can be interpreted differently based on context and intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act in question is praying two rak'ahs after completing Sa'y. The dispute is whether this prayer is specifically recommended for Sa'y or is a general greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid).
The dispute is intra-Hanafi and also involves Shafi'i scholars.
2
Examine the primary evidence
The hadith of al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'ah explicitly states the Prophet prayed after finishing Sa'y. The wording 'when he finished his Sa'y' and 'prayed two rak'ahs' suggests a connection to Sa'y.
The hadith is ahad (single-narrator) so its thubut is zanni.
3
Consider the counter-argument
Al-Qari and al-Marshidi argue the prayer was tahiyyat al-masjid, not for Sa'y. In Masjid al-Haram, the greeting is Tawaf, but if unable, one prays tahiyyat. The Prophet entered the mosque after Sa'y and greeted it.
This interpretation relies on the principle that the greeting of the Haram is Tawaf, not prayer, unless there is an impediment.
4
Analyze the author's preference
The author leans toward the narrator's understanding that it was for Sa'y, questioning why one would deviate from the apparent meaning. The author also notes al-Qari's view but seems to favor the literal reading.
The author uses the phrase 'al-mutabādir' (the apparent meaning) to support the recommendation.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that it is mustahabb to pray two rak'ahs after Sa'y, based on the hadith. However, there is a valid intra-Hanafi difference of opinion.
Some later Hanafis like al-Saruji and al-Marshidi hold that there is no specific prayer for Sa'y.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (لما رواه أحمد قال في الفتح: روى المطلب بن أبي وداعة قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حين فرغ من سعيه جاء حتى إذا حاذى الركن فصلى ركعتين في حاشية المطاف وليس بينه وبين الطائفين أحد . رواه أحمد ابن ماجه وابن حبان. وقال في روايته : رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي حذو الركن الأسود والرجال والنساء يمرون بين يديه ما بينهم وبينه سترة. وعنه أنه رآه عليه السلام يصلي يلي باب بني سهم والناس يمرون الخ. وباب بني سهم هو الذي يقال له اليوم باب العمرة، لكن على هذا لا يكون حذو الركن الأسود والله أعلم بحقيقة الحال ا.هـ. ونازعه القاري في شرح اللباب بأنه لا دلالة في الحديث أن هذ الصلاة من مستحبات السعي لاحتمال أن تكون لتحية المسجد حين أراد أن يقعد من غير قصد له إلى طواف. وقال الشيخ حنيف الدين المرشدي في شرحه عليه بعد قول السروجي في منسكه ليس للسعي صلاة أقول : وهو الظاهر الذي يميل إليه الخاطر، وما تقدم من صلاته عليه الصلاة والسلام فمحمول على تحية المسجد لا أنها للسعي وذلك لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام ما أحب حال دخوله إليه أن يخليه من التحية فحياه بها وحيث كان دخوله عقيب السعي وفعل ذلك اشتبه الحال على من راه ا هـ. كذا في حاشية المدني. أقول : لكن ذكر القاري في شرحه أن تحية هذ المسجد الشريف بخصوصه هو الطواف إلا إذا كان له مانع فحينئذ يصلي تحية المسجد إن لم يكن وقت كراهية الصلاة ا.هـ. والمتبادر من فعله عليه السلام ما فهمه الراوي من أ أن صلاته للسعي فما الداعي إلى العدول عنه مع ما علمته تأمل.
His statement: (Because of what Ahmad narrated said in Al-Fath: Al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'ah narrated, he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ when he finished his Sa'y, he came until when he was parallel to the corner, he prayed two rak'ahs on the edge of the Mataf, with no one between him and those performing Tawaf. Ahmad, Ibn Majah, and Ibn Hibban narrated it. And he said in his narration: I saw the Messenger of Allah ﷺ praying opposite the Black Stone while men and women passed in front of him with no screen between them and him. And from him that he saw him ﷺ praying near the door of Banu Sahm while people passed, etc. And the door of Banu Sahm is the one today called Bab al-Umrah, but on this, it would not be opposite the Black Stone, and Allah knows best the reality of the situation. End. And Al-Qari contested it in Sharh al-Lubab, saying there is no evidence in the hadith that this prayer is among the recommended acts of Sa'y, because it could have been the greeting of the mosque when he intended to sit without intending Tawaf. And Shaykh Hanif al-Din al-Marshidi said in his commentary on it after the statement of al-Saruji in his Mansak: 'There is no prayer for Sa'y.' I say: That is the apparent view to which the mind inclines, and what preceded of his ﷺ prayer is carried on greeting the mosque, not that it is for Sa'y, because when he entered, he did not want to leave it without greeting, so he greeted it, and since his entry was immediately after Sa'y and he did that, the situation became ambiguous for the one who saw it. End. Similarly in the gloss of al-Madani. I say: But Al-Qari mentioned in his commentary that the greeting of this noble mosque specifically is Tawaf unless there is an impediment, in which case one prays the greeting of the mosque if it is not a time when prayer is disliked. End. And the apparent meaning from his action is what the narrator understood, that his prayer was for Sa'y, so what reason is there to deviate from it, given what you know? Reflect.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage discusses whether there is a recommended (mustahabb) prayer after completing the Sa'y between Safa and Marwah. The author cites a hadith narrated by Ahmad and others, where al-Muttalib ibn Abi Wada'ah saw the Prophet ﷺ pray two rak'ahs after Sa'y near the corner of the Ka'bah. However, some scholars like al-Qari and al-Marshidi argue that this prayer was not specifically for Sa'y but rather a greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid), since the Prophet entered the mosque after Sa'y and prayed the greeting. Al-Marshidi supports the view of al-Saruji, who stated that there is no prayer for Sa'y. On the other hand, the author leans towards the understanding of the narrator that the prayer was indeed for Sa'y, questioning why one would deviate from that apparent meaning. Thus, the passage presents the difference of opinion, with the author favoring the recommendation of prayer after Sa'y based on the literal interpretation of the hadith.

Key Terms
تحية المسجد (tahiyyat al-masjid): A prayer of two rak'ahs performed upon entering a mosque to greet it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, which interpretation of the Prophet's prayer after Sa'y is more apparent (al-mutabādir)?
A) It was a greeting of the mosque (tahiyyat al-masjid).
B) It was specifically for Sa'y.
C) It was a missed obligatory prayer.
D) It was a voluntary prayer unrelated to the time.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends prayer after Sa'y based on the apparent meaning of the hadith, though the alternative interpretation as tahiyyat al-masjid is acknowledged and respected.

The Sa'y Course: Dimensions and Validity
Factual statement about the length and width of the Sa'y course with a discussion on its validity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the reported length and width of the Sa'y course and explain the Hanafi position on its continued validity.

Core Idea
The Sa'y course dimensions are historically transmitted; its current area is valid because changes did not completely eliminate the original space.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the dimensions of the Sa'y course between Safa and Marwah. Two different lengths are reported, and the width is given. The author then raises a critical issue: the current Sa'y area may not exactly match the original due to later constructions. How can Sa'y be valid if the place has changed? The Hanafi response is grounded in historical continuity and the lack of scholarly objection.

Guided Path
1
Identify the reported dimensions
Note the two lengths: 750 cubits (al-Marshidi) and 766 cubits (al-Shumunni). The width is 35 cubits. These are from historical sources.
The length is the distance one way; total Sa'y (7 trips) is 5250 cubits (750 x 7).
2
Recognize the problem
Understand that over time, parts of the original Sa'y area were incorporated into the Sacred Mosque or built upon, raising doubt about the current area's correspondence to the original.
The concern is that Sa'y is an act of devotion tied to a specific place.
3
Understand the Hanafi solution
The answer is that the original area was wide, and the changes were partial. The scholar al-Madani notes that the houses built within the width were partially demolished and the area was not completely relocated. The lack of objection from earlier scholars supports continuity.
This is based on the principle that established practices remain valid unless proven otherwise.
4
Apply the ruling
Conclude that Sa'y performed in the current course is valid according to the Hanafi school, as the essential area remains.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مهمة : ذكر الشيخ عبد الرحمن المرشدي في شرحه على الكنز أن مسافة ما سبعمائة وخمسون ذرعاً، فعليه فعدة السعي خمسة آلاف ومائتان وخمسون ذراعاً ا وفي الشمني : سبعمائة وستة وستون ذراعاً وأما عرض المسعى فحكى العلامة الشيخ قطب الدين الحنفي في تاريخه نقلاً عن تاريخ الفاكهي أنه خمسة وثلاثون ذراعاً ثم قال : وههنا إشكال عظيم ما رأيت أحداً تعرض وهو السعي بين الصفا والمروة من الأمور التعبدية في ذلك المكان المخصوص، وعلى ما ذكر الثقات أدخل ذلك المسعى في الحرم الشريف وحول ذلك المسعى إلى دار ابن عباد كما تقدم. والمكان الذي يسعى فيه الآن لا يتحقق أنه من عرض المسعى الذي سعى فيه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره، فكيف يصح السعي فيه وقد حول عن محله؟ ولعل الجواب أن المسعى كان عريضاً وبنيت تلك الدور بعد في عرض المسعى القديم فهدمها المهدي وأدخل بعضها في المسجد الحرام وترك البعض ولم يحول تحويلاً كلياً وإلا لأنكره علماء الدين من الأئمة المجتهدين ا.هـ. ملخصاً من المدني
Important note: Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Marshidi mentioned in his commentary on al-Kanz that the distance is seven hundred and fifty cubits, so accordingly the total of Sa'y is five thousand two hundred and fifty cubits. And in al-Shumunni: seven hundred and sixty-six cubits. As for the width of the Sa'y area, the scholar Shaykh Qutb al-Din al-Hanafi narrated in his history, quoting from the history of al-Fakihi, that it is thirty-five cubits. Then he said: And here is a great problem that I have not seen anyone address: And it is that Sa'y between Safa and Marwah is among the devotional acts in that specific place, and according to what trustworthy people mentioned, that Sa'y area was included in the noble sanctuary and that Sa'y area was transferred to the house of Ibn Abbad as previously mentioned. And the place where Sa'y is performed now cannot be verified to be from the width of the Sa'y area in which the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed Sa'y or others, so how can Sa'y be valid in it when it has been moved from its place? Perhaps the answer is that the Sa'y area was wide, and those houses were built later within the width of the old Sa'y area, so al-Mahdi demolished them and included some of them in the Sacred Mosque and left some, and it was not completely moved, otherwise the religious scholars from the mujtahid imams would have objected. End. Summarized from al-Madani.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage provides the dimensions of the Sa'y course between Safa and Marwah. Two different lengths are given: 750 cubits (al-Marshidi) and 766 cubits (al-Shumunni). The width is reported as 35 cubits from historical sources. The author then raises an important issue: the current Sa'y area may not be exactly the same as the original course used by the Prophet ﷺ due to later constructions and expansions. Some of the original area was incorporated into the mosque, and buildings were erected within it. The answer provided is that the original area was sufficiently wide, and the changes did not completely remove the Sa'y area, otherwise the scholars would have raised objections. Therefore, the validity of Sa'y in the current location is upheld based on the continuity of the practice and the lack of objection from earlier imams.

Key Terms
ذراع (dhira'): A cubit, a unit of length approximately the length of the forearm.
مسعى (mas'a): The designated area between Safa and Marwah where the Sa'y is performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the width of the Sa'y course according to historical sources cited in the passage?
A) 35 cubits
B) 750 cubits
C) 766 cubits
D) 5250 cubits

Key Takeaway
The Sa'y course dimensions are historically transmitted, and the current area is considered valid for sa'y due to the width and continuity of the practice.

The Prohibition of Dissolving Hajj into Umrah
Ruling with proof on dissolution and additional mutamatti' case

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dissolving Hajj into Umrah and explain the evidence that supports it, including the treatment of the prophetic hadiths that appear to permit it.

Core Idea
Once you enter ihram for Hajj, you cannot change your mind — dissolving Hajj into Umrah is forbidden.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author explains a fundamental ruling for the pilgrim: after entering ihram for Hajj, it is not permissible to dissolve the intention and convert it to Umrah. He addresses the apparent conflict with hadiths that show the Prophet ﷺ ordered some companions to do exactly that, and resolves it by showing those instructions were specific or abrogated. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence, and a related issue concerning the mutamatti'.

Guided Path
1
Extract the explicit ruling
Identify the clear statement: 'Then reside in Makkah in ihram because you are in ihram for Hajj, so it is not permissible for him to exit ihram until he performs its actions. So it indicates that dissolving Hajj into Umrah is not permissible.'
2
Identify the contradictory evidence
The two Sahihs contain hadiths where the Prophet ordered his companions (except those with sacrificial animals) to dissolve their Hajj into Umrah. This appears to conflict with the ruling.
These hadiths are the basis for the Shafi'i position.
3
Analyze the Hanafi resolution
The author provides two interpretations: either the order was specific to the Companions (as per Sahih Muslim from Abu Dharr) or it was later abrogated, similar to the abrogation of temporary marriage. Therefore, the general prohibition remains.
The hadith from Abu Dharr explicitly states 'Tamattu' was specific to the companions of Muhammad.'
4
Note the supporting evidence
Another hadith from the two Sahihs states: 'Those who entered ihram for Hajj or Hajj and Umrah did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr.' This supports the general prohibition.
This is considered the stronger evidence by the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the ruling to the mutamatti' case
The passage adds that a mutamatti' (one who performed Umrah before Hajj) should not perform another Umrah while residing in Makkah. If he does, he commits a wrong and must offer a dam (sacrifice). This is a related prohibition derived from the same principle.
The commentator suggests that if it is not during the disliked times, it may be permissible, but the preferred view is prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم أقم بمكة حراماً لأنك محرم بالحج فلا يجوز له التحلل حتى يأتي بأفعاله فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز، وما في الصحيحين من أنه عليه السلام أمر بذلك أصحابه إلا من ساق منهم الهدي فهو مخصوص بهم لما في صحيح مسلم عن أبي ذر أن المتعة كانت لأصحاب محمد خاصة، وفي بعض الشروح أنها كانت مشروعة على العموم ثم نسخت كمتعة النكاح، أو معارض بما في الصحيحين أيضاً أن من أهل بالحج أو بالحج والعمرة لم يحلوا إلى يوم النحر قوله : فطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك أي ظهر لك لحديث الطحاوي وغيره «الطواف بالبيت صلاة إلا أن الله قد أحل لكم المنطق (۱) والصلاة خير موضوع فكذا الطواف إلا أنه لا يسعى لكونه لا يتكرر لا وجوباً ولا نفلاً، وكذا الرمل. ويجب أن يصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين كما قدمناه فالطواف التطوع أفضل للغرباء من صلاة التطوع، ولأهل مكة الصلاة أفضل منه هكذا أطلقه كثير وينبغي تقييده بزمن الموسم وإلا فالطواف أفضل الصلاة مكياً كان أو غريباً، وينبغي أن يكون قريباً من البيت في طوافه إذا لم يؤذ به من له ذلك أفعاله ويجعل وهو السعي بين الصفا والمروة من الأمور التعبدية في ذلك المكان المخصوص، وعلى ما ذكر الثقات أدخل ذلك المسعى في الحرم الشريف وحول ذلك المسعى إلى دار ابن عباد كما تقدم. والمكان الذي يسعى فيه الآن لا يتحقق أنه من عرض المسعى الذي سعى فيه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره، فكيف يصح السعي فيه وقد حول عن محله؟ ولعل الجواب أن المسعى كان عريضاً وبنيت تلك الدور بعد في عرض المسعى القديم فهدمها المهدي وأدخل بعضها في المسجد الحرام وترك البعض ولم يحول تحويلاً كلياً وإلا لأنكره علماء الدين من الأئمة المجتهدين ا.هـ. ملخصاً من المدني قوله : (فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز أي بأن يفسخ نية الحج بعد ما أحرم به ويقطع إحرامه وأفعاله للعمرة، وكذا لا يجوز فسخ العمرة ليجعلها حجاً. كذا في اللباب قبيل الجنايات، وفيه : لا يعتمر أي المتمتع حال إقامته بمكة فإن فعل أساء ولزمه دم سواء كان في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، وإن كان لم يسق الهدي وأحل بعد الحلق يفعل كما يفعل الحلال . قال شارحه : والظاهر أنه يجوز له الإتيان بالعمرة حينئذ لأنه غير ممنوع منها لكراهتها في الأزمنة المخصوصة، وإنما كرهت العمرة للمكي في أشهر الحج لأن الغالب أنه يجح فيبقى متمتعاً مسيئاً قوله : (وإلا فالطواف أفضل من الصلاة الخ) مخالف لما في الفتاوى الولوالجية ونصه الصلاة بمكة أفضل لأهلها من الطواف، وللغرباء الطواف أفضل لأن الصلاة في نفسها أفضل من الطواف لأن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه (۱) رواه النسائي في كتاب المناسك باب ١٣٦. الدارمي في كتاب المناسك باب ٣٢. أحمد في مسنده (٤١٤/٣( )٦٤/٤)
His statement: (Then reside in Makkah in ihram because you are in ihram for Hajj, so it is not permissible for him to exit ihram until he performs its actions. So it indicates that dissolving Hajj into Umrah is not permissible. And what is in the two Sahihs that he ﷺ ordered his companions to do that except those who had brought a sacrificial animal is specific to them, because in Sahih Muslim from Abu Dharr that Tamattu' was specific to the companions of Muhammad. And in some commentaries it was legislated generally then abrogated like the Tamattu' of marriage. Or it is countered by what is also in the two Sahihs that those who entered ihram for Hajj or Hajj and Umrah did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr. His statement: So perform Tawaf around the House whenever it becomes apparent to you, i.e., whenever it appears to you, due to the hadith of al-Tahawi and others: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer except that Allah has permitted speech for you.' And prayer is the best act, so Tawaf is the same, except that it is not done as Sa'y because it is not repeated, neither obligatory nor supererogatory. And similarly Ramal. And it is obligatory to pray two rak'ahs for every seven circuits as we have presented. So voluntary Tawaf is better for strangers than voluntary prayer, and for the people of Makkah, prayer is better than it. This is how many have stated it absolutely, but it should be restricted to the time of the season; otherwise, Tawaf is better than prayer whether one is Makkan or stranger. And he should be close to the House in his Tawaf if he does not cause harm to others. His statements and actions: and it (the Sa'y) is between Safa and Marwah, one of the devotional acts in that specific place. And according to trustworthy people, that Sa'y area was included in the noble sanctuary and that Sa'y area was transferred to the house of Ibn Abbad as previously mentioned. And the place where Sa'y is performed now cannot be verified to be from the width of the Sa'y area in which the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed Sa'y or others, so how can Sa'y be valid in it when it has been moved from its place? Perhaps the answer is that the Sa'y area was wide, and those houses were built later within the width of the old Sa'y area, so al-Mahdi demolished them and included some of them in the Sacred Mosque and left some, and it was not completely moved, otherwise the religious scholars from the mujtahid imams would have objected. End. Summarized from al-Madani. His statement: (So it indicates that dissolving Hajj into Umrah is not permissible) means that one does not dissolve the intention of Hajj after entering ihram and cut off his ihram and actions for Umrah. Similarly, it is not permissible to dissolve Umrah to make it Hajj. Thus in al-Lubab before the chapters on injuries. And in it: The mutamatti' should not perform Umrah while residing in Makkah; if he does, he does wrong and owes a dam, whether it is in the months of Hajj or before them. And if he has not brought a sacrificial animal and has exited ihram after shaving, he does as the non-muhrim does. Its commentator said: And it is apparent that it is permissible for him to perform Umrah at that time because he is not prevented from it due to its dislike at specific times. Umrah is only disliked for a Makkan during the months of Hajj because the majority of the time he performs Hajj and thus becomes a mutamatti' doing wrong. His statement: (And if not, Tawaf is better than prayer, etc.) contradicts what is in al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyyah, the text of which is: Prayer in Makkah is better for its people than Tawaf, and for strangers, Tawaf is better because prayer is inherently better than Tawaf, because the Prophet ﷺ... (1) Narrated by al-Nasa'i in Kitab al-Manasik, bab 136. al-Darimi in Kitab al-Manasik, bab 32. Ahmad in his Musnad (3/414, 4/64).
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the actions after completing Sa'y. The first ruling is that the pilgrim must remain in ihram after Sa'y and cannot dissolve Hajj into Umrah. This is supported by hadiths from the two Sahihs indicating that the Prophet's companions who performed Hajj did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr. There is a discussion that the permission for tamattu' (combining Umrah with Hajj with a break) was specific to the companions or later abrogated. The second part discusses the virtue of Tawaf: the pilgrim is encouraged to perform Tawaf frequently based on the hadith that Tawaf is like prayer. However, Tawaf is not repeated in the same manner as prayer (i.e., Sa'y is not repeated). It is recommended to pray two rak'ahs after each seven circuits. There is a difference of opinion on whether Tawaf or prayer is better in Makkah: many say that voluntary Tawaf is better for strangers (non-Makkans) while prayer is better for Makkans, but some restrict this to the season of Hajj, while others hold that Tawaf is always better. The passage then repeats the note about the Sa'y area's dimensions and validity, which was covered in Lesson 3. Finally, it returns to the issue of dissolving Hajj, adding that a mutamatti' should not perform another Umrah while in Makkah; if he does, he must offer a dam (sacrifice). The commentator notes that some allow it if it is not in the disliked times.

Key Terms
فسخ الحج (faskh al-hajj): Dissolving the intention of Hajj and converting it to Umrah after entering ihram.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs Umrah during the Hajj months and then performs Hajj in the same year with a break.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on dissolving Hajj into Umrah?
A) It is recommended.
B) It is permissible as long as one has not started Tawaf.
C) It is not permissible.
D) It is permissible only for the people of Makkah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school strictly prohibits dissolving Hajj into Umrah, and the apparent permission in the hadith is understood to be specific or abrogated.

The Virtue of Tawaf vs Prayer in Makkah
Ruling with proof on the virtue of Tawaf vs prayer and intra-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi preference between voluntary Tawaf and voluntary prayer in Makkah and identify the intra-madhhab difference regarding Makkans.

Core Idea
For strangers in Makkah, voluntary Tawaf is better than voluntary prayer; for Makkans, prayer is better, but some restrict this to the Hajj season.

The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the relative virtue of Tawaf and prayer in Makkah, citing the hadith that Tawaf is like prayer. He states the common view that voluntary Tawaf is better for non-Makkans while prayer is better for the people of Makkah, but then notes a disagreement with al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyyah and suggests restricting the Tawaf preference to the Hajj season. This lesson unpacks that dispute and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith basis
The passage cites the hadith: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer except that Allah has permitted speech.' This establishes the high status of Tawaf.
The hadith is recorded by al-Tahawi and others; it is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalala.
2
State the general Hanafi preference
Based on this hadith and other considerations, the Hanafi school holds that voluntary Tawaf is better than voluntary prayer for strangers (non-Makkans).
The author says: 'So voluntary Tawaf is better for strangers than voluntary prayer.'
3
Identify the qualification for Makkans
Many scholars state that for the people of Makkah, voluntary prayer is better than voluntary Tawaf. The author reports this as a common view.
This is based on the principle that prayer is inherently the best act of worship, and Makkans have easy access to both.
4
Note the internal Hanafi dispute
Al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyyah holds that prayer is better for Makkans absolutely. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq disagrees and argues that this should be restricted to the Hajj season; outside the season, Tawaf is better even for Makkans.
The author states: 'It should be restricted to the time of the season; otherwise, Tawaf is better than prayer whether one is Makkan or stranger.'
5
Derive the mufta bihi
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) combines both views: For non-Makkans, Tawaf is better at all times. For Makkans, prayer is better during the Hajj season; outside the season, the stronger evidence suggests Tawaf is better, though some scholars still prefer prayer.
The dispute is legitimate within the Hanafi school; the fatwa may vary based on the mufti's tarjih.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم أقم بمكة حراماً لأنك محرم بالحج فلا يجوز له التحلل حتى يأتي بأفعاله فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز، وما في الصحيحين من أنه عليه السلام أمر بذلك أصحابه إلا من ساق منهم الهدي فهو مخصوص بهم لما في صحيح مسلم عن أبي ذر أن المتعة كانت لأصحاب محمد خاصة، وفي بعض الشروح أنها كانت مشروعة على العموم ثم نسخت كمتعة النكاح، أو معارض بما في الصحيحين أيضاً أن من أهل بالحج أو بالحج والعمرة لم يحلوا إلى يوم النحر قوله : فطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك أي ظهر لك لحديث الطحاوي وغيره «الطواف بالبيت صلاة إلا أن الله قد أحل لكم المنطق (۱) والصلاة خير موضوع فكذا الطواف إلا أنه لا يسعى لكونه لا يتكرر لا الصلاة مكياً كان أو غريباً، وينبغي أن يكون قريباً من البيت في طوافه إذا لم يؤذ به من له ذلك أفعاله ويجعل وهو السعي بين الصفا والمروة من الأمور التعبدية في ذلك المكان المخصوص، وعلى ما ذكر الثقات أدخل ذلك المسعى في الحرم الشريف وحول ذلك المسعى إلى دار ابن عباد كما تقدم. والمكان الذي يسعى فيه الآن لا يتحقق أنه من عرض المسعى الذي سعى فيه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أو غيره، فكيف يصح السعي فيه وقد حول عن محله؟ ولعل الجواب أن المسعى كان عريضاً وبنيت تلك الدور بعد في عرض المسعى القديم فهدمها المهدي وأدخل بعضها في المسجد الحرام وترك البعض ولم يحول تحويلاً كلياً وإلا لأنكره علماء الدين من الأئمة المجتهدين ا.هـ. ملخصاً من المدني قوله : (فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز أي بأن يفسخ نية الحج بعد ما أحرم به ويقطع إحرامه وأفعاله للعمرة، وكذا لا يجوز فسخ العمرة ليجعلها حجاً. كذا في اللباب قبيل الجنايات، وفيه : لا يعتمر أي المتمتع حال إقامته بمكة فإن فعل أساء ولزمه دم سواء كان في أشهر الحج أو قبلها، وإن كان لم يسق الهدي وأحل بعد الحلق يفعل كما يفعل الحلال . قال شارحه : والظاهر أنه يجوز له الإتيان بالعمرة حينئذ لأنه غير ممنوع منها لكراهتها في الأزمنة المخصوصة، وإنما كرهت العمرة للمكي في أشهر الحج لأن الغالب أنه يجح فيبقى متمتعاً مسيئاً قوله : (وإلا فالطواف أفضل من الصلاة الخ) مخالف لما في الفتاوى الولوالجية ونصه الصلاة بمكة أفضل لأهلها من الطواف، وللغرباء الطواف أفضل لأن الصلاة في نفسها أفضل من الطواف لأن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه (۱) رواه النسائي في كتاب المناسك باب ١٣٦. الدارمي في كتاب المناسك باب ٣٢. أحمد في مسنده (٤١٤/٣( )٦٤/٤)
His statement: (Then reside in Makkah in ihram because you are in ihram for Hajj, so it is not permissible for him to exit ihram until he performs its actions. So it indicates that dissolving Hajj into Umrah is not permissible. And what is in the two Sahihs that he ﷺ ordered his companions to do that except those who had brought a sacrificial animal is specific to them, because in Sahih Muslim from Abu Dharr that Tamattu' was specific to the companions of Muhammad. And in some commentaries it was legislated generally then abrogated like the Tamattu' of marriage. Or it is countered by what is also in the two Sahihs that those who entered ihram for Hajj or Hajj and Umrah did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr. His statement: So perform Tawaf around the House whenever it becomes apparent to you, i.e., whenever it appears to you, due to the hadith of al-Tahawi and others: 'Tawaf around the House is prayer except that Allah has permitted speech for you.' And prayer is the best act, so Tawaf is the same, except that it is not done as Sa'y because it is not repeated, neither obligatory nor supererogatory. And similarly Ramal. And it is obligatory to pray two rak'ahs for every seven circuits as we have presented. So voluntary Tawaf is better for strangers than voluntary prayer, and for the people of Makkah, prayer is better than it. This is how many have stated it absolutely, but it should be restricted to the time of the season; otherwise, Tawaf is better than prayer whether one is Makkan or stranger. And he should be close to the House in his Tawaf if he does not cause harm to others. His statements and actions: and it (the Sa'y) is between Safa and Marwah, one of the devotional acts in that specific place. And according to trustworthy people, that Sa'y area was included in the noble sanctuary and that Sa'y area was transferred to the house of Ibn Abbad as previously mentioned. And the place where Sa'y is performed now cannot be verified to be from the width of the Sa'y area in which the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed Sa'y or others, so how can Sa'y be valid in it when it has been moved from its place? Perhaps the answer is that the Sa'y area was wide, and those houses were built later within the width of the old Sa'y area, so al-Mahdi demolished them and included some of them in the Sacred Mosque and left some, and it was not completely moved, otherwise the religious scholars from the mujtahid imams would have objected. End. Summarized from al-Madani. His statement: (So it indicates that dissolving Hajj into Umrah is not permissible) means that one does not dissolve the intention of Hajj after entering ihram and cut off his ihram and actions for Umrah. Similarly, it is not permissible to dissolve Umrah to make it Hajj. Thus in al-Lubab before the chapters on injuries. And in it: The mutamatti' should not perform Umrah while residing in Makkah; if he does, he does wrong and owes a dam, whether it is in the months of Hajj or before them. And if he has not brought a sacrificial animal and has exited ihram after shaving, he does as the non-muhrim does. Its commentator said: And it is apparent that it is permissible for him to perform Umrah at that time because he is not prevented from it due to its dislike at specific times. Umrah is only disliked for a Makkan during the months of Hajj because the majority of the time he performs Hajj and thus becomes a mutamatti' doing wrong. His statement: (And if not, Tawaf is better than prayer, etc.) contradicts what is in al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyyah, the text of which is: Prayer in Makkah is better for its people than Tawaf, and for strangers, Tawaf is better because prayer is inherently better than Tawaf, because the Prophet ﷺ... (1) Narrated by al-Nasa'i in Kitab al-Manasik, bab 136. al-Darimi in Kitab al-Manasik, bab 32. Ahmad in his Musnad (3/414, 4/64).
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the actions after completing Sa'y. The first ruling is that the pilgrim must remain in ihram after Sa'y and cannot dissolve Hajj into Umrah. This is supported by hadiths from the two Sahihs indicating that the Prophet's companions who performed Hajj did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr. There is a discussion that the permission for tamattu' (combining Umrah with Hajj with a break) was specific to the companions or later abrogated. The second part discusses the virtue of Tawaf: the pilgrim is encouraged to perform Tawaf frequently based on the hadith that Tawaf is like prayer. However, Tawaf is not repeated in the same manner as prayer (i.e., Sa'y is not repeated). It is recommended to pray two rak'ahs after each seven circuits. There is a difference of opinion on whether Tawaf or prayer is better in Makkah: many say that voluntary Tawaf is better for strangers (non-Makkans) while prayer is better for Makkans, but some restrict this to the season of Hajj, while others hold that Tawaf is always better. The passage then repeats the note about the Sa'y area's dimensions and validity, which was covered in Lesson 3. Finally, it returns to the issue of dissolving Hajj, adding that a mutamatti' should not perform another Umrah while in Makkah; if he does, he must offer a dam (sacrifice). The commentator notes that some allow it if it is not in the disliked times.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circling the Kaaba seven times, a devotional act.
غرباء (ghuraba'): Strangers; non-Makkan pilgrims or visitors.
أهل مكة (ahl Makkah): The residents of Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, for a non-Makkan pilgrim, which is better: voluntary Tawaf or voluntary prayer?
A) Both are equal.
B) Prayer is better.
C) Tawaf is better.
D) It depends on the season.

Key Takeaway
The superiority of voluntary Tawaf over voluntary prayer in Makkah depends on the person's status and, for Makkans, the season, according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Prohibition of Faskh of Hajj to Umrah
explaining the prohibition of faskh and the specificity of the Prophet's command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on faskh of Hajj to Umrah and explain the dalil from the Sahihain that supports it.

Core Idea
The Prophet's command to change Hajj to Umrah was specific to his companions — it is not a general ruling.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains why a person who has entered ihram for Hajj cannot simply change their intention to Umrah. The matn states that one must remain in ihram until completing the Hajj actions. The commentator then addresses a potential objection from the hadith in Bukhari and Muslim where the Prophet ordered his companions to do faskh. He clarifies that this was a special concession, not a general ruling, and supports this with evidence from Sahih Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn says one must remain in ihram until completing Hajj actions, implying faskh is not allowed.
2
Locate the dalil cited
The commentator cites the hadith from Sahihain that the Prophet ordered his companions to do faskh except those who brought hadi.
3
Determine how the dalil is interpreted
The Hanafi response: the exception of those with hadi shows the command was not general. Also, another hadith shows those who entered for Hajj did not exit until the Day of Nahr.
4
Identify the opposing view
Some commentators claimed the permission was general and later abrogated.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon because the hadith itself restricts the permission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثم أقم بمكة حراماً لأنك محرم بالحج فلا يجوز له التحلل حتى يأتي بأفعاله فأفاد أن فسخ الحج إلى العمرة لا يجوز، وما في الصحيحين من أنه عليه السلام أمر بذلك أصحابه إلا من ساق منهم الهدي فهو مخصوص بهم لما في صحيح مسلم عن أبي ذر أن المتعة كانت لأصحاب محمد خاصة، وفي بعض الشروح أنها كانت مشروعة على العموم ثم نسخت كمتعة النكاح، أو معارض بما في الصحيحين أيضاً أن من أهل بالحج أو بالحج والعمرة لم يحلوا إلى يوم النحر
He said: (Then stay in Makkah in ihram because you are in ihram for Hajj, so it is not permissible for him to exit ihram until he performs its actions. So this indicates that faskh of Hajj to Umrah is not allowed. And what is in the two Sahihs that he عليه السلام ordered his companions to do so except those who brought the Hadi, so it is specific to them because in Sahih Muslim from Abu Dharr that Tamattu' was especially for the companions of Muhammad. And in some commentaries it was generally legislated then abrogated like the mut'ah of marriage, or it is opposed by what is in the two Sahihs also that whoever entered into ihram for Hajj or for Hajj and Umrah did not exit ihram until the Day of Nahr.)
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage from the sharh discusses the ruling that a person who has entered ihram for Hajj cannot change his intention to Umrah (faskh). The matn states that one must remain in ihram until completing the actions of Hajj. The commentator notes that the Prophet's command to his companions to change their ihram to Umrah was a special concession for them, as narrated in Muslim. Some commentators said the concession was general and later abrogated, but this is countered by the hadith that those who entered ihram for Hajj did not exit until the day of Nahr. The Hanafi position is that faskh is not permitted for anyone.

Key Terms
فسخ (faskh): Changing the intention of ihram from Hajj to Umrah or vice versa.
تحلل (tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram after completing the rituals.
هدي (hadi): Sacrificial animal brought by pilgrims during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the Prophet's command to his companions to change from Hajj to Umrah not a general ruling?
A) Because it was abrogated by later Quranic verses.
B) Because it was only for the companions and not for others.
C) Because it was only for those who did not bring a Hadi.
D) Because it was only for the year of the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Key Takeaway
Faskh of Hajj to Umrah is prohibited in the Hanafi school because the Prophet's permission was a special concession for his companions, not a general ruling.

Virtue of Tawaf and Comparison with Prayer
Explaining the virtue of tawaf via hadith and its comparison with prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the hadith proof for tawaf's virtue and apply the Hanafi ruling on whether tawaf or prayer is better for different individuals.

Core Idea
Tawaf is like prayer in reward, but its preference depends on need and opportunity.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the exceptional merit of tawaf, citing a hadith that likens it to prayer. The Hanafi school then navigates a nuanced comparison: while tawaf and prayer are both highly virtuous, the better act depends on whether one is a visitor to Makkah or a resident, and the timing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith proof and its meaning
The hadith 'Tawaf of the House is prayer except that Allah has allowed you to speak' establishes tawaf's high status. Understand that this equates tawaf to prayer in reward but permits speech, indicating a unique virtue.
2
Understand the general ruling that tawaf is like prayer
Both are acts of worship; tawaf shares the reward of prayer. The commentator notes that prayer is the best act, so tawaf is similarly excellent, but with the allowance for speech.
3
Analyze the distinction between strangers and Makkans
For a visitor (gharib), supererogatory tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer because the visitor may not have another opportunity. For a Makkan, prayer is better during the season, otherwise tawaf is better.
The distinction is based on the availability of tawaf elsewhere.
4
Apply the seasonal restriction
The general statement that prayer is better for Makkans is restricted to the Hajj season. Outside the season, tawaf is better for everyone.
5
Note additional rulings
Tawaf does not require sa'i (it is not repeated). Ramal is a sunnah during tawaf. It is obligatory to pray two rak'ahs after each seven circuits. One should stay close to the Kaaba if it does not harm others.
These details complete the practical guidance for performing tawaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : فطف بالبيت كلما بدا لك أي ظهر لك لحديث الطحاوي وغيره «الطواف بالبيت صلاة إلا أن الله قد أحل لكم المنطق» والصلاة خير موضوع فكذا الطواف إلا أنه لا يسعى لكونه لا يتكرر لا وجوباً ولا نفلاً، وكذا الرمل. ويجب أن يصلي لكل أسبوع ركعتين كما قدمناه فالطواف التطوع أفضل للغرباء من صلاة التطوع، ولأهل مكة الصلاة أفضل منه هكذا أطلقه كثير وينبغي تقييده بزمن الموسم وإلا فالطواف أفضل الصلاة مكياً كان أو غريباً، وينبغي أن يكون قريباً من البيت في طوافه إذا لم يؤذ به
He said: So perform tawaf of the House whenever it appears to you, according to the hadith of al-Tahawi and others: 'Tawaf of the House is prayer except that Allah has allowed you to speak.' And prayer is the best of acts, so tawaf is similar, but there is no sa'i because it is not repeated, neither obligatory nor supererogatory. Similarly, ramal. And it is obligatory to pray two rak'ahs for every seven circuits as we have mentioned. So supererogatory tawaf is better for strangers than supererogatory prayer, and for the people of Makkah, prayer is better than it. This is the general opinion, but it should be restricted to the season; otherwise, tawaf is better than prayer whether one is from Makkah or a stranger. And he should be close to the House in his tawaf if he does not cause harm to anyone.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage discusses the virtue of tawaf, citing the hadith that tawaf is like prayer but with allowance for speech. The commentator notes that tawaf does not require sa'i (because sa'i is separate and not repeated). Ramal (fast walking) is also mentioned as part of tawaf. It is obligatory to pray two rak'ahs after each seven circuits. Then a comparison is made: supererogatory tawaf is better than supererogatory prayer for visitors (ghuraba), while for the people of Makkah, prayer is better during the season; otherwise, tawaf is preferable for everyone. The commentator also emphasizes staying close to the Kaaba during tawaf as long as one does not inconvenience others.

Key Terms
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulating the Kaaba seven times, starting from the Black Stone.
رمل (ramal): Walking briskly with short steps during the first three circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For a visitor (gharib) performing tawaf in Makkah, which is better: supererogatory tawaf or supererogatory prayer?
A) Prayer is always better.
B) Tawaf is better because the visitor may not return.
C) They are equal.
D) It depends on the time of day.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that while tawaf is like prayer in virtue, its superiority is situational: visitors should prioritize tawaf, while residents should prioritize prayer during the season.
